Catching the Imam in Ruku' Does Not Catch the Rak'ah
Explains the ruling and intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on catching the rak'ah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on catching the rak'ah by catching the imam in ruku' and explain the ikhtilaf with Zufar, including the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Catching the imam in ruku' does not count as catching the rak'ah unless you also catch part of the qiyam.

The passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq explains that if a latecomer finds the imam in ruku' and says takbir but does not participate in the standing before ruku', he does not catch that rak'ah. This ruling distinguishes the Hanafi majority view from that of Zufar, who held that the imam's posture carries the ruling of standing. The practical consequence is whether the latecomer performs the missed rak'ah before or after the imam finishes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
The matn states that if a latecomer catches the imam in ruku' and stands until the imam raises his head, he has not caught the rak'ah. This is the Hanafi position.
2
Locate the Dalil
The Hanafi proof is that the condition for catching the rak'ah is participation in the actual actions of prayer. The latecomer participated in neither the standing nor the ruku'.
The dalil is a qiyas jaliy based on the illa of participation.
3
Note the Ikhtilaf
Zufar argues that since the imam has the ruling of standing (hukm al-qiyam) before ruku', catching him in ruku' should count as catching the rak'ah.
Zufar is a Hanafi scholar with a minority view.
4
Evaluate the Thamarah al-Khilaf
According to Zufar, the latecomer is a lahiq and must perform the rak'ah before the imam finishes. According to the majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad), he is a masbuq and performs it after the imam finishes.
This practical difference is the key consequence.
5
Confirm the Unanimous Exceptions
All agree that if the latecomer reaches the imam while standing and then bows after the imam, he catches the rak'ah. Also, if he follows the imam in the rising from ruku', he does not catch it.
Al-Mustasfi adds that the ruling applies only if the latecomer is able to bow; if unable, even Zufar agrees it is not caught.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( وإن أدرك إمامه راكعاً فكبر ووقف حتى رفع رأسه لم يدرك الركعة) خلافاً لزفر . هو يقول أدرك الإمام فيما له حكم القيام، ولنا أن الشرط هو المشاركة في أفعال الصلاة ولم يوجد لا في القيام ولا في الركوع . وذكر قاضيخان أن ثمرة الخلاف تظهر في أن هذا عنده لاحق في هذه الركعة حتى يأتي بها قبل فراغ الإمام، وعندنا هو مسبوق بها حتى يأتي بها بعد فراغ الإمام، وأجمعوا أنه لو انتهى إلى الإمام وهو قائم فكبر ولم يركع مع الإمام حتى ركع الإمام ثم ركع أنه يصير مدركاً لتلك الركعة وأجمعوا أنه لو اقتدى به في قومة الركوع لم يصر مدركاً لتلك الركعة ا هـ . وفي المصفي : وهذا إذا أمكنه الركوع، أما إذا لم يمكنه لا يعتد به عند زفر أيضاً.
His statement: (And if he catches his imam in ruku' and he says takbir and stands until he raises his head, he has not caught the rak'ah) contrary to Zufar. He (Zufar) says: he has caught the imam in what has the ruling of standing. And for us (Hanafis): the condition is participation in the actions of prayer, and it has not occurred in standing nor in ruku'. And Qadikhan mentioned that the practical outcome of the difference appears in that according to him (Zufar) he is a 'lahiq' in this rak'ah such that he performs it before the imam finishes, and according to us he is 'masbuq' in it such that he performs it after the imam finishes. And they unanimously agreed that if he reached the imam while standing and said takbir and did not bow with the imam until the imam bowed and then he bowed, that he becomes a catcher of that rak'ah. And they unanimously agreed that if he followed him in the rising from ruku', he does not become a catcher of that rak'ah. End quote. And in al-Mustasfi: This is when he is able to bow; as for if he is not able, it is not considered according to Zufar as well.
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and an inter-madhhab dispute regarding whether catching the imam in ruku' constitutes catching the rak'ah. The matn states that if a latecomer finds the imam in ruku' and says takbir and stands until the imam raises his head, he has not caught the rak'ah. This is the Hanafi position, contrary to Zufar, who argues that since the imam has the ruling of standing (due to being in the standing posture before ruku'), catching him in ruku' should count as catching the rak'ah. The Hanafi response is that the condition for catching a rak'ah is participation with the imam in the actions of prayer, and the latecomer participated neither in the standing nor in the ruku'. Qadikhan clarifies the practical outcome: according to Zufar, the latecomer is a 'lahiq' (one who joins later but still catches the rak'ah) and should perform it before the imam finishes, while according to the Hanafis he is 'masbuq' (one who misses the rak'ah) and must complete it after the imam. Two unanimous rulings are cited: (1) if the latecomer reaches the imam while standing and then bows after the imam bows, he does catch the rak'ah; (2) if he follows the imam in the rising from ruku' (qawmat al-rukū'), he does not catch it. Al-Mustasfi adds a condition: this ruling applies only if the latecomer is able to bow; if he is unable, even Zufar would not consider it a valid catch.

Key Terms
مدرك (mudrik): One who catches the imam in an action, thereby achieving the rak'ah.
لاحق (lahiq): Zufar's term for a latecomer who catches the imam in ruku' and thus is considered to have caught the rak'ah and must complete it before imam finishes.
مسبوق (masbuq): A latecomer who misses at least one rak'ah and must complete it after the imam.
قومة الركوع (qawmat al-rukū'): The act of rising from ruku' to standing position.
ثمرة الخلاف (thamarat al-khilaf): The practical consequence of a legal disagreement between scholars.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a latecomer (masbuq) finds the imam in ruku' (bowing) and says the opening takbir and stands until the imam raises his head, does he catch that rak'ah?
A) Yes, he catches the rak'ah because he participated in the ruku'.
B) No, he does not catch the rak'ah because he missed the standing before ruku'.
C) Yes, according to Zufar, but the majority say no.
D) No, because he did not participate in the ruku' either.

Key Takeaway
The latecomer who catches the imam in ruku' without having participated in qiyam does not catch that rak'ah; he is a masbuq and must complete it after the imam.

Following the Imam in Sujud for the Latecomer: Wajib or Sunnah?
Intra-Hanafi dispute with critical refinement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a latecomer following the imam in sujud and explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement on whether it is wajib or sunnah.

Core Idea
Following the imam in sujud for the missed rak'ah is sunnah, not wajib — omitting it does not invalidate the prayer.

A latecomer (masbuq) who joins the imam after the rak'ah has already begun faces a question: does he have to follow the imam in the two prostrations (sujud) even though they do not count towards his own prayer? Earlier Hanafi authorities like Qadikhan held it wajib, but later fatwa works from Samarqand declared it sunnah. This lesson walks through the dispute, its resolution, and a common misunderstanding corrected by later scholars.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The case is a person who joins the imam in prayer after the imam has already completed ruku' (i.e., the latecomer missed the rak'ah). The imam then performs the two sujud of that rak'ah. The question: must the latecomer follow the imam in those sujud, even though they will not be counted as part of his own rak'ah?
This is known as 'mutaba'ah' in the context of a masbuq.
2
State the intra-Hanafi positions
Qadikhan and the author of al-Umda ruled it wajib (obligatory). Al-Dhakhira also said wajib but noted that omitting it does not invalidate the prayer. The Imams of Samarqand, as quoted in al-Tajnīs, ruled it sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized sunnah) and that leaving it does not invalidate the prayer.
The disagreement is within the Hanafi school itself.
3
Analyze the evidence and reasoning
Qadikhan emphasized the general obligation of mutaba'ah (following the imam) in prayer. The Samarqand view considered that since the sujud are not counted for the latecomer's rak'ah, the obligation is reduced to a recommended act. The author of al-Bahr al-Raiq (the commentator) initially hesitated but then accepted the sunnah view from al-Tajnīs.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that following the imam in sujud for the missed rak'ah is sunnah mu'akkadah. If the latecomer omits it, his prayer remains valid and does not need repetition or sajdah al-sahw.
This is the view preferred by the commentator and supported by al-Ramli.
5
Understand the critical refinement
Later scholars like the author of al-Nahr and Manh al-Ghaffar misunderstood the issue, objecting that if mutaba'ah is wajib, then omitting it should invalidate the prayer. The commentator and al-Ramli clarified that the earlier statements about 'obligation' were not about legal obligation but simply emphasis, and the sunnah view is the correct one.
This shows the importance of distinguishing between technical and lay usage of terms like 'wajib'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم اعلم أنه إذا لم يكن مدركاً للركعة فإنه يجب عليه أن يتابع الإمام في السجدتين وإن لم يحتسبا له كما لو اقتدى بالإمام بعد ما رفع الإمام رأسه من الركوع. صرح قاضيخان في فتاواه بأن عليه المتابعة في السجدتين وإن لم يحتسبا له وصرح به في العمدة. وصرح في الذخيرة بأن المتابعة فيهما واجبة ومقتضاه أنه لو تركهما لا تفسد صلاته، وقد توقفنا في ذلك مدة حتى رأيت في التجنيس معزياً إلى فتاوى أئمة سمرقند أنه لا تفسد لو ترك وعبارته : رجل انتهى إلى الإمام وقد سجد سجدة فكبر ونوى الاقتداء به ومكث قائماً حتى قام الإمام ولم يتابعه في السجدة لو أتى بها اختلفوا، والصحيح أنه يسن الإتيان بها كما ذكره قاضيخان في شرحه. كذا في البحر وهو مشكل، كيف والجماعة واجبة كما مر ا هـ . وأنت قد سمعت نص كلام قاضيخان وأن ما ذكره المؤلف هو ما نقلناه عنه ولا إشعار له بما ذكره صاحب النهر أصلاً، وقد وقع هذا الوهم أيضاً لتلميذ المؤلف في منح الغفار فذكر عبارة شيخه ثم استشكل بما تقدم في الفجر، وأعجب من هذا أن عبارة الدرر كعبارة قاضيخان وقد ذكر الشيخ اسمعيل إشكال صاحب النهر ووجهه عليها، وقد علمت أن إشكال النهر ليس في هذه الصورة ووقع للشيخ علاء الدين في شرح التنوير نظير ما وقع للشيخ اسمعيل بل أبدع وأغرب محشيه المداري الحلبي فجزم بأن ما في الدرر باطل وتعجب من الشرنبلالي حيث لم يتعرض لذلك في حاشيته على الدرر والحاصل أن أصل السهو من صاحب النهر والمنح منشؤه عدم فهم المسألة، وقد نبه على ذلك العلامة الرملي في حاشيته على المنح وفي حاشيته على هذا الكتاب فقال بعد تصويره المسألة على وجه الصواب فافهم ذلك وكن على بصيرة منه فإن
Then know that if he is not one who caught the rak'ah, then it is obligatory upon him to follow the imam in the two prostrations even if they are not counted for him, just as if he followed the imam after the imam raised his head from ruku'. Qadikhan declared in his Fatawa that he must follow in the two prostrations even if not counted for him, and he declared it in al-Umda. And al-Dhakhira declared that following in them is obligatory, and its implication is that if he leaves them, his prayer is not invalidated. And I hesitated on that for a while until I saw in al-Tajnīs, attributed to the Fatawa of the Imams of Samarqand, that it is not invalidated if he leaves. And his expression: a man reached the imam while he had prostrated one prostration, so he said takbir and intended to follow him, and he remained standing until the imam stood up, and he did not follow him in the prostration; if he performed it, they differed, and the correct is that it is recommended (yasunnu) to perform it, as Qadikhan mentioned in his commentary. This is in al-Bahr, and it is problematic: how can it be when congregation is obligatory as mentioned? End. And you have heard the text of Qadikhan's statement, and that what the author (the commentator) mentioned is what we have quoted from him, and there is no indication in it for what the author of al-Nahr mentioned at all. And this misunderstanding also occurred to the student of the author in Manh al-Ghaffar, who mentioned his teacher's statement then questioned based on what preceded in Fajr. And more amazing than this is that the expression in al-Durar is like Qadikhan's statement, and Sheikh Isma'il mentioned the objection of the author of al-Nahr and addressed it. And you know that the objection of al-Nahr is not in this scenario. And similar occurred to Sheikh Ala' al-Din in his commentary on al-Tanwir, and he innovated and became strange, and his commentator al-Madari al-Halabi asserted that what is in al-Durar is false and wondered at al-Shurnabulali for not addressing it in his gloss on al-Durar. The summary is that the original error is from the author of al-Nahr and Manh, and its source is lack of understanding of the issue. And al-Allama al-Ramli pointed this out in his gloss on Manh and in his gloss on this book, so after depicting the issue correctly, understand that and be insightful about it.
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage discusses the obligation of the latecomer (who missed a rak'ah) to follow the imam in the two prostrations (sujud) of the current rak'ah, even though those prostrations do not count for his own prayer. The author begins by stating that it is obligatory (yajib) to follow the imam in the sujud. Qadikhan in his Fatawa and al-Umda affirm this, while al-Dhakhira states it is wajib but if omitted, the prayer is not invalidated. The author then recounts his hesitation over this, until he found in al-Tajnīs a ruling from the Imams of Samarqand that the prayer is not invalidated by leaving it, and that performing it is sunnah (recommended) not wajib. This leads to a discussion of the apparent contradiction: how can the following be obligatory when the congregation itself is obligatory? The author clarifies that the ruling of following in sujud is sunnah, not wajib, and that the objections of later scholars (like the author of al-Nahr) stem from misunderstanding. He concludes with a warning to understand the issue correctly. The main point is that while following the imam in sujud is recommended, it is not so mandatory that omitting it invalidates the prayer; it is considered a sunnah act.

Key Terms
متابعة (mutaba'ah): Following the imam in prayer actions, here specifically in sujud.
احتسب (ihtasaba): To be counted (for the prayer); here meaning that the sujud is not counted as part of the latecomer's own rak'ah.
تجنييس (tajnīs): A work of Hanafi fiqh (Tajnīs al-Majīd).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (mufta bihi), what is the ruling for a latecomer regarding following the imam in the two prostrations of a rak'ah that he missed?
A) It is wajib and omitting it invalidates the prayer.
B) It is sunnah and omitting it does not invalidate the prayer.
C) It is fard and must be performed.
D) It is makruh to follow in sujud.

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is that a latecomer's following the imam in sujud for the missed rak'ah is sunnah mu'akkadah, and omitting it does not affect the validity of the prayer.

Ruling on a Muqtadi Preceding the Imam in Ruku'
Ruling on muqtadi preceding imam in ruku'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a muqtadi bowing before the imam, explain the condition for validity, and identify the evidence that makes it makruh tahrimi.

Core Idea
A muqtadi's ruku' before the imam is valid if caught, but sinful due to prohibition.

When a follower bows before the imam in congregational prayer, does his ruku' count? The Hanafi school distinguishes between validity and sinfulness. In this lesson, we will examine the ruling, the condition of participation, and the evidence from hadith that makes this action prohibitively disliked.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is the muqtadi doing? He bows (ruku') before the imam, but the imam then bows while the muqtadi is still bowing. The Hanafi ruling: the muqtadi's ruku' is valid but makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked).
The act is the muqtadi preceding the imam in ruku'.
2
State the condition for validity
The condition (shart) for validity is that the imam catches the muqtadi in that ruku'—i.e., the imam bows while the muqtadi is still in ruku', so there is participation (musharaka) in a single part of the action.
If the muqtadi raises his head before the imam bows, it is invalid by agreement.
3
Examine the Hanafi response to Zufar
Zufar argues that the ruku' is invalid because the initial part (before the imam) is not considered, so the later catching does not fix it. The Hanafi response: the condition is participation in a single part, which is satisfied when the imam bows while the muqtadi is still bowing.
This is an intra-Hanafi disagreement.
4
Analyze the dalil from hadith
The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Do not precede me in ruku' and sujud' (لا تبادروني بالركوع والسجود). This prohibition indicates that the act of preceding is sinful, but it does not invalidate the ruku' if the condition of participation is met.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut), so it does not render the act haram but makruh tahrimi.
5
Determine the practical consequence
Since the ruku' is valid, the prayer continues normally, but the muqtadi incurs sin for disobeying the prohibition. The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is that the ruku' is valid but makruh tahrimi.
The muqtadi should avoid repeating the same mistake.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ولو ركع مقتد فأدركه إمامه فيه صح وقال زفر : لا يجزئه لأن ما أتى به قبل الإمام غير معتد به فكذا ما يبنيه عليه. ولنا أن الشرط هو المشاركة في جزء واحد كما في الطرف الأول. قيد بكون إمامه شاركه فيه لأن المقتدي لو رفع رأسه قبل أن يركع الإمام فإنه اتفاقاً لعدم المشاركة فيه والمتابعة وأراد بالركوع كل ركن سبقه المأموم به. وقيده في يصح الذخيره بأن يركع المقتدي بعد فراغ الإمام من القراءة، أما لو ركع قبل أن يأخذ الإمام في القراءة ثم قرأ الإمام وركع والرجل راكع فأدركه في الركوع لا يجزئه عن الركوع لأنه ركع قبل أوانه. ولو ركع بعد ما قرأ الإمام ثلاث آيات ثم أتم القراءة وأدركه جاء، ولو ركع الإمام بعد ما قرأ الفاتحة ونسي السورة فرفع المقتدي معه ثم عاد الإمام إلى السورة ثم ركع والمقتدي على ركوعه الأول أجزأه الركوع ولو تذكر الإمام في ركوعه في الركعة الثالثة أنه ترك سجدة من الركعة الثانية فاستوى الإمام فسجد للثانية وأعاد التشهد ثم قام وركع للثالثة والرجل على حاله راكع لم يجز المقتدي ذلك الركوع والوجه ظاهر ا هـ . وذكر المصنف في الكافي في مسألة الكتاب أنه يصح، ويكره لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام «لا تبادروني بالركوع والسجود) (۱) وقوله عليه السلام أما يخشى الذي يركع قبل الإمام ويرفع أن يحول الله رأسه رأس حمار (۲) اهـ . وهو يفيد أنها كراهة تحريم للنهي المذكور. وفي الخلاصة : المقتدي إذا
His statement: (And if a muqtadi bows and his imam catches him in it, it is valid) contrary to Zufar who says it is not valid because what he did before the imam is not considered, so what is built upon it (the catching) is also not considered. And for us (Hanafis): the condition is participation in a single part, as in the first case. He restricted (the ruling) with the condition that his imam shares with him in it because if the muqtadi raises his head before the imam bows, then it is agreed that it is not valid due to lack of participation and following. And he meant by 'ruku' every integral (rukn) that the follower precedes the imam in. And al-Dhakhira restricted it by saying that the muqtadi should bow after the imam finishes recitation; as for if he bows before the imam begins recitation, then the imam recites and bows while the man is still bowing, and he catches him in the ruku', it does not count as ruku' because he bowed before its proper time. And if he bows after the imam recited three verses, then (the imam) completes the recitation and catches him, it counts. And if the imam bows after reciting al-Fatihah and forgot the surah, so the muqtadi raises with him, then the imam returns to the surah, then bows while the muqtadi is still in his first ruku', his ruku' suffices. And if the imam remembers in his ruku' of the third rak'ah that he left a prostration from the second rak'ah, so the imam straightens up and prostrates for the second (rak'ah) and repeats the tashahhud, then stands and bows for the third while the man is still bowing, the muqtadi's ruku' does not suffice, and the reason is apparent. End quote. And the author (of al-Kenzi?) mentioned in al-Kafi regarding the issue of the book that it is valid, but disliked (makruh) due to his (the Prophet's) statement: 'Do not precede me in ruku' and sujud' and his statement: 'Does not he who bows before the imam and raises (his head) fear that Allah may turn his head into the head of a donkey?' This indicates that it is a makruh tahrimi due to the mentioned prohibition. And in al-Khulasa: the muqtadi if...
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling of a muqtadi (follower) who bows before the imam and then the imam catches him in his ruku' (i.e., the imam bows while the muqtadi is still bowing). The matn states that it is valid (sah). Zufar disagrees, arguing that since the ruku' was performed before the imam, it is not considered valid, and the catching by the imam does not remedy it. The Hanafi response is that the condition for validity is participation in a single part of the action; here, the muqtadi and imam share the ruku' at the same moment. The text further qualifies that this applies only if the imam catches him in that ruku' (i.e., the imam bows while the muqtadi is still in ruku'). If the muqtadi raises his head before the imam bows, then it is invalid by agreement. Al-Dhakhira adds that the muqtadi's ruku' before the imam must occur after the imam has finished his recitation; if it occurs before the imam begins recitation, it is invalid because it is before its proper time. Several scenarios illustrate this: if the muqtadi bows after the imam has recited three verses, and then the imam completes recitation and bows while the muqtadi is still bowing, it counts; but if the imam forgets a surah and returns to it, etc., it may or may not count depending on the circumstances. The final ruling from al-Kafi is that such a ruku' is valid but makruh (disliked) due to the prophetic prohibitions against preceding the imam. The hadith cited indicate that it is a makruh tahrimi (prohibitory dislike), meaning it is sinful but not invalidating.

Key Terms
مقتدي (muqtadi): The person following the imam in congregational prayer.
مبادر (mubadir): One who precedes the imam in an action; here the one who bows before the imam.
كراهة تحريم (karahah tahrimi): A level of prohibition that is sinful but not invalidating; closer to haram but still within the valid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A muqtadi (follower) bows for ruku' before the imam, but the imam then bows while the muqtadi is still in ruku'. What is the Hanafi ruling on the muqtadi's ruku'?
A) It is invalid and the prayer is broken.
B) It is valid but makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked).
C) It is valid and recommended because it shows enthusiasm.
D) It is invalid unless the muqtadi repeats the ruku' after the imam.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a muqtadi's ruku' before the imam is valid if caught, but it is a sin (makruh tahrimi) due to the prophetic prohibition.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
12 min
Rulings on the Muktadi Preceding the Imam in Bowing and Prostration
Ruling with proof and detailed scenarios on preceding the imam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of a follower's prayer when he precedes the imam in bowing, and apply the five-case classification to determine the required makeup rak'ahs.

Core Idea
Preceding the imam in bowing is sinfully disliked, but the prayer remains valid if the imam catches the follower in any part of the action.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on a common scenario in congregational prayer: the follower (muktadi) unintentionally or intentionally performs an action before the imam. The source passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies that while such preceding is prohibited and sinful, the prayer is not automatically invalidated. We will explore the proof, the intra-madhhab dispute with Zufar, and the detailed five-case classification that determines how many rak'ahs must be made up.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
State the act: the follower bows or prostrates before the imam. Then state the Hanafi ruling: the prayer is valid (sahih) but prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi).
The ruling applies if the imam catches the follower in any part of that action.
2
Locate the dalil
The passage cites a hadith: 'Do not precede me in bowing and prostration' and a severe warning. Identify this as a hadith ahad (zanni al-thubut).
The hadith is from Abu Dawood, Tirmidhi, and others.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'la tubadiruni' indicates prohibition. In Hanafi usul, a prohibition (nahy) implies karahah tahrimiyyah, not nullification (butlan). The severe warning reinforces the sinfulness but does not change the validity.
This is why the prayer remains valid despite the prohibition.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Zufar holds that the prayer is invalid because actions before the imam are not considered. The Hanafi response: participation in a single part is sufficient, just as at the start of prayer.
The mufta bihi is validity with karahah, as confirmed by later authorities.
5
Apply the five-case classification
From al-Khulasa, five patterns are given. For each, determine if makeup rak'ahs are required and how many. For example, if the follower precedes in both bowing and prostration in all rak'ahs, he must make up one rak'ah without recitation.
The classification assumes the follower catches the beginning of the imam's prayer (lahiq).

وأدركه الإمام ظاهر أيضاً وهي
He catches the rak'ah. And if a follower bowed and his imam caught him in it, it is valid. Zufar said: It does not suffice him because what he performed before the imam is not considered, so likewise what he builds upon it. Our proof: The condition is participation in a single part, as in the first part. It is conditioned that his imam shares it with him, because if the follower raised his head before the imam bowed, it is agreed it is invalid due to lack of participation and following. By 'bowing' he means every pillar that the follower preceded. Al-Dhakhira conditions validity by the follower bowing after the imam finishes recitation. If he bowed before the imam started recitation, then the imam recited and bowed while the man was still bowing, and the imam caught him in bowing, it does not count for bowing because he bowed before its time. If he bowed after the imam recited three verses, then the imam completed recitation and caught him, it avails. If the imam bowed after reciting al-Fatihah and forgot the surah, so the follower raised with him, then the imam returned to the surah, then bowed while the follower was on his first bowing, the bowing avails him. If the imam remembered in his bowing of the third rak'ah that he left a prostration from the second rak'ah, so the imam rose and prostrated for the second and repeated the tashahhud, then stood and bowed for the third while the man was still bowing, that bowing is not acceptable for the follower. The author mentioned in al-Kafi that it is valid but disliked due to the hadith 'Do not precede me in bowing and prostration' and 'Does he who bows before the imam and lifts fear that Allah will turn his head into a donkey's head?' This indicates it is prohibitively disliked. In al-Khulasa: The follower if... Sahib al-Nahr and Manh al-Ghaffar have mixed and confused in this issue greatly. Allah knows best. His saying: (And if he bowed after the imam recited three verses...) al-Ramli said: it should suffice with one because it is obligatory. After our research, we saw in al-Nahr that the qualification with three verses indicates it is after the obligatory, and it should consider the verse. And if he bowed after the imam recited it and the imam caught him in it, it is valid. His saying: (And the face is apparent) I say: That is based on the dismissal of the rak'ah he was in. Then the follower's bowing is not considered, but it has preceded at the author's saying: if he remembers while bowing or prostrating a prostration so he prostrates it, he does not repeat them, but it is better. The author mentioned there his text, and with what is mentioned here appears the weakness of what is in the fatwas of Imam: if one prayed a rak'ah and left a prostration from it, and prayed another and prostrated for it, then remembered the omitted one... that Qadi Khan from the hadith references. The third case: He came with bowing and prostration before the imam. These are five aspects: either he does both before him, or after, or bowing before and prostrate with him, or bowing with him and prostrate before, or does both before and the imam catches him in the last rak'ahs. If he does bowing and prostration before the imam in all, he must make up one rak'ah without recitation and complete his prayer. If he bows with him and prostrates before, he must make up two rak'ahs. If he bows before and prostrates with him, he makes up four without recitation. If he bows after the imam and prostrates after, his prayer is valid. Its explanation in Fath al-Qadir: The one who catches the first part of the imam's prayer is a latecomer and he makes up before the imam finishes. In the first scenario, he missed the first rak'ah, so his bowing and prostration in the second are compensation for the first. In the second scenario... and the make-up of four in the third is apparent. In al-Khulasa: If the follower raises his head from prostration before the imam, and the imam prolongs the prostration, so the follower thinks the imam is in the second prostration, so he prostrates a second time while the imam is in the first. If he intends to follow the imam, or intends the prostration the imam is in, or intends the first prostration, it is valid. If he intends... Prostration: He raises his head from prostration and prostrates the omitted one, then repeats what was in it because it was dismissed. But you have learned that it is not dismissed and repetition is recommended. Then I saw in the twelfth chapter of al-Dhakhira detail: if he raises his head from the bowing of the third and remembers the prostration of the second, he prostrates it, then recites tashahhud for the second, then prostrates for the third two prostrations, then completes his prayer. Because his return to the omitted prostration does not dismiss the bowing after its completion. That is consistent with the apparent narration. If he remembers while bowing, he prostrates it and recites tashahhud and performs the third and fourth with their bowings and prostrations because bowing before completion is susceptible to dismissal, unlike after raising the head. Evidently, what is here is not according to the apparent narration. Consider his saying: (Or bowing before him and prostrating with him) al-Ramli said in al-Khulasa: He placed his saying 'Or bowing before him and prostrating with him' after his saying 'Or bowing with him and prostrating before him' which is appropriate for the subsequent detail. His saying: (And the imam catches him in the last rak'ahs) the clearer is the expression of al-Nahr: 'and catches him in all the rak'ahs.' Meaning the imam catches him in the last of them in all rak'ahs. His saying: (His prayer is valid) likewise in the fifth picture: if he does both before and the imam catches him in all rak'ahs. The result is that nothing is due from him in the second and fifth pictures. His saying: (And the make-up of four in the third is apparent) meaning the third in the detail, and its explanation as transmitted from al-Khaniyyah: bowing before the imam is not considered, so prostration with him is not considered. So he was not performing all the rak'ahs. Al-Ramli said: and the reason for no make-up in the picture of doing both after or before and the imam catching him is also apparent, and it is...
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary on the matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq discussing the chapter of catching the obligatory prayer. It begins by stating the ruling: if a follower (muktadi) bows before the imam and the imam catches him in that bowing, the follower's prayer is valid. This is the Hanafi position. Zufar disagreed, arguing that what is done before the imam is not valid, so what is built on it is also invalid. The Hanafi proof is that the condition for validity is participation in a single part, just as in the beginning of the prayer. The text then details conditions: the bowing must occur after the imam finishes recitation; if before, it does not count. Various scenarios follow, including when the imam forgets a surah or a prostration. The author mentions that the prayer is valid but makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked) based on authentic hadith prohibiting preceding the imam. The passage then presents a famous five-case classification from al-Khulasa detailing the required makeup rak'ahs for different patterns of preceding. It also discusses a case where the follower raises his head before the imam in prostration and then prostrates again, with conditions on intention. Further, it addresses a scenario where the imam omits a prostration and later remembers. The commentary includes notes from al-Ramli, al-Dhakhira, and others, refining the rulings and noting differences between the apparent narration and other views. The overall authority weight is from the later Hanafi commentary tradition (fatawa mutakhkhirin). The mufta bihi is the validity with karahah tahrimiyyah.

Key Terms
المقتدي (al-muktafī): The follower in congregational prayer who prays behind an imam.
الركوع (al-rukūʿ): Bowing in prayer, a pillar of salah.
كراهة تحريم (karāhah taḥrīmiyyah): Prohibitively disliked; sinful if done deliberately, but the act is not nullified.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the five-case classification from al-Khulasa, if the follower bows before the imam and prostrates with the imam, how many rak'ahs must he make up without recitation?
A) One rak'ah
B) Two rak'ahs
C) Four rak'ahs
D) No makeup required

Key Takeaway
Preceding the imam in prayer is sinfully disliked (makruh tahrimi), but the prayer remains valid if the imam catches the follower in any part of the action.

Five Scenarios of Latecomer's Bowings and Prostrations
Explaining the five cases of a latecomer's bowing and prostration relative to the imam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the five cases of a latecomer's bowing and prostration relative to the imam and state the number of rak'ahs to make up (qaḍāʾ) without recitation in each case.

Core Idea
If a latecomer bows or prostrates before the imam, his prayer is valid but he must make up specific rak'ahs without recitation.

When you join the congregation late, aligning your bowings and prostrations with the imam is critical. But what happens if you accidentally bow or prostrate before or after the imam? Does your prayer break? This passage from Kanz al-Daqāʾiq and its commentary from Fatḥ al-Qadīr and al-Khulāṣa gives the Hanafi rulings for five possible scenarios, clarifying exactly when you owe additional rak'ahs and when your prayer is complete without any qaḍāʾ.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five cases
List the five cases of a latecomer's rukūʿ and sujūd relative to the imam as described in the text.
The four explicit cases are: (1) both before, (2) both after, (3) rukūʿ before + sujūd with, (4) rukūʿ with + sujūd before. The fifth case is both before but imam catches up.
2
Determine the qaḍāʾ requirement for each case
For each case, find the number of rak'ahs that must be made up after the imam's salām, and note that they are prayed without recitation.
Case 1: 1 rak'ah; Case 2 (both after): 0 rak'ah (prayer valid); Case 3: 4 rak'ahs; Case 4: 2 rak'ahs; Fifth case: apparently no qaḍāʾ.
3
Understand the reasoning from Fatḥ al-Qadīr
The latecomer is considered a lāḥiq; his actions are evaluated relative to the imam's sequence. The commentary explains why each case yields a specific number of invalid rak'ahs that need replacement.
The reasoning involves which bowings and prostrations are 'attached' to each other and which are null.
4
Analyze the additional issue from al-Khulāṣa
Examine the scenario where the follower mistakenly prostrates twice due to misjudging the imam's position. The ruling depends on the follower's intention (niyya).
If the follower intends to follow the imam or the correct prostration, it's valid; if he intends the second prostration knowingly, it's invalid.
5
Apply the rulings to practical situations
Given a specific latecomer scenario, determine which case it falls under and what qaḍāʾ is required.
Practice with examples to solidify the distinctions.

أتى بالركوع والسجود قبل الإمام هذه على خمسة أوجه إما أن يأتي بهما قبله أو بعده أو بالركوع قبله وسجد معه أو بالركوع معه وسجد قبله أو أتى بهما قبله ويدركه الإمام في آخر الركعات، فإن أتى بالركوع والسجود قبل الإمام في كلها يجب عليه قضاء ركعة بلا قراءة ويتم صلاته، وإذا ركع معه وسجد قبله يجب عليه قضاء ركعتين وإذا ركع قبله وسجد معه يقضي أربعاً بلا قراءة، وإذا ركع بعد الإمام وسجد بعده جازت صلاته ا هـ. ووجهه في فتح القدير بأن مدرك أول صلاة الإمام لاحق وهو يقضي قبل فراغ الإمام؛ ففي الصورة الأولى فاتته الركعة الأولى فركوعه وسجوده في الثانية قضاء عن الأولى، وفي الثانية، وفي الرابعة عن الثالثة ويقضي بعد الإمام ركعة بغير قراءة لأنه لاحق، وفي الثانية تلتحق سجدتاه في الثانية بركوعه في الأولى لأنه كان معتبراً ويلغوا ركوعه في الثانية لوقوعه عقب ركوعه الأول بلا سجود بقي عليه ركعة ثم ركوعه في الثالثة مع الإمام معتبر ويلتحق به سجوده في رابعة الإمام فيصير عليه الثانية والرابعة فيقضي ركعتين وقضاء الأربع في الثالثة ظاهرا هـ. وفي الخلاصة : المقتدي إذا رفع رأسه من السجدة قبل الإمام وأطال الإمام السجدة فظن المقتدي أن الإمام في السجدة الثانية فسجد ثانياً والإمام في السجدة الأولى إن نوى متابعة الإمام أو نوى السجدة التي فيها الإمام أو نوى السجدة الأولى جاز وإن نوى السجدة الثانية فرفع الإمام رأسه من السجود وانحط للثانية فقبل أن يضع الإمام جبهته على الأرض للسجدة رفع المقتدي من الثانية لا تجوز سجدة المقتدي وكان عليه إعادة تلك السجدة ولو لم يعد تفسد صلاته ا هـ . والله أعلم ..
He performed bowing and prostration before the imam; these are five cases: either he performs them both before him, or after him, or he bows before him and prostrates with him, or he bows with him and prostrates before him, or he performs them both before him and the imam catches up with him in the last rak'ahs. If he performs bowing and prostration before the imam in all (rak'ahs), he must make up one rak'ah without recitation and complete his prayer. If he bows with him and prostrates before him, he must make up two rak'ahs. If he bows before him and prostrates with him, he makes up four without recitation. If he bows after the imam and prostrates after him, his prayer is valid. The explanation in Fath al-Qadir: The one who catches the first part of the imam's prayer is a latecomer and makes up before the imam finishes. In the first case, he missed the first rak'ah; his bowing and prostration in the second (rak'ah) are a replacement for the first. In the second (case?), and in the fourth for the third; he makes up after the imam one rak'ah without recitation because he is a latecomer. In the second (case), his two prostrations in the second (rak'ah) attach to his bowing in the first because it was considered, and his bowing in the second is null because it occurred after his first bowing without prostration; one rak'ah remains upon him. Then his bowing in the third with the imam is considered and his prostration in the imam's fourth attaches to it; so the second and the fourth become incumbent upon him, and he makes up two rak'ahs. The making up of four in the third case is apparent. In al-Khulasa: If the follower raises his head from prostration before the imam and the imam prolongs the prostration, so the follower thinks the imam is in the second prostration and prostrates a second time while the imam is in the first prostration—if he intends following the imam, or intends the prostration in which the imam is, or intends the first prostration, it is valid. If he intends the second prostration, then the imam raises his head from prostration and goes down for the second, and before the imam places his forehead on the ground for the prostration, the follower raises from the second—his prostration is not valid, and he must repeat that prostration; if he does not repeat, his prayer is invalid. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling on the situation of a latecomer (mujtahid) in congregational prayer who performs the bowing (rukūʿ) and prostration (sujūd) at different times relative to the imam. The text presents five scenarios, each with a specific ruling on what must be made up (qaḍāʾ) without recitation. The commentary from Fatḥ al-Qadīr provides the reasoning: the latecomer is considered a lāḥiq (one who catches up) and his actions are evaluated based on alignment with the imam's sequence. The first case: if the follower does both rukūʿ and sujūd before the imam in every rakʿah, he owes one additional rakʿah (without recitation) because his first rakʿah is invalid. Second: if he bows with the imam but prostrates before him, he owes two rakʿahs. Third: if he bows before and prostrates with, he owes four. Fourth: if he does both after the imam, his prayer is valid (no qaḍāʾ). The fifth case (mentioned earlier) is when he does both before and the imam catches up in the last rakʿahs—apparently no qadāʾ. The text then includes a secondary issue from al-Khulāṣa about a follower who mistakenly prostrates twice due to misjudging the imam's position; the ruling depends on his intention.

Key Terms
مقتدي (muqtadī): A follower in congregational prayer who joins after the imam has started.
قضاء (qaḍāʾ): Making up a rakʿah or prayer that was invalidated due to improper sequence.
لاحق (lāḥiq): A follower who joins the prayer late and is considered to have caught the imam in some rakʿahs, making up the missed ones after the imam's salām.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a latecomer bows before the imam but prostrates with him, how many rakʿahs must he make up?
A) None, his prayer is valid
B) One rakʿah without recitation
C) Two rakʿahs without recitation
D) Four rakʿahs without recitation

Key Takeaway
A latecomer's prayer remains valid in all five cases, but he must make up the affected rak'ahs without recitation.

Definitions of Performance, Repetition, and Make-up
Setting the lexicological framework for the chapter on making up missed prayers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definitions of adā', iʿāda, and qaḍā', and distinguish adā' from iʿāda based on timing and defect.

Core Idea
Adā' requires only the opening takbīr within the time; iʿāda repeats in time due to defect; qaḍā' makes up after time.

This passage opens the chapter on making up missed prayers by establishing the threefold classification of obligatory acts. Understanding these definitions is crucial because they determine whether an act fulfills the obligation initially, needs repetition, or must be made up later. The Hanafi school has a distinctive leniency in defining adā' by only requiring the taḥrīma in time.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories
The text divides the commanded act into adā', iʿāda, and qaḍā'. Note that qaḍā' is mentioned as a branch of adā'.
These categories are from uṣūl al-fiqh.
2
Parse the definition of adā'
Adā' is the initial performance of the obligatory act in its specified time. The Hanafi refinement is that it is sufficient for only the taḥrīma (opening takbīr) to occur in the time; the rest may extend beyond.
This contrasts with schools that require the entire act in time.
3
Parse the definition of iʿāda
Iʿāda is performing a like of the act in its time due to a defect. It is used for following the imam or correcting a flaw without missing the time.
Iʿāda does not invalidate the original act; it is a repetition for perfection.
4
Understand qaḍā' by contrast
Qaḍā' is performing a similar act after the time has expired as a substitute. The passage implies it is distinct from adā' because it occurs after the time.
The definition is not given explicitly here but is standard.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Some schools (e.g., Shāfiʿī) define adā' as requiring the entire act within the time, whereas Hanafī only requires the taḥrīma. This has practical implications for prayers that start just before time ends.
The text says 'we did not say as others said'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب قضاء الفوائت لما كان القضاء فرع الأداء أخره. وقد قسم الأصوليون المأمور به إلى أداء وإعادة وقضاء، فالأداء ابتداء فعل الواجب في وقته المقيد به سواء كان ذلك الوقت العمر أو غيره . وإنما لم نقل إنه فعل الواجب كما قال غيرنا لأنه لا يشترط فعله كله في وقته ليكون أداء لأن وجود التحريمة في الوقت كافٍ لكون الفعل أداء والإعادة فعل مثله في وقته لخلل غير وذلك للمتابعة في صورة البعدية والمشاركة في القبلية مع إدراك الإمام له فيهما قوله : (وإن نوى السجدة الثانية) أي ولم ينو المتابعة أيضاً، أما إذا نواهما تكون عن الأولى ترجيحاً للمتابعة وتلغونية غيره للمخالفة كما في الفتح، وكذا إذا لم ينو شيئاً حملاً لأمره على الصواب. فالحاصل كما في الذخيرة أن المسألة على ستة أوجه في الخمسة يصير ساجداً السجدة الأولى، وفي السادسة وهي ما إذا نوى الثانية فحسب يصير ساجداً عن الثانية لأن هذه ثانية باعتبار فعله فالنية صادفت محلها ولم يوجد في معارضته نية أخرى. ثم ذكر مسألة ما إذا أطال المقتدي السجدة الأولى وسجد الإمام الثانية ثم رفع المقتدي رأسه فرأى الإمام ساجداً فظن أنه في السجدة الأولى فسجد قال : فالمسألة أيضاً على ستة أوجه، وفي الوجوه كلها يصير ساجداً . عن الثانية .
Chapter on making up missed prayers. Since qaḍāʾ is a branch of adāʾ, it was delayed (in the order). The scholars of uṣūl have divided the commanded act into adāʾ, iʿāda, and qaḍāʾ. Adāʾ is the initial performance of the obligatory act in its specified time, whether that time is the entire life or something else. We did not say it is the performance of the obligatory act as others said, because it is not necessary that the entire act occur in its time for it to be adāʾ; the presence of the taḥrīma (opening takbīr) in the time suffices for the act to be adāʾ. Iʿāda is performing a like of it in its time due to a defect, for the sake of following (the imam) in the case of delay and participation in precedence, with the imam catching him in both. His statement: 'And if he intended the second prostration' i.e., and he also did not intend following; but if he intended both, it is considered as (from) the first, giving precedence to following and nullifying the other due to contradiction, as in al-Fatḥ. Similarly, if he intended nothing, his action is interpreted as correct. The conclusion, as in al-Dhakhīra, is that the issue has six aspects: in five, he becomes one who prostrates for the first prostration; in the sixth, which is when he intended only the second, he becomes one who prostrates for the second, because this is second according to his action, so the intention met its place and no other intention opposed it. Then he mentioned the issue when the follower prolongs the first prostration and the imam prostrates the second, then the follower raises his head and sees the imam prostrating, so he thinks he is in the first prostration and prostrates. He said: the issue also has six aspects, and in all aspects he becomes one who prostrates for the second.
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on making up missed prayers (qāḍāʾ al-fawāʾit) by defining the three categories of performing obligatory acts: adāʾ (performance in its time), iʿāda (repetition in its time due to a defect), and qāḍāʾ (making up after its time). The author explains that adāʾ is the beginning of the act in its time, and it is sufficient that the opening takbīr (taḥrīma) occurs in the time; the rest can extend beyond. This is a Hanafi refinement to include partial performance. The text then diverges into a continuation of the previous topic about the follower's prostration intention, which seems to be a scribal overlap. The core definition stands as the main point of this section. The definitions are based on uṣūl al-fiqh terminology.

Key Terms
أداء (adāʾ): The initial performance of an obligatory act in its prescribed time, even if only part occurs in the time.
إعادة (iʿāda): Repeating the obligatory act in its time due to a defect that does not invalidate the original.
قضاء (qaḍāʾ): Performing a similar act after the time has expired, as a substitute for the missed obligatory act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi definition, what is sufficient for an act to be considered adā' (performance in time) of a prayer?
A) The entire prayer must be completed within the time
B) The opening takbīr (taḥrīma) must be in the time
C) The first rakʿah must be in the time
D) The intention must be made in the time

Key Takeaway
Adā' is defined by the presence of the opening takbīr in the prescribed time, not by the entire act; iʿāda is a repeat within the time due to a defect; qaḍā' is a make-up after the time.

The Latecomer's Intention in Sujud: Following the Imam's Sequence
Ruling on a follower's invalid prostration due to mismatched intention

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a follower intends a prostration that does not match the imam's current prostration and identify the consequence of failure to correct it.

Core Idea
A follower's prostration is invalid if it does not correspond to the imam's current prostration.

In congregational prayer, the follower (muqtadi) is obligated to follow the imam's actions exactly. This lesson examines a specific scenario: the follower mistakenly intends the second prostration while the imam is still in the first. The ruling clarifies that such a prostration is invalid and must be repeated, otherwise the entire prayer becomes invalid. This highlights the strict requirement of conformity (ittiba') in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its context
Recognize the scenario: the follower is praying behind an imam. The imam performs the first prostration (sajdah), raises his head, then goes down for the second prostration. Before the imam places his forehead for the second prostration, the follower, intending the second prostration, raises his head from his own (presumed) first prostration. What is the act in question? The follower's act of raising from the second prostration (or the prostration itself).
2
Determine the ruling on the follower's prostration
The text states clearly: 'لا تجوز سجدة المقتدي' – the follower's prostration is not valid (la tajuuz). This establishes that the act is legally invalid (batil) because it does not match the imam's current position.
The invalidity arises from the mismatch in intention and action; the follower is not following the imam properly.
3
Identify the required corrective action
The text says: 'وعليه إعادة تلك السجدة' – he must repeat that prostration. The follower must perform the prostration again, this time intending correctly to follow the imam.
This repetition is wajib? The text implies it is obligatory to correct the error.
4
State the consequence of non-correction
If he does not repeat the prostration, the text states: 'تفسد صلاته' – his prayer becomes invalid (fasid). This means the entire prayer is void and must be repeated from the beginning.
This underscores the severity: a single mismatched prostration, if uncorrected, nullifies the whole prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السجدة الثانية وكان الإمام في الأولى فرفع الإمام رأسه من السجدة وانحط للثانية فقبل أن يضع الإمام جبهته على الأرض للسجدة رفع المقتدي من الثانية لا تجوز سجدة المقتدي وكان عليه إعادة تلك السجدة ولو لم يعد تفسد صلاته ا هـ . والله أعلم ..
The second prostration while the imam is in the first. The imam raised his head from prostration and descended for the second. Before the imam placed his forehead on the ground for prostration, the follower raised from the second. The follower's prostration is not valid, and he must repeat that prostration. If he does not repeat, his prayer becomes invalid. End. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage states a ruling regarding a follower (muqtadi) in congregational prayer who mistakenly intends the second prostration when the imam is still in the first. The ruling is that the follower's prostration is invalid because it does not correspond to the imam's action. He must repeat that prostration, otherwise his prayer becomes invalid. This is a specific practical ruling within the Hanafi school regarding following the imam (itba'). The text then concludes with "Allah knows best," indicating the author's deference to divine knowledge.

Key Terms
المقتدي (al-muqtadī): The follower in congregational prayer who prays behind the imam.
السجدة (al-sajdah): Prostration, a pillar of prayer.
الإعادة (al-i'ādah): Repetition of the prostration due to invalidity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The follower's prostration is valid if he intended correctly.
B) The follower's prostration is invalid and must be repeated, otherwise the prayer is invalid.
C) The prayer is automatically valid regardless of intention.
D) The follower should cancel his intention and follow the imam.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a follower must exactly match the imam's sequence; a mismatched prostration is invalid and must be corrected, or the entire prayer is void.

Definitions of Ada', I'ada, and Qada in Hanafi Fiqh
Defining and discussing legal categories.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define ada', i'ada, and qada in Hanafi fiqh and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether i'ada is wajib.

Core Idea
Ada' requires only initiation in time; i'ada repeats a defective prayer; qada is after the time.

In this lesson, we dissect the three key categories of performing wajib acts in Hanafi fiqh: ada', i'ada, and qada. Understanding these definitions is crucial for correctly assessing the validity and obligation of prayers. The passage also explores an important intra-madhhab dispute on whether i'ada (repetition) is mandatory or merely recommended, with implications for when a prayer must be repeated.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Three Categories
Locate the definitions of ada', i'ada, and qada in the passage. Note that qada is presented as a branch of ada' and thus mentioned last.
The text begins by stating the order: 'since qada is a branch of ada', it was mentioned later.'
2
Analyze the Definition of Ada'
Study the text's definition: 'the initial performance of the wajib in its prescribed time.' Notice the key point that only initiation (tahrimah) is required to be within the time; completion may occur later.
The text explicitly states: 'because the existence of the tahrimah in the time is sufficient for the act to be ada'.'
3
Understand I'ada and Its Conditions
Examine the definition of i'ada: repeating the same act in its time due to a khalal (defect) that is not nullifying and does not invalidate the start. Consider the latecomer example to see how i'ada applies in practice.
The text defines i'ada as 'repeating the like of it in its time due to a defect other than invalidity and incorrect commencement.'
4
Evaluate the Dispute on Whether I'ada is Wajib
Identify the two positions: some Hanafi scholars (e.g., from Usul Fakh al-Islam) hold that i'ada is not wajib; others (e.g., from Hidayah) hold that it is. Note the author's reconciliation using the distinction between 'wajib' as fard vs. wajib in the technical sense.
The author states: 'The reconciliation is that the intended meaning of wujub in the statement of Shaykh Akmal al-Din is fardiyyah... and the intended meaning of [others'] wujub is istilahi.'

غيرنا لأنه لا يشترط فعله كله في وقته ليكون أداء لأن وجود التحريمة في الوقت كافٍ لكون الفعل أداء والإعادة فعل مثله في وقته لخلل غير وذلك للمتابعة في صورة البعدية والمشاركة في القبلية مع إدراك الإمام له الوجوه كلها يصير ساجداً . عن الثانية . الفساد وعدم صحة الشروع وهو المراد بقولهم كل صلاة أديت مع كراهة التحريم فسبيلها الإعادة فكانت واجبة فلذا دخلت في أقسام المأمور به والقضاء له تعريفان: أحدهما على أن القضاء يجب بما يجب به الأداء هو فعل الواجب بعد وقته وإن عرف المذهب الصحيح من بما يشمل غير الواجب من السنن التي تقضى فيبدل الواجب بالعبادة، فيقال هو فعل العبادة بعد وقتها ولا يكون خارجاً عن المقسم لأن المندوب مأمور به أيضاً بقوله تعالى وافعلوا مع أمير حاج في شرحه : إن هذا مبني على ما عليه البعض وإلا فقول الميزان الإعادة في عرف الشرع إتيان بمثل الفعل الأول على صفة الكمال بأن وجب على المكلف فعل موصوف بصفة الكمال فأداه على وجه النقصان وهو نقصان فاحش يجب عليه الإعادة وهو إتيان مثل الأول ذاتاً صفة الكمال ا هـ. يفيد أنه إذا فعل ثانياً في الوقت أو خارج الوقت يكون إعادة كما قال صاحب الكشف ا هـ . ونحوه في شرح أصول فخر الإسلام للشيخ أكمل الدين فإنه قال : ولم يذكر الشيخ الإعادة وهي فعل ما فعل أولاً مع ضرب من الخلل ثانياً، وقيل هو إتيان مثل الأول على وجه الكمال لأنها إن كانت واجبة بأن وقع الأول فاسداً فهي داخلة في الأداء أو القضاء، وإن لم تكن واجبة بأن وقع الأول ناقصاً لا فاسداً فلا يدخل في هذا التقسيم لأنه تقسيم الواجب وهي ليست بواجبة. وبالأول يخرج عن العهدة وإن كان على وجه الكراهة على الأصح فالفعل الثاني بمنزلة الجبر كالجبر بسجود السهو ا هـ . وهو موافق لكلام الميزان حيث لم يقيدها بالوقت ومخالف له حيث صرح بعدم وجوبها . وفي شرح التحرير : هل تكون الإعادة واجبة؟ فصرح غير واحد من شراح أصول فخر الإسلام بأنها ليست بواجبة وأن بالأول يخرج عن العهدة وإن كان على وجه الكراهة على الأصح، وإن الثاني بمنزلة الجبر والأوجه الوجوب كما أشار إليه في الهداية وصرح به بعضهم كالشيخ حافظ الدين في شرح المنار وهو موافق لما عن السرخسي وأبي اليسر من ترك الاعتدال تلزمه الإعادة، زاد أبو اليسر ويكون الفرض هو الثاني، وعلى هذا يدخل في تقسيم الواجب. ثم نقل عن شيخه ابن الهمام لا إشكال في وجوب الإعادة إذ هو الحكم في كل صلاة أديت مع كراهة التحريم ويكون جابراً للأول لأن الفرض لا يتكرر، وجعله الثاني يقتضي عدم سقوطه بالأول إذ هو لازم ترك الركن لا الواجب إلا أن يقال : المراد أن ذلك امتنان من الله تعالى إذ يحتسب الكامل وإن تأخر عن الفرض لما علم سبحانه أنه سيوقعه ا هـ. أقول : ويظهر لي التوفيق بأن المراد بالوجوب الافتراض في عبارة الشيخ أكمل الدين لأنه ذكر وجوبها عند وقوع الأول فاسداً، ولا شبهة في أنها حينئذ فرض وذكر عدم الوجوب عند وقوع الأول ناقصاً لا فاسداً ولا شبهة في عدم افتراضها حينئذ . وعلى هذا يحمل كلام شراح أصول فخر الإسلام فلا ينافي ذلك ما أشار إليه في الهداية وصرح به في شرح المنار من أن الأوجه الوجوب لأن المراد به الوجوب المصطلح لا الافتراض قوله : (غير الفساد وعدم صحة الشروع) قال في النهر : لا حاجة إليه إذ اختلال الشيء يؤذن ببقائه ولا له فيما ذكر أهـ. قلت: قد يجاب بأن الخلل وإن لزم منه أن يكون بغير | الفساد وعدم صحة الشروع لكن التصريح باللازم في التعريف غير بدعي تدبر واحترز عن الخلل بغير ما ذكر لأنه لو وجود
(Omitted due to length) The passage defines ada' as the initial performance of the wajib in its time, i'ada as its repetition in the same time due to a defect, and qada as performance after the time. It then discusses various opinions on whether i'ada is obligatory.
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage defines the three categories of performing wajib acts: ada' (initial performance in time), i'ada (repetition in time due to a defect), and qada (performance after time). It starts by stating that qada is a branch of ada', so it is mentioned later. The definition of ada' includes that the act must be initiated in its time, even if not completed. I'ada is defined as repeating the act in the same time due to a defect that is not nullifying and does not invalidate the start. The text then gives an example from the latecomer's situation to illustrate i'ada. It then discusses qada, giving two definitions: one specific to wajib acts and one general including sunan. This is followed by a dispute about whether i'ada is wajib or not. The author reconciles the positions by noting that "wajib" in some contexts means fard (when the first was invalid) and in others means wajib in the technical sense (when the first was makruh).

Key Terms
أداء (adā'): The initial performance of a wajib act in its prescribed time, with initiation (tahrimah) occurring within the time.
إعادة (i'ādah): Repeating a wajib act in its same time due to a defect (khalal) that is not nullifying and does not invalidate the start.
قضاء (qaḍā'): Performing a wajib act after its prescribed time, whether the obligation is by the same cause as ada' or by a general command.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the key condition for an act to be considered ada'?
A) The entire act must be completed within the prescribed time.
B) The initiation (tahrimah) must occur within the prescribed time.
C) The act must be performed without any defect.
D) The act must be performed with intention.

Key Takeaway
Ada' requires only initiation in time; i'ada repeats a defective prayer within time; qada is after time; and the obligation of i'ada is a settled ikhtilaf resolved by distinguishing fard from wajib.

Qada and I'ada: Definitions and the Obligation of Repetition
Expounds definitions of qada and i'ada and debates obligation of i'ada

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two definitions of qada, define i'ada, and explain the Hanafi position on when i'ada is wajib.

Core Idea
Qada is the same obligation performed late; i'ada is wajib only if the first prayer was fasid, otherwise it is a compensatory act.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq opens the chapter on making up missed prayers. It first defines the key terms qada and i'ada, then delves into an intra-Hanafi debate about whether repeating a prayer performed with a deficiency (karahah tahrimiyyah) is obligatory. The author reconciles conflicting positions by distinguishing between a prayer that was fasid (void) and one that was merely naqis (deficient but valid). Understanding this distinction is crucial for determining whether a missed or deficient prayer must be repeated.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two definitions of qada
Locate where the author presents two definitions: one stating qada is the same wajib performed after its time, and another (weaker) stating it is a 'like' (mithl) of the wajib due to a new cause. Note which is relied upon.
The first definition is the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school.
2
Define i'ada and its trigger
Find the definition of i'ada: repeating an act of worship that was initially performed with a deficiency. Note the condition: i'ada is wajib when the first act was fasid; otherwise it is a compensatory act (jabr).
I'ada is linked to prayers performed with karahah tahrimiyyah.
3
Identify the intra-Hanafi dispute
The author cites scholars who say i'ada is wajib for any prayer with karahah tahrimiyyah (e.g., al-Hidayah), and others who say i'ada is not wajib (e.g., Usul of Fakhr al-Islam). Trace the arguments.
The dispute centers on whether the first prayer fulfills the obligation.
4
Understand the author's reconciliation
The author resolves the conflict by distinguishing between a fasid first prayer and a naqis first prayer. If fasid, i'ada is fard; if naqis, i'ada is not fard but a jabar.
This reconciliation is the mufta bihi position.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Given a scenario where a person prayed with a deficiency, determine whether i'ada is wajib based on whether the deficiency made the prayer fasid or merely naqis.
Consider examples like missing a rukn (fasid) vs. missing a wajib (naqis).

Source Text

الفساد وعدم صحة الشروع وهو المراد بقولهم كل صلاة أديت مع كراهة التحريم فسبيلها الإعادة فكانت واجبة فلذا دخلت في أقسام المأمور به والقضاء له تعريفان: أحدهما على أن القضاء يجب بما يجب به الأداء هو فعل الواجب بعد وقته وإن عرف · المذهب الصحيح من بما يشمل غير الواجب من السنن التي تقضى فيبدل الواجب بالعبادة، فيقال هو فعل العبادة بعد وقتها ولا يكون خارجاً عن المقسم لأن المندوب مأمور به أيضاً بقوله تعالى وافعلوا مع أمير حاج في شرحه : إن هذا مبني على ما عليه البعض وإلا فقول الميزان الإعادة في عرف الشرع إتيان بمثل الفعل الأول على صفة الكمال بأن وجب على المكلف فعل موصوف بصفة الكمال فأداه على وجه النقصان وهو نقصان فاحش يجب عليه الإعادة وهو إتيان مثل الأول ذاتاً صفة الكمال ا هـ. يفيد أنه إذا فعل ثانياً في الوقت أو خارج الوقت يكون إعادة كما قال صاحب الكشف ا هـ . ونحوه في شرح أصول فخر الإسلام للشيخ أكمل الدين فإنه قال : ولم يذكر الشيخ الإعادة وهي فعل ما فعل أولاً مع ضرب من الخلل ثانياً، وقيل هو إتيان مثل الأول على وجه الكمال لأنها إن كانت واجبة بأن وقع الأول فاسداً فهي داخلة في الأداء أو القضاء، وإن لم تكن واجبة بأن وقع الأول ناقصاً لا فاسداً فلا يدخل في هذا التقسيم لأنه تقسيم الواجب وهي ليست بواجبة. وبالأول يخرج عن العهدة وإن كان على وجه الكراهة على الأصح فالفعل الثاني بمنزلة الجبر كالجبر بسجود السهو ا هـ . وهو موافق لكلام الميزان حيث لم يقيدها بالوقت ومخالف له حيث صرح بعدم وجوبها . وفي شرح التحرير : هل تكون الإعادة واجبة؟ فصرح غير واحد من شراح أصول فخر الإسلام بأنها ليست بواجبة وأن بالأول يخرج عن العهدة وإن كان على وجه الكراهة على الأصح، وإن الثاني بمنزلة الجبر والأوجه الوجوب كما أشار إليه في الهداية وصرح به بعضهم كالشيخ حافظ الدين في شرح المنار وهو موافق لما عن السرخسي وأبي اليسر من ترك الاعتدال تلزمه الإعادة، زاد أبو اليسر ويكون الفرض هو الثاني، وعلى هذا يدخل في تقسيم الواجب. ثم نقل عن شيخه ابن الهمام لا إشكال في وجوب الإعادة إذ هو الحكم في كل صلاة أديت مع كراهة التحريم ويكون جابراً للأول لأن الفرض لا يتكرر، وجعله الثاني يقتضي عدم سقوطه بالأول إذ هو لازم ترك الركن لا الواجب إلا أن يقال : المراد أن ذلك امتنان من الله تعالى إذ يحتسب الكامل وإن تأخر عن الفرض لما علم سبحانه أنه سيوقعه ا هـ. أقول : ويظهر لي التوفيق بأن المراد بالوجوب الافتراض في عبارة الشيخ أكمل الدين لأنه ذكر وجوبها عند وقوع الأول فاسداً، ولا شبهة في أنها حينئذ فرض وذكر عدم الوجوب عند وقوع الأول ناقصاً لا فاسداً ولا شبهة في عدم افتراضها حينئذ . وعلى هذا يحمل كلام شراح أصول فخر الإسلام فلا ينافي ذلك ما أشار إليه في الهداية وصرح به في شرح المنار من أن الأوجه الوجوب لأن المراد به الوجوب المصطلح لا الافتراض قوله : (غير الفساد وعدم صحة الشروع) قال في النهر : لا حاجة إليه إذ اختلال الشيء يؤذن ببقائه ولا له فيما ذكر أهـ. قلت: قد يجاب بأن الخلل وإن لزم منه أن يكون بغير | الفساد وعدم صحة الشروع لكن التصريح باللازم في التعريف غير بدعي تدبر واحترز عن الخلل بغير ما ذكر لأنه لو وجود
Book of Prayer, Chapter of Making up Missed Prayers. Corruption and lack of validity of commencement is what is meant by their statement: Every prayer performed with karahah tahrimiyyah, its repetition (i'ada) is required, so it was wajib. Hence it entered into the divisions of the commanded. And qada has two definitions: One, that qada is obligatory by that by which the performance (ada) is obligatory, it is the act of the wajib after its time, even if it is known... the correct school includes non-wajib from the sunan that are made up, substituting the wajib with the act of worship. So it is said: It is the act of worship after its time, and it is not outside the division because mandub is also commanded by His statement "and do good" (22:77) but it is metaphorical, so most did not include it in the definition. The application of qada in the speech of the jurists to what is not wajib is metaphorical, as occurred in the statement of al-Mukhtasar where he said: "He made up that which was before Zuhr." Similarly, the application of qada by the jurists to Hajj after its corruption is metaphorical, as it has no time by the exit of which it becomes qada. The second (definition) is upon the weak position that qada is obligatory due to a new cause, so it is the delivery of the like of the wajib. And he who added upon it a command — like the author of al-Manar — has contradicted himself because what is done after the time is the very wajib by command, not its like. For what is understood from the command is the demand of two things: the action and its being in its time. When he is unable for the second due to its passing, the command remains requiring the first. So his explicit mention of "like" requires it being due to a new cause, and his explicit mention of "command" requires it being the very act. Full verification is in our book named Lub al-Usul, abridgment of Tahrir al-Usul: The difference mentioned regarding the cause of qada has no effect, as known by those who study the books of usul. In Kashf al-Asrar: The similitude in qada is in removing sin, not in attaining virtue. The apparent meaning is that the sin referred to is the omission of the prayer, so he will not be punished for it when he makes it up. As for the sin of delaying it from its time, which is a major sin, it remains and is not removed by mere qada without repentance; repentance is necessary. And it is permissible to delay the prayer from its time due to an excuse, as al-Walwaliji said in his Fatawa: If she is busy with prayer and fears her child may die, there is no harm in her delaying the prayer and attending to the child, because delaying the prayer from its time is permissible due to an excuse. Do you not see that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) delayed the prayer from its time on the day of al-Khandaq? Similarly, if a traveler fears thieves and highway robbers, it is permissible for them to delay the time-bound prayer because of the excuse. In al-Mujtaba: The correct view is that delaying missed prayers due to striving for one's family and in necessary matters is permissible, it was said: even if it is obligatory immediately, he is permitted to delay. From Abu Ja'far: The prostration of recitation, absolute vow, and making up Ramadan are broad in time. Al-Halwani and al-Amiri made it narrow. Al-Walwaliji mentioned regarding fasting: Making up fasting is at leisure, and making up prayer is immediate except for an excuse. His statement: (And order between the missed and the time-bound, and between missed prayers is due (mustahaqq) beneficial for two things: one by explicit wording and the other by implication. As for the second, it is the obligation of making up the missed prayer. The basis for it is that every prayer that was missed... it is according to one of them, so the action is performance (ada') if it falls within the time, and qada if it falls outside it. His statement: (And he who added upon it a command) al-Nahr said: Some verifiers said: The identity and similitude are in relation to what is known from the command. For if the commanded act is the very thing known, it is ada'; if it is its like, it is qada. This is because the Lawgiver commanded him to pray, and he did not perform it, so it remains in his obligation, and he has the ability to perform its like, because voluntary prayer is legislated for him of the same kind as what is due, and it is its like. So he was commanded to redirect his voluntary act to what is due as qada. By this the contradiction is resolved, so reflect. Sheikh Ismail said: It is not hidden what is in it of burden, and how can it be said that he redirected his voluntary act to what is due of qada of the obligatory, so reflect.
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq, a Hanafi sharh of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, opens the chapter on making up missed prayers (Qada al-Fawa'it). The author first defines the key terms: 'qada' and 'i'ada'. He states that any prayer performed with karahah tahrimiyyah requires repetition (i'ada), and this i'ada is wajib, thus it falls under the category of the commanded. He then presents two definitions of qada. The first definition (the relied-upon view) holds that qada is the same obligation as ada, merely performed after the designated time. This definition includes both wajib and sunan that are made up. The second definition (weak) holds that qada is a new obligation due to a separate cause, and the act is a 'like' (mithl) of the wajib rather than the same act. The author then delves into a intra-Hanafi debate: Is i'ada (repeating a prayer that was performed with some deficiency) wajib? He cites several authorities: Some, like the authors of Usul Fiqh of Fakhr al-Islam, say i'ada is not wajib; the first prayer suffices even if performed with karahah, and the second act is merely a jabar (compensation) like sajdat al-sahw. Others, like al-Hidayah and Sharh al-Manar, favor wujub, especially for missing an essential part like rukn. Al-Sarakhsi and Abu al-Yusr hold that i'ada is required for leaving i'tidal, and Abu al-Yusr goes further to say the second becomes the actual fard. The author then reconciles: When the first prayer was fasid (void), i'ada is fard. When it was merely naqis (deficient) but not fasid, i'ada is not fard but rather a jabar. This resolves the apparent contradiction in the texts. The passage also discusses the definition of qada more broadly, including the issue of using 'qada' for non-obligatory acts (metaphorically) and the debate over whether qada is the same act or a like act. The author concludes that the practical difference (thamar al-khilaf) is minimal. This is a dense technical discussion typical for advanced students of Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
قضاء (qada'): Fulfilling an obligation after its designated time; either the same act (first definition) or its like (second definition).
إعادة (i'ada): Repeating an act of worship that was initially performed with a deficiency.
كراهة التحريم (karahah tahrimiyyah): A degree of prohibition in Hanafi fiqh just short of haram; acts with karahah tahrimiyyah are sinful if done, and the prayer so performed must be repeated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author's reconciliation, when is i'ada (repeating a prayer) wajib?
A) Whenever the prayer was performed with karahah tahrimiyyah.
B) Only when the first prayer was fasid (void).
C) Only when the first prayer was naqis (deficient).
D) I'ada is never wajib; it is always optional.

Key Takeaway
I'ada is wajib only when the first prayer is fasid; otherwise, it is a compensatory act (jabr) and the first prayer suffices.

Salah — Prayer

Tartib Between Missed and Current Prayers: Obligation and Exceptions
Ruling on tartib with evidence and exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on tartib between missed and current prayers, identify when it drops, and apply the Hanafi position on delaying prayer due to a valid excuse.

Core Idea
Tartib is wajib but drops when time is tight; delay is allowed for genuine excuses.

The Hanafi school holds that performing missed prayers in order (tartib) is an obligation, but this obligation is not absolute. It can be waived when the time for the current prayer is constricted, or when a valid excuse justifies delay. This lesson unpacks the ruling from Al-Bahr al-Raiq, examining the proof from the Prophet's ﷺ action at Khandaq and the fatwa of al-Walwaliji allowing a mother to delay prayer to save her child.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling on Tartib
The matn states that tartib between missed and current prayers, and among missed prayers, is 'mustahaqq' (due). Under Hanafi usul, this indicates wujub (obligation). Recognize that 'mustahaqq' here means wajib, not fard.
2
Identify the Exception: Constriction of Time
The matn adds 'يسقط بضيق الوقت' (it drops with constriction of time). Understand that when the remaining time for the current prayer is so short that only its essential parts can be performed, the obligation of tartib is lifted.
3
Examine the Evidence for Permissibility of Delay
The commentator cites al-Walwaliji's fatwa allowing a woman to delay prayer if she fears her child's death, and the Prophet's ﷺ delaying prayer during the Battle of the Trench. This establishes that a valid excuse (e.g., fear of harm) permits postponing the prayer.
4
Differentiate Between Immediate and Delayed Qada
The text notes intra-Hanafi differences: al-Halwani and al-Amiri held qada must be immediate, while the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that delay for excuse is allowed. For fasting, qada is at leisure; for prayer, it is immediate except with excuse.
5
Apply the Ruling to a Scenario
Consider a traveler who fears bandits. According to the fatwa, he may delay the current prayer until safe. Similarly, a person who has three missed prayers and the current Asr time is about to expire may perform Asr first and then make up the missed ones after.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
