Commentary
This concluding passage synthesizes the earlier discussion on i'adah. The author first confirms that the obligation of i'adah is restricted to the prayer's time, as per the definition from Sharh al-Manar. After time, i'adah is better (afdal) but not obligatory. This resolves apparent contradictions with the statement 'every prayer performed with karahah is to be repeated'. The author then adds a point not covered earlier: if a prayer is performed with karahah tanzihiyyah (light dislike, e.g., leaving a sunnah), i'adah is recommended (mustahabb) but not obligatory. This is supported by al-Shurunbulali's argument from al-Tajnisi that the general wording 'every prayer performed with karahah' includes both types. However, Abu al-Yusr distinguishes: for karahah tahrimiyyah, i'adah is wajib; for tanzihiyyah, it is not. The author concludes by citing Fath al-Qadir that the detailed view is correct: tahrimiyyah requires wajib i'adah, tanzihiyyah makes it mustahabb. He urges the reader to grasp this refined analysis. The commentary follows the author's order, clarifying the Hanafi position that i'adah is time-specific, and that the degree of karahah determines the ruling (wajib vs. mustahabb).

Key Terms
كراهة التنزيه (karahah al-tanzih): A light dislike, such as leaving a sunnah; renders i'adah recommendable rather than obligatory.
إعادة مندوبة (i'adah mandubah): A recommended repetition, not obligatory, applicable when deficiency is due to leaving a sunnah or performing after time.

Ruling on Missing One Prayer of a Day
Ruling for a person who missed a single prayer of a day and does not know which one

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a person who missed one prayer of a day and cannot identify which one, and explain the principle that certainty of obligation is not removed by doubt.

Core Idea
Certainty of obligation is not removed by doubt — all prayers of the day must be repeated.

Imagine you know you missed one of the five daily prayers, but you cannot recall which one. This common scenario tests our understanding of certainty and doubt in Islamic law. In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi position based on the principle that what is certain cannot be undone by uncertainty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and ruling
The passage describes a person who is certain that one prayer of the day was missed but does not know which one. The ruling is that he must repeat all prayers of that day.
The ruling applies to any obligatory prayer missed with certainty.
2
Extract the underlying principle
The principle is that certainty of obligation (the missed prayer) cannot be discharged by doubt (not knowing which one). The person owes a prayer, so he must repeat until the obligation is fulfilled.
This is a core Hanafi usul principle: al-yaqīn lā yazūlu bi al-shakk.
3
Note the authority
The ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah, specifically cited in al-Tajnīs and other works, making it the relied-upon position.
The authority level confirms the ruling is mufta bihi.
4
Compare with other schools
The Shafi'i school holds that if uncertain, one repeats only the prayers likely to have been missed, not necessarily all. This difference stems from different treatments of doubt.
This comparison highlights the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).

Source Text

And in al-Tajnīs and others: A man missed one prayer of a day and does not know which prayer it was, then he repeats the prayers of a day, obligatory with certainty, so he does not discharge the obligation by doubt.

This passage presents a ruling from the Hanafi school concerning a person who knows he missed one prayer during a day but cannot identify which one. Since he is certain that an obligatory prayer was missed, he must repeat all the prayers of that entire day. This is based on the principle that certainty of obligation cannot be removed by doubt. The ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah as transmitted in al-Tajnīs and other works.

Key Terms

Rulings on Doubt in Prayer: Within Time vs. After Time
Rulings on doubt whether prayer was performed and doubt about missing a rak'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi ruling on doubt about performing a prayer depending on whether it arises within or after the prescribed time, and apply the same principle to doubt about deficiency in prayer.

Core Idea
Certainty of obligation requires action; doubt about prior performance prevents obligation.

In daily worship, one may sometimes doubt whether a prayer was performed or whether a rak'ah was missed. The Hanafi school provides clear rulings based on the concepts of cause of obligation (sabab al-wujub) and condition of discharge. This lesson unpacks the passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, showing how the same logical structure applies to both types of doubt, and how the timing of the doubt determines the legal consequence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios of doubt
The passage covers two distinct doubts: (1) doubt about whether a prayer was performed at all, and (2) doubt about missing a rak'ah within the prayer. For each, the ruling depends on when the doubt arises—before or after the time ends, or before or after the prayer ends.
Keep these two categories separate; they are governed by the same principle but applied differently.
2
Apply the principle of sabab al-wujub and condition
For doubt about performing the prayer: within the time, the cause of obligation (time) is still present, and the condition of having performed it is doubtful—so the prayer must be repeated. After the time, the cause has ceased, and the condition for qada (non-performance) is doubtful—so no repetition is required.
The key is that obligation is not imposed when the condition for its discharge is uncertain.
3
Determine the ruling for doubt about deficiency
If doubt about a missing rak'ah arises before finishing (before salam), the person must build on certainty and complete the prayer, sitting for tashahhud after every rak'ah as a precaution. If the doubt arises after salam, nothing is required—the prayer is presumed valid.
This mirrors the first scenario: before finishing, the act is still in progress (cause present); after finishing, the cause is resolved.
4
State the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon Hanafi position (mufta bihi) is: repeat within time, do not repeat after time; for deficiency doubt, complete the prayer if still in it, but do nothing after salam. This is based on Zahir al-Riwayah and is consistent across the school.
The Shafi'i school differs for post-time doubt, but within Hanafi this is settled.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا شك في صلاة أنه صلاها أم لا، فإن كان في الوقت فعليه أن يعيد لأن سبب الوجوب قائم وإنما لا يعمل هذا السبب بشرط الأداء قبله وفيه شك، وإن خرج الوقت ثم شك فلا شيء عليه لأن سبب الوجوب قد فات. وإنما يجب القضاء بشرط عدم الأداء قبله وفيه شك، وإن شك في نقصان الصلاة أنه ترك ركعة فإن لم يفرغ من الصلاة فعليه إتمامها ويقعد في كل ركعة وإن شك بعد ما فرغ وسلم لا شيء عليه لما قلنا ا هـ .
And if he doubts about a prayer whether he prayed it or not, then if it is within the time, he must repeat it because the cause of obligation is present, and this cause only becomes ineffective with the condition of prior performance, and there is doubt about that. And if the time has exited and then he doubts, then nothing is upon him because the cause of obligation has ceased. And the making up of prayers is only obligatory with the condition of non-performance prior, and there is doubt about that. And if he doubts about a deficiency in the prayer, that he left a rak'ah, then if he has not yet finished the prayer, he must complete it and sit in every rak'ah, and if he doubts after finishing and making salam, then nothing is upon him, as we have said.
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage gives detailed rulings on two types of doubt: (1) doubt about whether a prayer was performed at all, and (2) doubt about a deficiency in the prayer (e.g., missing a rak'ah). For the first, if doubt arises during the prayer's prescribed time, the prayer must be repeated because the cause of obligation (the time) is still present, and the condition of having performed it is doubtful. After the time exits, no repetition is needed because the cause of obligation is gone, and the condition for qada (having not performed it) is doubtful. For the second type, if doubt about deficiency arises before completing the prayer, one must build on certainty and complete it, sitting for tashahhud in every rak'ah as a precaution. If doubt arises after salam, no action is required because the prayer is presumed valid.

Key Terms
سبب الوجوب (sabab al-wujūb): The cause that makes an act obligatory; here, the entry of time for the prayer.
قضاء (qaḍā'): Performing a missed obligatory prayer after its prescribed time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person doubts during the prayer that he missed a rak'ah, what should he do?
A) Stop praying and start over
B) Complete the prayer and sit in every rak'ah
C) Continue and ignore the doubt
D) Perform sajda al-sahw only

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school treats doubt about an act of worship by examining the cause of obligation: if the cause is present and the condition of discharge is uncertain, the act is required; if the cause has ended and the condition for qada is uncertain, no action is required.

Definition of I'adah and Its Time-Bound Obligation
Definition of i'adah with time restriction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of i'adah and explain why its obligation is confined to the time.

Core Idea
I'adah is repeating an act performed with a gross deficiency; it is wajib within the time, not after.

This passage defines i'adah as the repetition of an act that was performed with a gross deficiency in its essential or perfective attributes. According to the Hanafi school, such repetition is obligatory only within the prescribed time. Understanding this definition helps clarify when a prayer must be repeated and when merely making up later is acceptable.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition
Locate the phrase 'الإتيان بمثل ما فعل أولاً مع نقصان فاحش ذاتاً صفة الكمال' – performing the like of what one did first with a gross deficiency in essence or attribute of perfection.
This is the classical definition.
2
Understand 'gross deficiency'
A deficiency in the act's essential components (arkan) or perfective qualities (sifat kamal) that is significant (fahish).
Minor deficiencies do not require i'adah.
3
Note the time restriction
The text states that i'adah is wajib only within the time (waqt). After the time, it is merely better (afdal) according to one view.
There is a dispute on whether i'adah is wajib after time, but the definition given restricts it to the time.
4
Apply to a scenario
If someone prays without wudu (a gross deficiency), they must repeat the prayer within its time. If they do not, they have sinned and must make it up later, but the later performance is not 'i'adah' in the technical sense.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتحصل من هذا أن بوجوب الإعادة يقيدها بالوقت كما قال المصنف في شرح المنار من قال الإعادة الإتيان بمثل ما فعل أولاً مع نقصان فاحش ذاتاً صفة الكمال لأنه إذا وجب على المكلف فعل موصوف بصفة فأداه ناقصاً نقصاناً فاحشاً يجب عليه إعادته في وقته ا هـ. ويكون على هذا القول فعلها بعد الوقت أفضل كما أفاده كلام القنية في مسألة قضاء صلاة العمر، وعلى القول الآخر في الإعادة يكون هي الأفضل في الوقت وبعده كما أفاده ما رقم له في القنية ثانياً، فقد ظهر لك أن ما ذكره المؤلف في هذا الحاصل موافق لما ذكره في تعريف الإعادة وأنه لا مخالفة بين التعريف وبين قولهم كل صلاة «الخ خلافاً لما يفهم من قوله وقد قدمنا الخ»، واندفع ما ذكره المقدسي. بقي هنا شيء لم يتعرض له المؤلف وهو أنه لو أداها مع كراهة التنزيه فالأفضل إعادتها أيضاً كما ذكره الشرنبلالي في إمداد الفتاح مستدلاً بعموم قول التجنيس كل صلاة أديت مع الكراهة فإنها تعادلا على وجه الكراهة قال وهذا شامل للإعادة بكراهة التنزيه ولا يمنع منه تمثيل الشيخ أكمل الدين بالواجب في قوله وتعاد على وجه غير مكروه أي تعاد الصلاة للاحتياط على وجه ليس فيه كراهة وهو الحكم في كل صلاة أديت مع الكراهة كما إذا ترك واجباً من واجبات الصلاة ا هـ . بترك الواحب واجبة فلا يمنع أن تكون الإعادة مندوبة بترك سنة لأن المكروه موجود بترك السنة والنكرة في سياق النفي بقوله تعاد على وجه ليس فيه كراهة تعم المكروه تنزيهاً وتحريماً ا هـ. كلام الشرنبلالي قلت ويوافقه ما قال القهستاني وفي التمرتاشي : لو صلى وفي ثوبه صورة وجب الإعادة. وقال أبو اليسر : هذا هو الحكم في كل صلاة أديت مع كراهة التحريم؛ وفيه إشعار بأن كراهة التنزيه لا توجب وجوب الإعادة وكذا كراهة التحريم عند غير أبي اليسر بل الأولى أن تعاد عندهم ا هـ . وفي مكروهات الصلاة من فتح القدير والحق التفصيل بين كون تلك الكراهة كراهة تحريم فتجب الإعادة أو تنزيه فتستحب ا هـ . فاغتنم هذا التحرير .
And it is obtained from this that the obligation of i'adah is restricted to the time, as the author said in Sharh al-Manar: 'Whoever said i'adah is performing the like of what one did first with a gross deficiency in the essence or attribute of perfection, because if an act described with a quality is obligatory upon the mukallaf, and he performs it deficiently in a gross deficiency, then he must repeat it in its time' end quote. And according to this statement, performing it after the time is better, as indicated by the words of al-Qunyah in the issue of making up the prayer of a lifetime. And according to the other statement in i'adah, it is better both in time and after, as indicated by what is marked in al-Qunyah secondly. So it has become clear to you that what the author mentioned in this summary matches what he mentioned in the definition of i'adah, and there is no contradiction between the definition and their statement 'every prayer' contrary to what is understood from his saying 'and we have presented' etc., and the objection of al-Maqdisi is repelled. There remains something here that the author did not address: if he performed it with karahah tanzih, then repeating it is better, as mentioned by al-Shurnubalali in Imdad al-Fattah, using as evidence the general application of the statement in al-Tajnis: 'Every prayer performed with karahah is repeated', on a disliked manner. He said: 'This includes i'adah with karahah tanzih, and the example of Shaykh Akmal al-Din with the obligatory does not prevent it, in his statement: it is repeated in a non-disliked manner, meaning the prayer is repeated for precaution in a manner without dislike, and that is the ruling for every prayer performed with karahah, such as when he leaves an obligatory act of the prayer' end quote. By leaving an obligatory act—an obligatory act—so it does not prevent that the i'adah be recommended due to leaving a sunnah, because the disliked exists with leaving the sunnah, and the indefinite in the context of negation in his statement 'it is repeated in a manner without dislike' includes both tanzih and tahrim. I say: and this is supported by what al-Qahistani said: 'And in al-Tamartashi: if he prayed while there was an image on his garment, i'adah is obligatory.' And Abu al-Yusr said: 'This is the ruling for every prayer performed with karahah tahrim; and it indicates that karahah tanzih does not necessitate obligation of i'adah, likewise karahah tahrim according to others besides Abu al-Yusr, rather it is preferable that it be repeated according to them.' And in the Makruhat of al-Fath al-Qadir: 'The truth is the distinction: if that karahah is tahrim, i'adah is obligatory; if tanzih, it is recommended.' So seize this tahreer.
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage is an advanced discussion on the definition of i'adah (repetition) and its application to prayers performed with karahah (dislike). The author explains that i'adah is defined as repeating an act that was performed with a gross deficiency in its essential or perfective attributes, and such repetition is obligatory within the time. There are two views on repeating after the time: one holds it is better, another holds it is obligatory. The author then resolves apparent contradictions and discusses the specific case of prayers performed with karahah tanzih (disliked but not prohibitively). Citing al-Shurnubalali, the general ruling from al-Tajnis is that every prayer performed with karahah should be repeated without dislike. The discussion distinguishes between karahah tahrim (prohibitively disliked) and tanzih (lightly disliked): the former necessitates obligatory repetition, the latter makes it recommended. This is the relied-upon position.

Key Terms
إعادة (i'ādah): Repeating an act of worship due to a significant deficiency in its performance, wajib only within the time.
نقصان فاحش (nuqṣān fāḥish): A gross deficiency in the essential parts or perfective attributes of an act of worship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi definition, i'adah is wajib only:
A) Within the time
B) After the time
C) At any time
D) Never

Key Takeaway
I'adah is defined as repeating an act with a gross deficiency, and its obligation is confined to the time.

Ruling on Repeating a Prayer Performed with Karahah: Tahrim vs Tanzih
Ruling on i'adah for prayers with karahah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between karahah tahrim and tanzih and state the Hanafi ruling on i'adah for each.

Core Idea
For a prayer performed with karahah tahrim, i'adah is wajib; for tanzih, it is mustahabb.

The passage builds on the definition of i'adah and applies it to prayers performed with dislike (karahah). The relied-upon Hanafi position distinguishes between two levels of karahah: prohibitively disliked (tahrim) and merely offensive (tanzih). For the former, repetition is obligatory; for the latter, it is recommended. This nuance helps avoid overly strict or overly lenient rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of karahah
From the text, locate references to 'كراهة التحريم' and 'كراهة التنزيه'. Understand that they are distinct levels.
Karahah tahrim is closer to haram; tanzih is less severe.
2
Find the ruling for each
The passage cites al-Fath al-Qadir: 'الحق التفصيل بين كون تلك الكراهة كراهة تحريم فتجب الإعادة أو تنزيه فتستحب'. So for tahrim, i'adah is wajib; for tanzih, mustahabb.
3
Understand the evidence
The general principle from al-Tajnis: 'كل صلاة أديت مع الكراهة فإنها تعاد' – every prayer performed with karahah is repeated. This is then qualified by the distinction.
The indefinite in negation includes both types, but the scholars refined it.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu al-Yusr holds that even karahah tahrim does not obligate i'adah, but the majority (including the author) differ.
The text says 'عند غير أبي اليسر' – so the majority favor wajib for tahrim.
5
Apply the distinction
If someone prays with an image on their garment (which is karahah tahrim), they must repeat. If they pray while feeling distracted (tanzih), repetition is recommended but not required.

Avoiding Dislike of Supererogatory Prayer After 'Asr by Alternating Recitation
Ruling on recitation when doubtful about 'Asr time

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi method of alternating recitation in pairs of rak'ahs to avoid the disliked supererogatory prayer after 'Asr.

Core Idea
Alternating recitation in each pair of rak'ahs after 'Asr avoids dislike because the prayer is not intentionally supererogatory.

This lesson examines a nuanced scenario where a person is uncertain whether they have performed the 'Asr prayer and wishes to pray extra rak'ahs without incurring the dislike of supererogatory prayer after 'Asr. The Hanafi jurists devised a method involving alternating recitation in pairs of rak'ahs, which we will analyze step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Problem
Recognize that supererogatory prayer after 'Asr is makruh tahrim in the Hanafi school. The person wants to pray but is uncertain if 'Asr was performed.
2
Understand the Solution: Alternating Recitation
The text proposes praying in pairs (shaf') and reciting in only one rak'ah of each pair. This ensures that if 'Asr was missed, the prayer counts as obligatory; if 'Asr was performed, it becomes supererogatory without the disliked intention.
The key is that recitation is not specified to the first or second rak'ah, so the intention is not purely supererogatory.
3
Analyze the Legal Effect
By leaving recitation in one rak'ah per pair, the prayer is either obligatory or invalid (tamahhada lil-fard aw lil-fasad) but it is not intentionally supererogatory, so the dislike is avoided.
The author notes that the disliked supererogatory prayer is the intentional one; this method avoids that intention.
4
Apply the Alternative: Recite in First Two or All
The text concludes that one can also recite in the first two rak'ahs or in all rak'ahs, providing flexibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإذا ترك القراءة في ركعة من كل شفع تمحض للفرض على تقدير أنه لم يصل أو للفساد على تقدير أنه صلى الفرض أو لا فلم يكن متنفلاً على كل تقدير لكن مقتضاه أن يقول يقرأ في كل شفع من الشفعين في ركعة ويترك القراءة في ركعة من كل شفع من غير تعيين الأولى والثانية للقراءة لأن القراءة في الفرض في ركعتين غير عين كما سبق تقريره. وقد يقال : إن التنفل المكروه هو القصدي وهذا ليس كذلك فلا يكون مكروهاً كما لا يخفى فيقرأ في الأوليين أو في الكل.
And if he leaves recitation in one rak'ah of every pair, then it devotes itself to the obligatory on the assumption that he did not pray, or to invalidity on the assumption that he prayed the obligatory or not, so he is not performing supererogatory prayer in every assumption. But its implication is that he should say: he recites in one rak'ah of each pair of pairs, and leaves recitation in one rak'ah of each pair without specifying the first or second for recitation, because recitation in the obligatory is not specified to two rak'ahs, as previously established. And it may be said that the disliked supererogatory prayer is the intentional one, and this is not like that, so it is not disliked, as is obvious; so he recites in the first two or in all.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage addresses a scenario of doubt about whether the 'Asr prayer has been performed. A person wants to pray supererogatory rak'ahs but knows that supererogatory prayer after 'Asr is disliked (makruh). To avoid this, he can intend a prayer that combines elements of both obligatory and supererogatory, such that in every pair of rak'ahs, he recites in one and leaves recitation in the other. This ensures that if he has already prayed 'Asr, the prayer is supererogatory but not intentionally disliked; if he has not prayed 'Asr, it becomes obligatory. The author notes that this method avoids the specific prohibition of intentional supererogatory prayer in this time. Alternatively, he may recite in the first two rak'ahs or in all rak'ahs.

Key Terms
شفع (shaf'): A pair of rak'ahs in prayer.
تنفل مكروه (tanafful makrūh): Supererogatory prayer that is disliked when performed at certain times, such as after 'Asr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
To avoid the dislike of supererogatory prayer after 'Asr, what does the author suggest doing?
A) Pray with the intention of obligatory only
B) Alternate recitation in pairs of rak'ahs
C) Pray without any recitation
D) Skip supererogatory prayer entirely

Key Takeaway
By alternating recitation in pairs, a prayer after 'Asr can avoid the dislike of supererogatory prayer when the worshiper is uncertain about having performed 'Asr.

When Does One Witness Suffice for Prayer Repetition?
Ruling on accepting testimony regarding completion of prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the number of witnesses required to obligate repeating a prayer when doubting its completion, and distinguish between the rulings for an imam and a non-imam.

Core Idea
For an imam, two just witnesses are needed to obligate repeating; for an ordinary person, one witness suffices.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses when the testimony of witnesses forces a person to repeat their prayer. While a single trustworthy person's report is normally accepted in religious matters, the imam's case is different because his prayer repetition binds the congregation. Thus, two witnesses are required for the imam, similar to legal testimony.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The passage deals with a person who doubts whether he completed his prayer. Two just witnesses inform him he did not complete. What is the ruling?
2
Note the general rule from al-Hawi al-Qudsi
Al-Hawi states that with two witnesses, repetition is obligatory; with one, it is not. But this is contested.
3
Understand the restriction in al-Muhit
The ruling is restricted to the imam because his decision affects others; for a non-imam, one witness suffices.
4
Apply the distinction
For a non-imam, one just person's report is sufficient to obligate repetition; for an imam, two witnesses are required.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الحاوي القدسي : لو شك في إتمام صلاته فأخبره عدلان أنك لا تتم أعاد وبقول الواحد لا تجب الإعادة ا هـ . وفيه بحث لأن خبر الواحد العدل مقبول في الديانات اللهم إلا أن يقال : إن فيه إلزاماً من كل وجه فشابه حقوق العباد وقيده في المحيط بالإمام وعلله بأنها شهادة لأن حكمه يلزم الغير دون المخبر وشهادة الفرد لا تقبل ا هـ . فيفيد أنه لو لم يكن إماماً فقول الواحد مقبول فإطلاق الحاوي ليس بالحاوي.
And in al-Hawi al-Qudsi: If he doubts about the completion of his prayer, and two just men inform him that you did not complete, he repeats, and by the statement of one, i'adah is not obligatory. And there is discussion in it because the report of a single just person is acceptable in religious matters, unless it is said: there is an obligation from every side, so it resembles the rights of people. And in al-Muhit it is restricted to the imam, and he reasoned that it is a testimony because its ruling binds the other without the informer, and the testimony of an individual is not accepted. So it indicates that if he is not an imam, then the statement of a single person is accepted, so the absolute statement of al-Hawi is not comprehensive.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage discusses the evidentiary value of witnesses in matters of prayer completion. According to al-Hawi al-Qudsi, if a person doubts whether he completed his prayer, and two trustworthy witnesses (adlan) inform him that he did not complete, he must repeat the prayer. However, if only one witness informs him, he is not obligated to repeat. The author notes a discussion: normally, the report of a single just person is accepted in religious matters (e.g., reports of hadith). But here, because the ruling imposes an obligation on the person from all sides (i.e., forces a repeat), it resembles legal rights (huquq al-'ibad) where two witnesses are required. Al-Muhit restricts this to the imam, reasoning that it is testimony (shahada) because the ruling binds others. If the person is not an imam, the report of one witness is sufficient. Thus, the absolute statement in al-Hawi is not comprehensive.

Key Terms
عدلان (ʿadlān): Two just witnesses who are morally upright.
شهادة (shahāda): Testimony, which in this context is a legal proof requiring two witnesses for matters that bind others.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Muhit, how many witnesses are needed to obligate the imam to repeat his prayer?
A) One
B) Two
C) Three
D) None

Key Takeaway
The number of witnesses needed to obligate prayer repetition depends on the status of the person: two for an imam, one for a non-imam.

Leaving Recitation in One Rak'ah of a Day and Night's Prayers
Ruling for one who remembers leaving recitation in a rak'ah of a day and night's prayers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a resident who remembers leaving recitation in one rak'ah of the prayers of a day and night, and identify the exception for travelers.

Core Idea
Leaving recitation in one rak'ah only invalidates Fajr and Witr for a resident; a traveler must repeat all.

This passage from al-Hawi clarifies a common point of confusion: if you finish the prayers of a day and night and then realize you omitted recitation in one rak'ah of some prayer, you do not need to redo all of them. The ruling distinguishes between regular prayers and the two special cases of Fajr and Witr, and between residents and travelers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What act is being discussed? (remembering leaving recitation after completing the prayers) What is the general ruling? (only Fajr and Witr need to be made up)
2
Identify the exceptional prayers
Which prayers are invalidated by leaving recitation in one rak'ah? (Fajr and Witr)
This is because in these prayers, recitation is wajib in every rak'ah.
3
Note the condition
What restriction is placed on this ruling? (the person is a resident, not a traveler)
4
Apply the traveler exception
What is the ruling for a traveler? (repeat all prayers of that day and night)
Traveler's prayers are subject to stricter rules.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الحاوي أيضاً: لو تذكر أنه ترك القراءة في ركعة من صلاة يوم وليلة قضى الفجر والوتر ا هـ. ووجهه أن ترك القراءة في ركعة واحدة لا يبطلها في سائر الصلوات إلا الفجر والوتر، وينبغي تقييده بأن لا يكون مسافراً، أما لو كان مسافراً فينبغي أن يعيد صلاة يوم وليلة كما لا يخفى.
And in al-Hawi also: If he remembers that he left recitation in one rak'ah of the prayers of a day and night, he makes up Fajr and Witr. And its reasoning is that leaving recitation in one rak'ah does not invalidate the prayer in other prayers except Fajr and Witr. And it should be restricted to when he is not a traveler; as for if he is a traveler, then he should repeat the prayers of the day and night, as is not hidden.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage gives a ruling for a person who remembers after completing the prayers of a day and night that he forgot to recite (al-Fatihah or a surah) in one rak'ah of some prayer. According to al-Hawi, he only needs to make up Fajr and Witr because these two prayers are invalidated by leaving recitation in any rak'ah; for other prayers, leaving recitation in one rak'ah does not invalidate the entire prayer. However, this ruling applies only if he is a resident (muqim). If he is a traveler, all prayers of that day and night must be repeated because traveler's prayers are subject to different conditions.

Key Terms
قراءة (qirā'a): Recitation of Qur'an in prayer, specifically al-Fatiha and a surah.
وتر (witr): The Witr prayer, which is wajib in the Hanafi school.
قضاء (qaḍā): Making up a missed or invalidated prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
For a resident, only Fajr and Witr require qada if recitation is missed in one rak'ah; for a traveler, all prayers must be repeated.

Ten Forgotten Prostrations: The Precautionary Qada Rule
Ruling for one who remembers leaving ten prostrations over a month

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi precautionary principle (ihtiyat) to determine the number of missed prayers to make up when the number of missed prostrations is known but their distribution is unknown.

Core Idea
Ten forgotten prostrations over a month require ten full days of qada — precaution distributes the doubt.

In this passage from al-Muhit, the Hanafi school addresses a scenario where someone knows they have missed a certain number of prostrations but cannot pinpoint which prayers. The solution applies ihtiyat (precaution) to spread the missed acts across the possible days, leading to a specific number of make-up prayers. Understanding this principle helps resolve similar cases of doubt in prayer obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the doubt and its scope
The person knows he missed ten prostrations but does not know which prayers they were missed from. The doubt is about the identity of the missed prostrations.
2
Apply the precautionary distribution
The ten prostrations are distributed over ten different prayers, one per day, to be on the safe side. This makes it as if one prayer per day was missed.
This is the maximum possible spread to avoid underestimation.
3
Apply the rule for an unknown missed prayer
When a person knows a prayer was missed but not which one, the Hanafi rule is to repeat a full day's prayers. Thus, for each day affected, a full day's prayers must be made up.
A full day's prayers includes all five daily prayers.
4
Calculate the total qada
Since the prostrations are assumed to be spread over ten days, ten full days of prayers must be repeated.
5
Note the ihtiyat justification
This ruling is a precaution to ensure no obligation is left unfulfilled, even though it seems strict.
This principle is common in Hanafi fiqh for resolving doubts in ibadat.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي المحيط : رجل صلى شهراً ثم تذكر أنه ترك عشر سجدات من هذه الصلوات يقضي صلوات عشرة أيام لجواز أنه ترك كل سجدة في يوم اهـ. وتوضيحه أن العشر سجدات تجعل مفرقة على عشر صلوات احتياطاً فصار كأنه ترك صلاة من صلوات كل يوم وإذا ترك صلاة ولم يدر تعينها يقضي صلاة يوم كامل فلزمه قضاء عشرة الأيام.
And in al-Muhit: A man prayed for a month, then remembered that he left ten prostrations from these prayers. He makes up the prayers of ten days, because it is possible that he left each prostration in a different day. And its explanation is that the ten prostrations are distributed over ten prayers as a precaution, so it becomes as if he left one prayer from each day, and if he leaves a prayer and does not know its specific identity, he makes up a full day's prayers, so he is obliged to make up ten days.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage presents a case from al-Muhit: a person prayed for a whole month but later recalls that he missed ten prostrations (sajdas) during that month's prayers. Since he does not know which prayers these prostrations were missed from, as a precaution, he must repeat the prayers of ten full days. This is because the ten prostrations are assumed to be distributed one per day, making it equivalent to having missed one prayer each day. And the rule for a person who knows he missed a prayer but does not know which one is to repeat a whole day's prayers. Thus, ten days' worth of prayers are required.

Key Terms
سجدة (sajda): Prostration in prayer; an essential component of each rak'ah.
احتياط (iḥtiyāṭ): Precautionary measure to ensure fulfillment of obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Ten days
C) One day
D) Twenty days

Key Takeaway
Ten forgotten prostrations over a month require ten full days of qada due to ihtiyat in distributing the doubt.

Tartib of Missed Prayers for a Newly Pubescent Boy
Ruling on a boy who reaches puberty at Fajr time and prays Dhuhr without making up Fajr first

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling from al-Qunyah regarding tartib for a newly pubescent boy and explain the commentator's reservation.

Core Idea
Tartib is waived for a boy who just reached puberty, but the riwayah is contested.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents a specific ruling from al-Qunyah: a boy who reaches puberty at Fajr time, misses Fajr, and then prays Dhuhr while remembering the missed prayer, is not required to observe tartib. However, the commentator Ibn Nujaym expresses doubt about the authenticity of this ruling, noting that after puberty, a person becomes fully responsible. He suggests that an excuse of ignorance due to recent childhood may apply. This lesson unpacks the nuances of the tartib obligation and the conditions under which it can be waived.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
Identify the specific scenario mentioned: a boy reaches puberty at the time of Fajr, misses Fajr, then prays Dhuhr while remembering the missed Fajr.
Note that the passage mentions 'ma‘a tadhakkurihi' – with remembrance, so he is not forgetful.
2
State the Ruling from al-Qunyah
According to al-Qunyah, the Dhuhr prayer is permissible (ja’iz) and tartib is not obligatory to this extent. This is an exception to the general rule that missed prayers must be made up in order.
The phrase 'bi-hadha al-qadr' (to this extent) suggests the exception is limited to this specific scenario.
3
Analyze the Commentator's Critique
Ibn Nujaym questions the authenticity of the ruling, arguing that upon puberty the boy becomes mukallaf (legally responsible) and thus should be bound by tartib. He proposes that the only possible excuse is ignorance due to recent childhood.
This analysis shows the importance of verifying riwayat and understanding the basis of fiqh rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي القنية : صبي بلغ وقت الفجر ولم يصل الفجر وصلى الظهر مع تذكره يجوز ولا يجب الترتيب بهذا القدر ا هـ. وهو إن صح يكون مخصصاً للمتون وفيه نظر عندي لأنه بالبلوغ صار مكلفاً اللهم إلا أن يكون جاهلاً به فيعذر لقرب عهده من زمن الصبا.
And in al-Qunyah: A boy reaches puberty at the time of Fajr and did not pray Fajr, and he prayed Dhuhr with the remembrance (that he missed Fajr), it is permissible and order (tartib) is not obligatory to this extent. And if it is authentic, it is a specification of the texts, but there is consideration in its authenticity in my view, because by reaching puberty he becomes a responsible person (mukallaf), unless he is ignorant of it, then he is excused because of his recent departure from childhood.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage reports a ruling from al-Qunyah: a boy who reaches puberty at the time of Fajr but does not pray Fajr, then later remembers that he missed it while praying Dhuhr, is allowed to pray Dhuhr without first making up Fajr. The usual rule is that missed prayers must be made up in order (tartib), but here it is waived. The author of the commentary (Ibn Nujaym) expresses doubt about the authenticity of this ruling, as upon puberty one becomes fully responsible. He suggests that an excuse of ignorance might apply due to the boy's recent emergence from childhood.

Key Terms
ترتيب (tartīb): Performing missed prayers in the order they were missed.
بالغ (bāligh): A person who has reached puberty and is thus legally responsible for religious obligations.
مكلف (mukallaf): A legally responsible person, bound to fulfill religious duties.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He must repeat Dhuhr after making up Fajr.
B) It is permissible and tartib is not required.
C) He must pray both Fajr and Dhuhr with a specific intention.
D) His Dhuhr prayer is invalid.

Key Takeaway
The obligation of tartib (order) in missed prayers is a general rule, but exceptions exist for reasons such as narrow time, forgetfulness, and, according to some riwayat, recent puberty with ignorance.

Dropping the Order of Missed Prayers in Narrow Time
Ruling on when the order of missed prayers is dropped due to insufficient time

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the order of missed prayers is dropped when time is narrow and apply the Hanafi principle of preferring qat'i over zanni evidence in case of conflict.

Core Idea
When the time for the current prayer is tight, it takes precedence over missed prayers because its obligation is based on the Qur'an (qat'i) while the missed prayer's obligation is based on a solitary hadith (zanni).

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq explains an important exception to the general rule that missed prayers must be made up in order. When the time for the current obligatory prayer is so short that performing a missed prayer would cause the current prayer to be missed, the obligation of order (tartib) drops. The reasoning is based on the strength of evidence: the current prayer's obligation is established by the Qur'an (definitive), while the missed prayer's obligation is established by a solitary hadith (presumptive). In case of conflict, the stronger evidence prevails.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule of tartib
Recall that the Hanafi school generally requires missed prayers to be made up in order (tartib). This passage introduces an exception.
Tartib is wajib when there is no narrow time.
2
Define the exception: narrow time (ḍīq al-waqt)
Understand that 'narrow time' means the remaining time for the current prayer is just enough to perform it; performing a missed prayer would cause the current prayer to be missed.
If there is sufficient time, tartib remains wajib.
3
Analyze the evidence for each obligation
The current prayer's obligation is based on the Qur'an (qat'i al-thubut). The missed prayer's obligation is based on a solitary hadith (zanni al-thubut).
The hadith cited: 'Whoever sleeps through a prayer or forgets it, let him pray it when he remembers it.'
4
Apply the principle of preference
When there is a conflict, the stronger evidence (qat'i) overrides the weaker (zanni). Therefore, the current prayer takes precedence.
This is a usul principle: al-thabit bi al-qat'i la yuzaham bi al-zanni.
5
Conclude the ruling
The order (tartib) is dropped; one must pray the current prayer first and then make up the missed one later.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ويسقط بضيق الوقت أي يسقط الترتيب المستحق بضيق وقت المكتوبة لأنه وقت للوقتية بالكتاب ووقت للفائتة بخبر الواحد وهو قوله عليه الصلاة والسلام «من نام عن صلاة أو نسيها فليصلها إذا ذكرها» فإنه يقتضي وجوب القضاء متى ذكرها لكن التعارض مع الوقت الحاضر يوجب تقديم الوقت الحاضر لكونه أقوى.
His statement: (And it drops due to narrowness of time) i.e., the required order drops due to the narrowness of the time of the current obligatory prayer, because the time is for the current prayer by the Book (Qur'an) and for the missed prayer by a solitary report, and that is his saying (peace be upon him): 'Whoever sleeps through a prayer or forgets it, let him pray it when he remembers it.' This necessitates the obligation of qada whenever he remembers it, but the conflict with the present time requires giving priority to the present time because it is stronger.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling that the obligatory order (tartib) between missed prayers and the current prayer is dropped when the time for the current prayer is very narrow. The evidence for the current prayer's obligation is the Qur'an (e.g., 'Establish prayer at the time'), which is qat'i al-thubut (definitive in transmission), while the obligation to make up a missed prayer is based on a solitary hadith (khabar wahid), which is zanni. When there is a conflict, the stronger evidence prevails, so the current prayer takes precedence. Therefore, if performing a missed prayer would cause the current prayer to be missed, one should pray the current prayer first and make up the missed one later.

Key Terms
ضيق الوقت (ḍīq al-waqt): The remaining time for the current prayer is so short that performing a missed prayer would cause the current prayer to be missed.
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wāḥid): A solitary hadith, which gives zanni knowledge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Pray the missed prayer first, then the current
B) Pray the current prayer first, then make up the missed
C) Pray both together in one setting
D) The ruling depends on the school

Key Takeaway
The order of missed prayers is dropped when time for the current prayer is narrow because the current prayer's obligation is based on a stronger source (Qur'an) than the missed prayer's (solitary hadith).

Ruling on Recitation in the First Two Rak'ahs When Making up Missed Prayers
Explains the ruling on recitation when combining qada' and current prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on recitation when combining qada' prayer with the current obligatory prayer and identify the conditions that affect its validity.

Core Idea
Reciting in the first two rak'ahs is obligatory when making up a missed prayer; omission invalidates the intention.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on recitation when one intends to perform a missed (qada') prayer during the time of the current obligatory prayer. The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies that the first two rak'ahs are considered part of the missed prayer, making recitation obligatory. Understanding this ruling helps avoid invalidating the prayer due to incorrect intention or omission.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Context
Recognize that the scenario involves combining a missed prayer (qada') with the current obligatory prayer during its time.
The intention must be for the missed prayer, not the current one.
2
Determine the Ruling on Recitation
State that recitation in the first two rak'ahs is obligatory (wajib) for the missed prayer.
This follows the general rule for obligatory prayers: recitation is wajib in the first two rak'ahs.
3
Analyze the Condition of Intention
Consider the two assumptions: whether the person already prayed the current obligatory prayer or not. The ruling changes accordingly.
If he has not prayed the current prayer, the first two rak'ahs become for the missed prayer; if he has, the combination may be invalid.
4
Examine the Consequence of Omitting Recitation
If he omits recitation in one rak'ah of each pair, the prayer either becomes purely for the obligatory (if he hadn't prayed it) or invalid (if he had).
Omission of wajib can lead to invalidity or change of intention.
5
Clarify the Status of Disliked Voluntary
The text notes that this combination is not considered a disliked voluntary act because the intention is for the missed prayer, not for a voluntary prayer.
Disliked voluntary (makruh tatawwu') applies to intentional voluntary acts, not to qada'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة باب قضاء الفوائت في الأوليين كان متنفلاً بالأربع أو بالأوليين على تقدير أنه صلى الفرض أو لا. وإذا ترك القراءة في ركعة من كل شفع تمحض للفرض على تقدير أنه لم يصل أو للفساد على تقدير أنه صلى الفرض أو لا فلم يكن متنفلاً على كل تقدير لكن مقتضاه أن يقول يقرأ في كل شفع من الشفعين في ركعة ويترك القراءة في ركعة من كل شفع من غير تعيين الأولى والثانية للقراءة لأن القراءة في الفرض في ركعتين غير عين كما سبق تقريره. وقد يقال : إن التنفل المكروه هو القصدي وهذا ليس كذلك فلا يكون مكروهاً كما لا يخفى فيقرأ في الأوليين أو في الكل.
Book of Prayer, Chapter on Making up Missed Prayers. In the first two [rak'ahs], he would be performing voluntary prayer with four or with the first two, on the assumption that he prayed the obligatory [prayer] or not. And if he omits recitation in one rak'ah of every pair, it becomes purely for the obligatory on the assumption that he did not pray, or for invalidity on the assumption that he prayed the obligatory or not, so he would not be performing voluntary in every assumption. But its requirement is that he should say: he recites in each pair of the two pairs in one rak'ah and omits recitation in one rak'ah of each pair without specifying the first or second for recitation, because recitation in the obligatory is in two rak'ahs not specified, as previously established. And it may be said: the disliked voluntary is the intentional one, and this is not like that, so it is not disliked, as is not hidden, so he recites in the first two or in all.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on recitation when one intends to make up a missed prayer in the time of the current obligatory prayer. The author explains that if one intends the missed prayer, the first two rak'ahs are considered part of the missed prayer, so recitation is obligatory in them. If one omits recitation in one rak'ah of each pair, it becomes purely for the obligatory prayer on the assumption that he did not pray the missed one, or invalid if he did pray it. The author clarifies that the disliked voluntary (tatawwu' makruh) is one intentionally performed, not this case, so it is not disliked. The ruling is that one should recite in the first two rak'ahs or in all.

Key Terms
الشفع (al-shaf'): A pair of rak'ahs in prayer.
التنفل (al-tatawwu'): Voluntary prayer performed in addition to obligatory prayers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the combination of a missed (qada') prayer with the current obligatory prayer, what is the ruling on recitation in the first two rak'ahs?
A) Recitation is not required
B) Recitation is obligatory
C) Recitation is only sunnah
D) Recitation is forbidden

Key Takeaway
Recitation in the first two rak'ahs is wajib when performing qada' during another prayer; omitting it can invalidate the prayer or nullify the qada' intention.

intermediate

Rulings from al-Hawi al-Qudsi on Prayer Completion and Recitation Omission
Cites rulings from al-Hawi al-Qudsi on testimony for incomplete prayer and omitting recitation in one rak'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which testimony of just men obligates repetition of prayer and identify which prayers require makeup after omitting recitation in one rak'ah, including exceptions for the imam and traveler.

Core Idea
Two just witnesses obligate prayer repetition; a single witness is insufficient. Omitting recitation in one rak'ah only requires Fajr and Witr makeup for residents, but all prayers for travelers.

This passage from al-Hawi al-Qudsi provides two specific rulings related to prayer. The first addresses when a person doubts whether he completed his prayer and is informed by just witnesses. The second addresses a person who recalls omitting recitation in one rak'ah of his daily prayers. Understanding these rulings helps clarify the role of testimony in prayer validity and the consequences of missing recitation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
The passage presents two separate rulings. First, regarding doubt in completing prayer based on testimony. Second, regarding omitting recitation in one rak'ah. Note that each has its own conditions.
2
Analyze the witness condition
For the first ruling, the number and quality of witnesses matter. Two just witnesses obligate repetition; one does not. Also note that according to al-Muhit, this ruling applies specifically to an imam, not a general individual.
This is an intra-Hanafi refinement.
3
Examine the omission ruling
For the second ruling, if a person recalls omitting recitation in one rak'ah of his day and night prayers, he must make up only Fajr and Witr, not the other prayers. This is because omitting recitation in one rak'ah does not invalidate other prayers except these two.
The reasoning is that Fajr and Witr have special status.
4
Apply the traveler exception
The ruling for omission is for a resident. If the person is a traveler, he must repeat the entire prayer of a day and night, as his prayers are shortened and the omission affects them differently.
The text says 'as is not hidden'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الحاوي القدسي : لو شك في إتمام صلاته فأخبره عدلان أنك لا تتم أعاد وبقول الواحد لا تجب الإعادة ا هـ . وفيه بحث لأن خبر الواحد العدل مقبول في الديانات اللهم إلا أن يقال : إن فيه إلزاماً من كل وجه فشابه حقوق العباد وقيده في المحيط بالإمام وعلله بأنها شهادة لأن حكمه يلزم الغير دون المخبر وشهادة الفرد لا تقبل ا هـ . فيفيد أنه لو لم يكن إماماً فقول الواحد مقبول فإطلاق الحاوي ليس بالحاوي. وفي الحاوي أيضاً: لو تذكر أنه ترك القراءة في ركعة من صلاة يوم وليلة قضى الفجر والوتر ا هـ. ووجهه أن ترك القراءة في ركعة واحدة لا يبطلها في سائر الصلوات إلا الفجر والوتر، وينبغي تقييده بأن لا يكون مسافراً، أما لو كان مسافراً فينبغي أن يعيد صلاة يوم وليلة كما لا يخفى.
And in al-Hawi al-Qudsi: If he doubts about completing his prayer, and two just men inform him that you did not complete it, he repeats it. And by the statement of one, repetition is not obligatory. End. And there is discussion in it because the statement of one just person is accepted in religious matters, unless it is said that it commits from every aspect, so it resembles the rights of servants. And in al-Muhit, he restricted it to the imam and reasoned that it is testimony because its ruling obligates others, not the informant, and the testimony of one person is not accepted. End. So it follows that if he is not an imam, the statement of one is accepted, so the absolute statement of al-Hawi is not accurate. And in al-Hawi also: If he recalls that he omitted recitation in one rak'ah of a day and night's prayer, he makes up Fajr and Witr. End. And its reasoning is that omitting recitation in one rak'ah does not invalidate it in other prayers except Fajr and Witr, and it should be restricted that he is not a traveler; as for if he is a traveler, then he should repeat the prayer of a day and night, as is not hidden.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage presents two rulings from al-Hawi al-Qudsi. The first deals with a person who doubts whether he completed his prayer. If two just men inform him that he did not complete it, he must repeat the prayer. However, the statement of one just man is not sufficient to obligate repetition. The author notes that there is discussion, as the testimony of a single just person is normally accepted in religious matters, but here it is like a testimony that obligates others, so only two witnesses are accepted. Al-Muhit restricts this to the imam, because his ruling affects others. For a non-imam, a single witness suffices. The second ruling: if a person recalls that he omitted recitation in one rak'ah of the entire day and night's prayers, he needs to make up only Fajr and Witr, because omitting recitation in one rak'ah does not invalidate other prayers except these two. However, if he is a traveler, he should repeat the entire day and night's prayers.

Key Terms
العدل (al-'adl): A just person whose testimony is acceptable in legal matters.
الشهادة (al-shahāda): Testimony given in a legal context, especially regarding the imam's prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Hawi al-Qudsi, if a person doubts completing his prayer and two just men inform him he did not complete, what must he do?
A) Ignore them
B) Repeat the prayer
C) Make up only the missing parts
D) Rely on his own doubt

Key Takeaway
In prayer, two just witnesses are required to obligate repetition for an imam, and omission of recitation in one rak'ah only necessitates makeup of Fajr and Witr for residents, but all prayers for travelers.

Tartib for a Boy New to Puberty
Cites a ruling from al-Qunyah and provides critical commentary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tartib for a boy who reaches puberty at Fajr time and misses Fajr, and identify the condition under which tartib is not required.

Core Idea
A boy newly reached puberty is excused from ordering missed prayers due to ignorance.

The passage from al-Qunyah presents an exceptional case to the general rule of tartib. The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, Ibn Nujaym, discusses its authenticity and provides a rationale based on the boy's recent childhood and potential ignorance. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its conditions, helping you understand when tartib may be waived.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act: a boy reaches puberty at Fajr time, misses Fajr, then prays Dhuhr while remembering the missed Fajr. According to al-Qunyah, his Dhuhr is valid and tartib (order) is not obligatory.
This is an exception to the general Hanafi rule that tartib is wajib when remembering missed prayers.
2
Locate the general principle
The general principle: in the Hanafi school, tartib between missed and current prayers is obligatory (wajib) unless the time is narrow or one is forgetful. The 'primary texts' mentioned refer to this rule.
The ruling from al-Qunyah seems to contradict this, so it would be a specification (takhsis).
3
Identify the exception and its condition
The exception applies only if the boy is ignorant of the obligation to make up the missed prayer in order. This ignorance is excused because he has just left childhood (qurb 'ahdihi min zaman al-siba).
Ignorance here is not willful; it stems from being new to legal responsibility.
4
Analyze the author's doubt
Ibn Nujaym questions the authenticity of this ruling from al-Qunyah. He argues that upon puberty, the person becomes fully responsible (mukallaf), so tartib should be obligatory. He only accepts the exception if the boy is genuinely ignorant.
This shows the cautious approach of later Hanafi scholars in weighing transmitted rulings against established principles.
5
Determine the practical consequence
If the boy is aware of the obligation (i.e., not ignorant), then tartib is obligatory and he must make up Fajr before Dhuhr. If he is ignorant, his Dhuhr is valid without tartib.
The ruling hinges on the boy's knowledge, which is a subjective condition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي القنية : صبي بلغ وقت الفجر ولم يصل الفجر وصلى الظهر مع تذكره يجوز ولا يجب الترتيب بهذا القدر ا هـ. وهو إن صح يكون مخصصاً للمتون وفي صحته نظر عندي لأنه بالبلوغ صار مكلفاً اللهم إلا أن يكون جاهلاً به فيعذر لقرب عهده من زمن الصبا.
And in al-Qunyah: A boy who reached puberty at Fajr time and did not pray Fajr, and prayed Dhuhr while remembering [the missed Fajr], it is permissible, and tartib (order) is not obligatory to this extent. End. And if it is authentic, it would be specifying the [primary] texts, but its authenticity is questionable in my view, because upon puberty he becomes legally responsible, unless he was ignorant of it, so he is excused due to his recent departure from the time of childhood.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This ruling from al-Qunyah addresses a boy who reaches puberty right at Fajr time and does not pray Fajr, then when Dhuhr time comes, he prays Dhuhr while remembering that he missed Fajr. The ruling says it is permissible and that the order (tartib) between missed and current prayers is not obligatory in this case. The author (Ibn Nujaym) comments that if this ruling is authentic, it would specialize the general texts that require tartib. However, he doubts its authenticity because after puberty, the person is fully responsible. The exception might be if he is ignorant, as he is new to maturity.

Key Terms
البلوغ (al-bulūgh): The attainment of puberty, marking legal responsibility (taklif).
الترتيب (al-tartīb): The order in which missed prayers must be made up relative to current prayers.
الجهل (al-jahl): Ignorance of the ruling, which can excuse in certain cases.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Qunyah, if a boy reaches puberty at Fajr time and misses Fajr but then prays Dhuhr while remembering the missed Fajr, what is the ruling?
A) He must first make up Fajr
B) His Dhuhr is valid and tartib is not required
C) He must repeat both prayers
D) He is sinful for not making up Fajr first

Key Takeaway
Tartib is generally wajib, but a boy newly reached puberty is excused if ignorant of the obligation due to his recent childhood.

The Definition of Tight Time in the Order of Missed Prayers: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Discussion of tartīb between fā'itah and hādirah when time is short

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the two Hanafi positions on tight time (ḍīq al-waqt) regarding the order of missed prayers, and state the muftā bihi position with its supporting evidence.

Core Idea
When time is short, the order between missed and current prayers depends on whether 'tight time' means original or preferred time.

The obligation to make up missed prayers immediately upon remembrance is established by a well-known hadith. However, when the current prayer's time is limited, a dispute arises within the Hanafi school: should one consider the original time (aṣl al-waqt) or the preferred time (al-waqt al-mustahab) when defining tightness? This lesson will dissect the two positions, their proofs, and the final tarjīh that settles the matter for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Establish the Ruling on Order
State the basic rule: tartīb (order) is wājib between fā'itah and hādirah when the missed prayer is remembered and there is sufficient time. Identify the primary proof (the hadith).
The hadith 'صلاة أو نسيها فليصلها إذا ذكرها' is the foundation.
2
Define Tight Time Objectively
Understand that tightness is measured by actual remaining time, not the person's assumption. If the time can accommodate both prayers, order is required. If not, pray the current prayer first (though it is valid but sinful).
The text gives examples: mistaken assumption invalidates the prayer; prolonging recitation that causes tightness invalidates it.
3
Identify the Two Interpretations of Tight Time
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf consider the original time (aṣl al-waqt) – the full span of the current prayer. Muhammad considers the preferred time (al-waqt al-mustahab) – e.g., for 'Asr before the sun changes colour.
The practical difference appears when praying Zuhr first would cause 'Asr to fall after the sun changes but before sunset.
4
Trace the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Follow the arguments: Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf rely on the general obligation and the principle that Qur'anic timings cannot be overridden by a single-narrator hadith. Muhammad relies on a Companion practice (al-Muntaqa) and the priority of the current prayer when its best time is slipping.
Note that the disagreement is ultimately over which transmission is authoritative.
5
Evaluate the Tarjīh and Identify the Muftā Bihi
The author of al-Bahr al-Rā'iq gives six reasons for preferring original time, including agreement with the matn, majority of shaykhs, Qadi Khan's verification, and logical consistency. Conclude: the muftā bihi is original time.
Forgetfulness (nisyān) is a separate ground for dropping order – a 'heavenly excuse'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

لزوم تفويت الوقتية وهو لا يعدم المشروعية واختلف في المراد بالنهي هنا فقيل نهى الشارح لأن الأمر بالشيء نهي عن ضده، وقيل نهي الإجماع لإجماعهم على أنه لا يقدم الفائتة وهو الأصح. في المعراج . وإنما قلنا صحيحة ولم نقل جائزة لأن هذا الفعل حرام كما لو اشتغل بالنافلة عند ضيق الوقت يحكم بصحتها مع الإثم، وتفسير ضيق الوقت أن يكون الباقي منه لا يسعهما معاً عند الشروع في نفس الأمر لا بحسب ظنه حتى لو ظن ضيقه الشروع فشرع في الوقتية وأطال القراءة فلما فرغ ضاق الوقت بطل ما أداه . واختلفوا فيما إذا كان الباقي منه يسع بعض الفوائت فقط، فظاهر كلامهم ترجيح أنه لا تجوز الوقتية ما لم يقض ذلك البعض. وفي المجتبى خلافه فإنه قال : ولو فاتته أربع والوقت لا يسع إلا الفائتتين والوقتية فالأص لأصح أنه تجوز الوقتية ا وظاهر كلام المصنف اعتبار أصل الوقت في الضيق لا الوقت المستحب، ولم يذكر في ظاهر الرواية ولذا وقع يلزمه مراعاة الترتيب ها هنا عند علمائنا الثلاثة، وصحح في المحيط الثاني فقال : والأصح أنه يسقط الترتيب لما فيه من تغيير حكم الكتاب وهو نقصان الوقتية بخبر الواحد وذلك لا يجوز ا هـ . فعلى هذا المراد يسقط بضيق الوقت المستحب ورجحه الظهيرية بما في المنتقى من أنه إذا افتتح العصر في أول وقتها وهو ناس للظهر ثم احمرت الشمس ثم ذكر الظهر مضى في العصر قال : فهذا نص على أن العبرة للوقت المستحب ا فحينئذ انقطع اختلاف المشايخ لأن المسألة حيث لم تذكر في ظاهر الرواية وثبتت في رواية أخرى تعين المصير إليها. وفي المجتبي : إن لم يمكنه أداء الوقتية إلا مع التخفيف في قصر القراءة والأفعال فيرتب ويقتصر على أقل ما تجوز به الصلاة. قوله : (والنسيان أي ويسقط الترتيب بالنسيان وهو عدم تذكر الشيء وقت حاجته وهو عذر سماوي مسقط للتكليف لأنه ليس في وسعه ولأن الوقت وقت للفائتة بالتذكر وما لم يتذكر لا يكون وقتاً لها. ومما ألحق بالنسيان الظن فليس مسقطاً رابعاً كما قد يتوهم فهو قسمان: معتبر وغير معتبر واختلفت عباراتهم فيه ففي كشف الأسرار شرح أصول فخر الإسلام أن الظن إنما يكون معتبراً إذاكان الرجل مجتهداً قد ظهر عنده أن مراعاة الترتيب وقد ذكرناه . وإنما أعاده . المسألة ووضع في العصر لمعرفة آخر الوقت، فعندنا آخر وقت العصر في حكم الترتيب غروب الشمس وفي حكم جواز تأخير العصر تغير الشمس، وعلى قول الحسن آخر وقت العصر عند تغيب الشمس، فعلى مذهبه إذا كان يتمكن من أداء الصلاتين قبل تغير الشمس يلزمه الترتيب وإلا فلا، وعندنا إذا كان يتمكن من أداء الظهر قبل تغير الشمس ويقع كل العصر أو بعضه بعد تغير الشمس يلزمه الترتيب، وإن كان يتمكن من أداء الصلاتين قبل غروب الشمس لكن لا يتمكن من أن يفرغ من الظهر قبل تغير الشمس لا يلزمه الترتيب لأن أداء شيء من الظهر لا يجوز بعد التغيير، وما بعد تغير الشمس ليس وقتاً لأداء شيء من الصلوات إلا عصر يومه ا هـ. قوله : ( فحينئذ انقطع اختلاف المشايخ الخ) أنت خبير بأن ما . ا مر عن الطحاوي صريح في أن المسألة ليست مبنية على اختلاف المشايخ بل هي مبنية على اختلاف الرواية عن علمائنا الثلاثة، بل مقتضى ما مر عن المبسوط أنه لا خلاف فيها فيتعين ترجيح كون المعتبر أصل الوقت لوجوه : الأول كونه موافقاً لإطلاق المتون وإذا اختلف التصحيح فالعمل بما وافق المتون أولى كما سيذكره المؤلف قبيل قوله «ولم تعد بعودها إلى القلة». الثاني كونه قول أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف والآخر قول محمد بل الظاهر أنه رواية عن محمد بدليل ما في المبسوط من أن الأول قول علمائنا الثلاثة أي وهم أبو حنيفة وأبو يوسف ومحمد. ثم رأيت التصريح بأنه رواية عن محمد في شرح المنية الكبير وجزم بأن المراد أصل الوقت لا الوقت المستحب الثالث كونه قد صححه قاضيخان وهو من أجل من يعتمد على تصحيحه كما ذكره العلامة قاسم لأنه فقيه النفس الرابع كون أكثر المشايخ عليه كما تقدم عن المبسوط، وإذا اختلف في مسألة فالعمل بما قاله الأكثر أولى كما ذكره البيري في حاشية الأشباه الخامس أن تصحيح سقوط الترتيب فيما إذا لزم وقوع العصر في وقت ناقص لا يلزمه تصحيح كون المراد الوقت المستحب في سائر الأوقات إذ يبعد غاية البعد أن يقال بسقوط الترتيب إذا فاته صلوات ولزم من قضائها تأخير ظهر الشتاء أو تأخير المغرب عن أول الوقت مع أنه لو تذكر الفائتة والخطيب يخطب يقوم ويقضيها وإن فاته الاستماع الواجب فكيف لا يقضيها إذا لزم فوات الوقت المستحب؟ السادس أن ما ذكره من
Book of Prayer, Chapter on Making Up Missed Prayers. 145. Likewise. 'He who forgot a prayer, let him pray it when he remembers.' (1) The Book (Quran) is given precedence over the single-narrator hadith. So if one offers the missed prayer in this situation and there is no time of dislike, it is valid because the prohibition is for a reason outside it, which is the necessary loss of the current prayer's timeliness, and it does not nullify legal validity. They differed concerning the intended meaning of the prohibition here: it is said the commentator prohibited because commanding something prohibits its opposite; it is said the prohibition is by consensus, for they all agree that one should not offer the current prayer (before the missed one). That is the most correct. In al-Mi'raj. We only said it is valid, not permissible, because this act is unlawful, just as if one busies himself with a supererogatory prayer when time is tight, one rules it valid while sinful. The definition of tightness of time is that the remaining time does not accommodate both together at the actual start, not according to one's assumption. So if he assumed tightness and prayed the current prayer, then after finishing it became apparent there was leeway, what he performed is void. And in al-Mujtaba: Whoever has the 'Isha' prayer due and assumes the time of Fajr is tight, and prays it while there is leeway, he repeats it until sunrise, and his obligatory prayer is what is near sunrise, and what is before it is supererogatory. If there was leeway at the start and he began the current prayer and prolonged the recitation, then when he finished the time became tight, what he performed is void. They differed concerning when the remaining time only accommodates some of the missed prayers. The apparent meaning of their words is a preference that the current prayer is not permissible until he makes up that part. In al-Mujtaba there is the opposite: he said if four prayers are missed and the time only accommodates two missed prayers and the current prayer, the correct opinion is that the current prayer is permissible. The apparent meaning of the author's words is considering the original time in tightness, not the preferred time. And it was not mentioned in the apparent transmission (zahir al-riwaya), hence disagreement among the shaykhs. Al-Tahawi attributed the first view to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and the second to Muhammad, as in al-Dhakhira. Its fruit appears if one remembers at the time of 'Asr that he did not pray Zuhr, and knows that if he busies himself with Zuhr it will occur before the sun's change, and 'Asr or part of it will occur after it. According to the first, he prays Zuhr then 'Asr; according to the second, he prays 'Asr then Zuhr after sunset. Qadi Khan chose the first in his commentary on al-Jami' al-Saghir and stated it in the form 'according to us'. In al-Mabsut: Most of our shaykhs affirm that observing the order is necessary here according to our three imams. But al-Muhit al-Thani corrected saying: The most correct is that the order falls because it would change the ruling of the Book, i.e., diminishing the timeliness of the current prayer by a single-narrator hadith, and that is not permissible. So according to this, the meaning is order falls due to tightness of the preferred time. Al-Zahiriyya preferred it based on al-Muntaqa: if one begins 'Asr at its first time while forgetful of Zuhr, then the sun reddened, then he remembered Zuhr, he continues in 'Asr. He said: This is a clear text that consideration is for the preferred time. Therefore, the disagreement of the shaykhs ended, because the issue was not mentioned in the apparent transmission but was established in another transmission, so one must adopt it. In al-Mujtaba: If he cannot perform the current prayer except with shortening of recitation and actions, then he observes order and restricts to the minimum that suffices for prayer. His saying: 'And forgetfulness' — that is, order falls due to forgetfulness, which is not remembering the thing at the time of need. It is a heavenly excuse that removes obligation because it is not within his capacity, and because time is time for the missed prayer only by remembering, and as long as he does not remember, it is not time for it. Included with forgetfulness is suspicion, but it is not a fourth faller as might be imagined; it is of two kinds: valid and invalid. Their expressions differ. In Kashf al-Asrar, commentary on Usul Fakhr al-Islam: Suspicion is only valid if the person is a mujtahid to whom it has become apparent that observing the order... And we have mentioned it. He only repeated it. The issue and placing it in 'Asr to know the end of time. According to us, the end of 'Asr time in the ruling of order is sunset, and in the ruling of permissibility of delaying 'Asr is the sun's change. According to the saying of al-Hasan, the end of 'Asr time is at sunset. According to his madhhab, if he is able to perform both prayers before the sun's change, order is necessary; otherwise not. According to us, if he is able to perform Zuhr before the sun's change and the whole of 'Asr or part of it occurs after the sun's change, order is necessary. If he is able to perform both prayers before sunset but cannot finish Zuhr before the sun's change, order is not necessary, because performing any part of Zuhr after the sun's change is not permissible, and what is after the sun's change is not time for performing any prayer except the 'Asr of that day. His saying: 'Therefore, the disagreement of the shaykhs ended, etc.' You are aware that what passed from al-Tahawi is explicit that the issue is not based on disagreement of shaykhs but is based on difference in transmission from our three imams. Rather, the implication of what passed from al-Mabsut is that there is no disagreement, so one must prefer considering the original time for several reasons: First, it agrees with the absolute wording of the matns, and when verification differs, acting according to what agrees with the matns is preferable, as the author will mention before his saying 'and she does not return by her return to the small number'. Second, it is the saying of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and the other is the saying of Muhammad, indeed it is apparent that it is a transmission from Muhammad, evidenced by what is in al-Mabsut that the first is the saying of our three imams — i.e., they are Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad. Then I saw explicit statement that it is a transmission from Muhammad in Sharh al-Munyah al-Kabir, and it is decided that the intended meaning is the original time, not the preferred time. Third, Qadi Khan verified it, and he is among the greatest whose verification is relied upon, as stated by Allamah Qasim because he is intuitive. Fourth, most of the shaykhs are upon it, as mentioned from al-Mabsut. Fifth, that verifying the falling of order when it necessitates 'Asr occurring in an incomplete time does not necessitate verifying that the intended meaning is the preferred time in all times, for it is extremely farfetched to say that order falls if he missed prayers and making them up necessitates delaying the winter Zuhr or delaying Maghrib from its first time, whereas if he remembered the missed prayer while the khatib was delivering the sermon, he would stand and make it up even if he missed the obligatory listening. So how does he not make it up if it necessitates losing the preferred time? Sixth: that what he mentioned of
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion of the chapter on making up missed prayers (qadā' al-fawā'it). The author begins by citing the well-known hadith, 'Whoever forgets a prayer or neglects it, let him pray it when he remembers.' This hadith establishes the obligation to make up missed prayers immediately upon recollection. The core issue addressed here is the order (tartīb) between missed (fā'itah) and current (hādirah) prayers when time is limited. The author clarifies that if one prays the current prayer first in a situation where the remaining time is insufficient for both, the prayer is valid (ṣaḥīḥah) but sinful (ḥarām). This distinction is important: validity does not imply permissibility. The definition of 'tight time' (ḍīq al-waqt) is objective: the actual remaining time cannot accommodate both prayers, not merely the person's assumption. If one assumes tightness but there is actually leeway, the current prayer is invalid. Similarly, if one starts with leeway but prolongs the prayer and the time becomes tight at the end, it is invalid. An intra-Hanafi dispute arises: When only part of the missed prayer can be made up before the current prayer's time ends, some scholars (including Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that one must still make up that part first; Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that the current prayer can be prayed first. The practical consequence appears in the 'Asr example: if one remembers missed Zuhr during 'Asr time, and praying Zuhr first would cause part of 'Asr to fall after the sun's change (the end of preferred time), then according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, one prays Zuhr then 'Asr; according to Muhammad, one prays 'Asr first and delays Zuhr. The passage then discusses forgetfulness (nisyān) as a cause for the order to fall: since the time for the missed prayer only becomes relevant upon remembering, forgetfulness is a valid excuse. Suspicion (ẓann) is not a separate category but is evaluated case by case. The author finally presents a strong tarjīḥ (preference) for the view that the original time (aṣl al-waqt), not the preferred time (al-waqt al-mustahab), is considered in defining tightness. Six reasons are given: (1) agreement with the absolute wording of the matn; (2) it is the position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (and even Muhammad according to one transmission); (3) Qadi Khan's verification; (4) majority of shaykhs; (5) logical consistency—if order falls merely due to losing preferred time, it would lead to absurdities like not making up prayers even when listening to the sermon; (6) textual support from al-Muntaqa.

Key Terms
الفائتة (al-fā'itah): A prayer that was missed (not performed in its prescribed time) and is now being made up.
الحاضرة (al-hādirah): The current prayer that is due at the present time.
الترتيب (al-tartīb): The obligation to perform missed prayers in their original chronological order before the current prayer, when the missed prayer is few and remembered.
ضيق الوقت (ḍīq al-waqt): The condition where the remaining time of the current prayer cannot accommodate both the missed prayer(s) and the current prayer.
الوقت المستحب (al-waqt al-mustahab): The best or preferred time for a prayer, e.g., for 'Asr before the sun changes (yellows).
النسيان (al-nisyān): Forgetfulness of the missed prayer; it is a valid excuse that removes the obligation of tartīb.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position (muftā bihi) in the Hanafi school, what is considered when defining 'tight time' (ḍīq al-waqt) that may allow offering the current prayer before the missed one?
A) The preferred time (al-waqt al-mustahab)
B) The original time (aṣl al-waqt) of the current prayer
C) The time until sunrise
D) The time until the sun changes color

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that tight time for the order of prayers is defined by the original time (aṣl al-waqt), not the preferred time, meaning that the order must be observed unless the entire time for the current prayer would be missed.

Salah — Prayer
