قوله (وصيرورتها ستاً) أي ويسقط الترتيب بصيرورة الفوائت ست صلوات لدخولها في حد الكثرة المفضية للحرج لو قلنا بـ ا بوجوبه والكثرة بالدخول فيجد التكرار وهو أن تكون الفوائت ستاً وهو الصحيح، وبه اندفع ما روي محمد أن المعتبر دخول السادسة، واندفع ما في السراج الوهاج وغاية البيان وكثير أن المعتبر دخول وقت السابعة لتصير الفوائت ستاً إذ لا يتوقف صيرورتها ستاً على دخول السابعة كما لو ترك صلاة يوم كامل وفجر اليوم الثاني فإن الفوائت صارت ستة بطلوع الشمس في اليوم الثاني ولم يدخل وقت السابعة، وقد يقال لما كان فائدة السقوط صحة الوقتية وهي لا تكون إلا بدخول وقت السابعة اعتبر وقت السابعة. وجوابه أن فائدة السقوط لم تنحصر فيما ذكر لأنه بدخول وقت السابعة لا يجب عليه الترتيب فيما بين الفوائت أيضاً كما سيأتي وعبارة المصنف أولى من عبارة الهداية والقدوري حيث قالا : إلا أن نزيد الفوائت على ست صلوات استثناء من قوله رتبها في القضاء لما يلزم من ظاهرها من كون الفوائت سبعاً على ما في فتح القدير، أو تسعاً على ما في النهاية. وإن أجاب عنه في غاية البيان بأن المراد بالفوائت الأوقات مجازاً للاشتباه مع ما قدمناه من عدم اشتراط دخول وقت السابعة. وصرح في المحيط بأن ظاهر الرواية أن الترتيب يسقط بصيرورة الفوائت ستاً موفقاً لما في المختصر
وصححه في الكافي، وبه اندفع ما صححه الشارح الزيعلي من أن المعتبر في سقوط الترتيب أن تبلغ الأقات المتخللة منذ فاتته ستة أوقات وإن أدى ما بعدها في أوقاتها، ولهذا ذكر في الفتاوى الظهيرية : لو تذكر فائتة بعد شهر لا تجوز الوقتية مع تذكر الفائتة إلا إذا كانت الفوائت ستاً. وقال الصدر الشهيد حسام الدين في واقعاته : إنه يجوز أهـ. وفي التجنيس : إن الجواز مختار الطحاوي والفقيه أبي الليث و به نأخذ لأن المتخلل بينهما أكثر من ست صلوات .اهـ. وفي الولواجيية : وهو المختار عند المشايخ وهو موافق لتصحيح الشارح . وحاصله أنهم اختلفوا هل المعتبر صيرورة الفوائت ستاً في نفسها لو كانت متفرقة أو كون الأوقات المتخللة ستاً، وثمرته تظهر فيما ذكرنا من الفروع. والظاهر اعتماد ما وافق المتون من اعتبار صيرورة الفوائت ستاً حقيقة، وما ذكره الشارح الزيلعي ثمرة للخلاف المذكور من أنه لو ترك ثلاث صلوات مثلاً الظهر من يوم والعصر من يوم والمغرب من يوم ولا يدري أيتها أولى، فعلى اعتبار الأوقات سقط الرتيب لأن المتخلل بين الفوائت كثيرة فيصلي ثلاثاً فقط، وعلى اعتبار الفوائت في نفسها لا يسقط فيصلي سبع صلوات والأول أصح اهـ. فغير صحيح لوجهين الأول أنه لا يتصور على قول أبي حنيفة كون المتخللات ست فوائت لأن مذهبه أن الوقتية المؤداة مع تذكر الفائتة تفسد فساداً موقوفاً إلى أن يصلي
كذلك قوله : (وإن أجاب عنه في غاية البيان الخ) قال بعد تقريره : وحاصله إلا أن يزيد بفوت ست صلوات بدخول وقت السابعة فيسقط الترتيب وهذا ما عندي من البيان ا هـ. ورده في العناية بأن الزيادة لا بد وأن تكون من جنس المزيد عليه ثم قال : والحق أن يقدر مضافان وتقديره إلا أن تزيد أوقات الفوائت على أوقات ست صلوات بحسب دخول الأوقات دون خروجها. ورده في السعدية بأن الرائد على أوقات ست صلوات ليس قوت الفائتة بل على العكس حيث زاد على أوقات الفوائت الستة وقت صلاة أخرى. واختار في الجواب أن الكلام على القلب أي إلا أن تزيد الصلوات المفروضة على ست فوائت قال : وهذا معنى صحيح لا غبار عليه والقلب فن معتبر من البلاغة سيما عند صاحب المفتاح ا هـ . لكن فيه أن اعتبار محاورات البلاغة في أداء الأحكام الشرعية غير ظاهر لا سيما فيما يؤدي إلى اشتباه الحكم كماهنا وثم تأويلات أخر قوله للاشتباه) تعليل للأولوية وقوله ما قدمناه» مع وجه آخر للأولوية أيضاً قوله : (و به اندفع ما صححه الشارح الزيلعي) وعبارته ثم المعتبر فيه أن تبلغ الأوقات المتخللة مذ فاتته سنة وإن أدى ما بعدها في أوقاتها، وقيل يعتبر أن تبلغ الفوائت ستاً ولو كانت متفرقة، وثمرة الاختلاف تظهر فيما إذا ترك ثلاث صلوات مثلاً الخ قوله :
(ولهذا ذكر الخ) تعليل للاندفاع لكن مع قطع النظر عن قوله وقال الصدر الشهيد الخ».
قوله: (وهو موافق الخ) أي ما ذكره الصدر الشهيد وما في التجنيس والولوالجية موافق لتصحيح الشارح قوله : (سقط الترتيب قال في الفتح يعني بين المتروكات ا هـ. وظاهره أنه لا يسقط بين المتروكات والوقتية على كل من الاعتبارين كما يفيده أيضاً ما سيذكره المؤلف عن الحقائق
His saying (And their becoming six): meaning that order drops by the missed prayers becoming six prayers due to entering the limit of abundance leading to hardship if we were to say... and abundance by entering the repetition which is that the missed prayers are six, and that is correct. And by it is refuted what was narrated from Muhammad that the criterion is the entry of the sixth, and what is in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj and Ghayat al-Bayan and many that the criterion is the entry of the time of the seventh so that the missed prayers become six, since their becoming six does not depend on the entry of the seventh, as if one misses a full day and the dawn of the second day: the missed prayers become six by sunrise of the second day and the time of the seventh has not entered. It may be said that since the benefit of dropping is the validity of the present prayer, and that is only by the entry of the time of the seventh, the time of the seventh is considered. Its answer is that the benefit of dropping is not limited to what was mentioned, because by the entry of the time of the seventh, he is not required to observe order among the missed prayers themselves, as will come. The wording of the author is preferable to the wording of al-Hidayah and al-Quduri where they said: 'Unless the missed prayers increase over six prayers' as an exception from his saying 'order them in making up' due to the implication of its apparent meaning of the missed prayers being seven according to Fath al-Qadir, or nine according to al-Nihayah. And he answered it in Ghayat al-Bayan that the intent of 'missed prayers' is the times metaphorically due to confusion, along with what we have presented of not requiring the entry of the time of the seventh. And it is stated in al-Muhit that the apparent narration is that order drops by the missed prayers becoming six, in agreement with what is in al-Mukhtasar.
And it was corrected in al-Kafi, and by it is refuted what the commentator al-Zayla'i corrected that the criterion for dropping order is that the intervening times since the first missed prayer reach six times, even if he performs what is after in their times. For this, it is mentioned in al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyya: If one remembers a missed prayer after a month, the present prayer is not valid with the memory of the missed prayer unless the missed prayers are six. And al-Sadr al-Shahid Husam al-Din said in his Waqi'at: It is permissible. In al-Tajnis: Permissibility is the choice of al-Tahawi and al-Faqih Abu al-Layth, and we adopt it because the intervening between them is more than six prayers. In al-Walwalijiyya: It is the choice of the shaykhs and it agrees with the correction of the commentator. The summary is that they differed whether the criterion is the missed prayers themselves becoming six, even if scattered, or the intervening times being six. Its fruit appears in the branches we mentioned. And the apparent is to rely on what agrees with the texts of considering the missed prayers becoming six in reality. And what the commentator al-Zayla'i mentioned as a fruit of the mentioned difference: that if one misses three prayers, e.g., Zuhr of one day, Asr of another, Maghrib of another, and does not know which is first, then on the consideration of times order drops because the intervening between the missed prayers are many, so he prays only three; on the consideration of the missed prayers themselves, order does not drop, so he prays seven prayers. And the first is more correct. But this is not correct for two reasons: first, it is not conceivable on the view of Abu Hanifa that the intervening are six missed prayers because his madhhab is that the present prayer performed while remembering the missed one is invalid in a suspended invalidity until he prays...
Similarly his saying (And he answered it in Ghayat al-Bayan etc.) He said after its establishment: Its summary is 'unless the loss of six prayers increases by the entry of the time of the seventh, then order drops, and this is my clarification.' And it was refuted in al-Inayah that the increase must be of the same type as the increased. Then he said: The truth is to estimate two additions, and its estimation is 'unless the times of the missed prayers increase over the times of six prayers according to the entry of the times, not their exit.' And it was refuted in al-Sa'diyya that the increase over the times of six prayers is not the time of the missed prayer, but rather the opposite, as the time of another prayer increased over the times of the six missed prayers. And he chose in the answer that the wording is inverted (qalb), i.e., 'unless the obligatory prayers increase over six missed prayers.' He said: This is a correct meaning with no dust; and qalb is a recognized art in rhetoric, especially with the author of al-Miftah. But there is that considering rhetorical discussions in deriving legal rulings is not evident, especially in what leads to confusion of the ruling as here. And there are other interpretations. His saying (due to confusion) is a reason for the preference, and his saying (what we presented) is another aspect for the preference. Also his saying (And by it is refuted what the commentator al-Zayla'i corrected) and his wording: then the criterion is that the intervening times since the first missed prayer reach six, even if he performs what is after in their times, and it is said that the criterion is that the missed prayers reach six even if scattered, and the fruit of the difference appears in the case of three missed prayers etc. His saying: (For this, he mentioned etc.) is a reason for the refutation, but disregarding his saying 'and al-Sadr al-Shahid said'. His saying: (And it is in agreement etc.) means what al-Sadr al-Shahid mentioned and what is in al-Tajnis and al-Walwalijiyya agrees with the correction of the commentator. His saying: (Order drops; said in al-Fath: meaning among the missed prayers. Its apparent meaning is that it does not drop between the missed prayers and the present prayer on both considerations, as also indicated by what the author will mention from al-Haqa'iq.
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion of the rule that when missed prayers become six (or more), the obligation to observe order in making them up drops. The commentator explains the matn: 'and their becoming six' means that the missed prayers become six, and then order is dropped due to hardship. The correct view is that the criterion is when the missed prayers themselves become six, not when the seventh time enters. He refutes the narration from Imam Muhammad that the entry of the sixth time is the criterion, and the view of some that the entry of the seventh time is necessary. He gives an example: if one misses a full day (five prayers) and the dawn of the second day, the missed prayers become six at sunrise of the second day without the seventh time entering. Then he discusses a possible objection: the benefit of dropping order is to allow the present prayer to be valid, and that only occurs when the seventh time enters? He answers that the benefit also includes that order among the missed prayers themselves is not required after six, so the ruling is established at the point of six. The commentator then compares the wording of the author (of Kanz) with that of al-Hidayah and al-Quduri, noting that the latter's phrase 'unless the missed prayers increase over six' could be interpreted as requiring the seventh prayer to be missed, but the author's wording is clearer. Then he cites various authorities: al-Kafi, al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyya, al-Sadr al-Shahid, al-Tajnis, al-Walwalijiyya, showing a difference of opinion. The core dispute: is the criterion the number of missed prayers themselves (even if scattered) or the number of intervening times (awqat mutakhalila) between them? The practical fruit (thamar) is given: if one misses three prayers from three different days with no knowledge of order, on the 'times' view order drops (many intervening times), so he prays only three; on the 'prayers' view, order does not drop, so he must pray seven (making up the missed ones plus the intervening present prayers). The commentator argues against al-Zayla'i's fruit, stating it is not correct because on Abu Hanifa's view, the present prayers performed while remembering are invalid, so the intervening times are not true missed prayers. The passage then discusses further interpretations, including the rhetorical device of qalb (inversion) proposed by al-Sa'diyya to resolve the wording of al-Hidayah, but the commentator is cautious about using rhetorical principles in legal rulings. Overall, the relied-upon position is that order drops when the missed prayers themselves reach six, regardless of the number of intervening times.

Key Terms
الكثرة (al-kathrah): The limit of six missed prayers after which order drops due to hardship.
الفوائت (al-fawa'it): Missed obligatory prayers that are to be made up.
الوقتية (al-waqtiyyah): The present prayer performed in its prescribed time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, when does the obligation to observe order in making up missed prayers drop?
A) When the number of missed prayers reaches five.
B) When the number of missed prayers reaches six, regardless of intervening times.
C) When the number of intervening times (awqat mutakhalila) reaches six.
D) When the seventh time enters.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that the obligation to observe order (tartib) in making up missed prayers drops when the missed prayers themselves become six, regardless of the number of intervening present prayer times.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Ruling for Three or More Missed Prayers: The Dispute of Three vs Seven
Explains the ruling for three or more missed prayers and the dispute

Learning Objective
State the relied-upon Hanafi position on the number of prayers to make up when three missed prayers of unknown order exist, and explain the reasoning based on the drop of tartib due to hardship.

Core Idea
When three prayers are missed with unknown order, tartib drops and only three need making up.

In the Hanafi school, making up missed prayers in order (tartib) is generally required. However, the school recognizes that when the number of missed prayers reaches six or more, tartib is dropped to avoid hardship. But what if only three are missed, yet to maintain tartib one would have to pray seven? Does the hardship principle still apply? This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses this nuance and resolves the intra-Hanafi dispute, ultimately affirming that only the three missed prayers need to be made up.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The passage discusses a case where a person missed three prayers from different days (dhuhr, asr, maghrib) and does not know the order. Understand that the dispute is about how many prayers he must perform in qada.
The scenario is explicitly described: 'دلم يدر ترتيبها'.
2
Follow the two opinions
Some Hanafi scholars (mashayikh) hold that seven prayers must be made up, others hold three. The first opinion insists on maintaining tartib because only three are actually missed. The second opinion argues that requiring seven effectively creates a situation equivalent to six or more missed prayers, so tartib is dropped.
Note the key concept: 'ست حقيقة أو معنى' (six in reality or in meaning).
3
Analyze the decisive argument
The author presents the reasoning for the second opinion: if tartib is dropped when there are six missed prayers due to hardship, then obligating seven prayers (to preserve tartib) creates even more hardship, so tartib should be dropped a fortiori.
This is an example of qiyas: from the known case (six missed prayers) to this case (seven required).
4
Identify the relied-upon ruling
The author states that the correct madhhab is that he only makes up what he left, without repeating any. The weak opinion requiring seven, fifteen, or thirty-one prayers is not relied upon.
The phrase 'على المذهب الصحيح' indicates the mufta bihi.
5
Apply the general rule
Generalize: when missed prayers are three or more and their order is unknown, tartib is dropped, and only the number missed is made up. If more prayers are missed, the same principle applies.
Examples are given: if another 'isha is missed, make up four; if another fajr, make up five.

كتاب الصلاة باب قضاء الفوائت
كمال خمس وقتيات، فإن لم يعد شيئاً منها حتى دخل وقت السادس صارت كلها صحيحة كما سيأتي. فقوله وقيل يعتبر أن تبلغ الفوائت ستاً ولو كانت متفرقة» غير متصور على قوله فلا يبنى عليه شيء . الثاني أن اختلاف المشايخ في لزوم السبع أو الثلاث ليس مبنياً على ما ذكر وإنما هو مبني على أن العبرة في سقوط الترتيب لتحقق فوت الست حقيقة أو معنى، فمن أوجب السبع نظر إلى الأول لأنه لم يفته إلا ثلاث فلم يسقط الترتيب فيعيد ما صلى أولاً، ومن اقتصر على الثلاث نظر إلى الثاني لأن بإيجاب السبع بإيجاب الترتيب تصير الفوائت كسبع معنى، فإذا كان الترتيب يسقط بست فأولى أن يسقط بسبع. فالحاصل أنا لو قلنا بوجوب الترتيب للزمه سبع وهي كسبع فوائت فلذا أسقطنا الترتيب، وقول من أسقطه أوجه لأن المعنى لأجله سقط الترتيب بالست وهو الدخول في حد الكثرة المقتضية للحرج موجود في إيجاب سبع بعينه، واقتصر عليه في التجنيس من غير حكاية خلاف ثم ذكر بعده الخلاف وقال : إن السقوط هو مختارنا وغيره لا يعتمد عليه. وذكر الولوالجي أن من أوجب الترتيب فيه لا اعتماد عليه لأنه قد زاد على يوم وليلة فلا يبقى الترتيب واجباً .اهـ. وصححه في الحقائق معللاً بأن إعادة ثلاث صلوات في وقت الوقتية لأجل الترتيب مستقيم، أما إيجاب سبع صلوات في وقت واحد لا يستقيم لتضمنه تفويت الوقتية .اهـ يعني أنه مظنة تفويت الوقتية .
قضاء
من يوم
فالحاصل أنه لا يلزمه إلا قضاء ما تركه من غير إعادة شيء على المذهب الصحيح إذا كانت الفوائت ثلاثاً أو أكثر فيلزمه قضاء ثلاث في الفرع المذكور، ولو ترك مع ذلك عشاء آخر لزمه أربع ، ولو ترك صبحاً آخر لزمه خمس ولا يعيد شيئاً مما صلاه وعلى القول الضعيف، ففي المسألة الأولى يصلي سبعاً لأنه إما أن يصلي ظهراً بين عصرين أو عصراً بين ظهرين لاحتمال أن يكون ما صلاه أولاً هو الآخر فيعيده ثم يصلي المغرب ثم يعيد ما صلاه أولاً لاحتمال كون المغرب أولاً، وفي المسألة الثانية يقضي خمس عشرة صلاة السبعة الأولى كما ذكرنا يصلي بعدها العشاء ثم يعيد السبعة الأولى لاحتمال أن تكون العشاء الأولى، وفي المسئلة الثالثة يقضي إحدى وثلاثين صلاة الخمسة عشر الأولى ثم يصلي الفجر ثم يعيد
هي
سوی
قوله : (غير متصور على (قوله لأنه مع دخول وقت السادسة ثبتت الصحة فلا تتحقق فائتاً المتروكة إذ ذاك والمسقط هو ست فوائت لا مجرد أوقات لا فوائت فيها كذا في فتح القدير وتمام الكلام فيه. وقد يجاب بأنها فائتة حكماً ولذا لو ترك صلاة وصلى بعدها خمساً ذاكراً لها سقط عنه الترتيب مع . أن الفائت حقيقة واحدة تأمل قوله : فالحاصل أي حاصل ما ذكره في توجيه قول من اقتصر على الثلاث قوله : ففي المسألة (الأولى) أي مسألة ما لو كانت الفوائت ثلاثاً ظهر من يوم وعصر من يوم ومغرب من يوم ولا يدري ترتيبها ولم يقع تحريه على شيء قوله : (لأنه إما أن يصلي الخ) تعليل لقوله يصلي سبعاً وقوله لاحتمال تعليل للتعليل. وحاصله أنه في هذه الصورة يصلي
صلاة الخمسة عشر لاحتمال أن يكون الفجر هي الأولى .
The Book of Prayer, Chapter of Making Up Missed Prayers. Completing five time-based prayers: if he did not make up any of them until the time of the sixth entered, all become valid as will come. So his statement: 'and it is said that it is considered that the missed prayers reach six even if they are scattered' is inconceivable according to his statement, so nothing is built upon it. Second: the difference among the mashayikh regarding the obligation of seven or three is not based on what was mentioned, but is based on whether the consideration in dropping tartib is for the realization of missing six in reality or in meaning. Whoever obligated seven looked to the first because he only missed three, so tartib is not dropped, so he repeats what he prayed first. Whoever restricted to three looked to the second because by obligating seven with the obligation of tartib, the missed prayers become like seven in meaning; if tartib is dropped by six, it is more appropriate to drop by seven. The conclusion: if we say tartib is obligatory, he must pray seven, and they are like seven missed prayers; so we drop tartib, and the opinion of the one who drops it is more appropriate because the meaning for which tartib was dropped by six—entering the limit of multiplicity necessitating hardship—exists in obligating seven exactly. The author of al-Tajnis restricted to it without narrating a difference, then after it he mentioned the difference and said: dropping is our choice, and other than it is not relied upon. Al-Walwaliji mentioned that whoever obligates tartib in it is not relied upon because he has exceeded a day and night, so tartib is not obligatory. In al-Haqa'iq, he corrected it, explaining that repeating three prayers in the time of the time-based prayer for the sake of tartib is proper, but obligating seven prayers in one time is not proper because it entails missing the time-based prayer. It means it is a cause of missing the time-based prayer. So the conclusion: he is only obligated to make up what he left without repeating anything on the correct madhhab if the missed prayers are three or more. So he must make up three in the mentioned branch; if he also left another 'isha, he must make up four; if he left another fajr, he must make up five, and he does not repeat anything he prayed. On the weak opinion: in the first issue, he prays seven because he either prays dhuhr between two asrs or asr between two dhuhrs due to the possibility that what he prayed first is the last, so he repeats it, then prays maghrib, then repeats what he prayed first due to the possibility that maghrib was first. In the second issue, he makes up fifteen prayers: the first seven as we mentioned, after them he prays 'isha, then he repeats the first seven due to the possibility that the 'isha was the first. In the third issue, he makes up thirty-one prayers: the first fifteen, then he prays fajr, then he repeats the fifteen due to the possibility that fajr was the first. His statement: (His statement: 'not conceivable according to' his statement because with the entry of the time of the sixth, validity is established, so the left [prayer] does not become a missed prayer at that time, and the dropper is six missed prayers, not mere times without missed prayers in them) as in Fath al-Qadir, and the complete discussion is therein. It can be answered that it is a missed prayer in ruling, and therefore if he left a prayer and prayed five after it while remembering it, tartib is dropped from him, even though the missed prayer is one in reality. Contemplate. His statement: 'the conclusion' means the conclusion of what he mentioned in directing the opinion of the one who restricted to three. His statement: 'so in the first issue' means the issue of when the missed prayers are three: dhuhr of a day, asr of a day, and maghrib of a day, and he does not know their order, and his ijtihad did not fall on anything. His statement: 'because he either prays' is an explanation for his statement 'he prays seven', and his statement 'due to possibility' is an explanation of the explanation. The summary is that in this case he prays the fifteen prayers due to the possibility that fajr was the first.
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq deals with the ruling on making up missed prayers when the number of missed prayers is three or more, specifically when the person does not know the order in which they were missed. The author first clarifies a principle: if a person misses a prayer and then prays five time-based prayers without making it up, and the time of the sixth prayer enters, those five become valid. This is because the missed prayer is considered 'made up' by the passage of time in a certain sense. However, the main discussion is about the difference among Hanafi scholars (mashayikh) regarding how many prayers must be made up in a scenario where three prayers from different days are missed (e.g., dhuhr of one day, asr of another, maghrib of a third) and the order is unknown. Some scholars say he must make up seven prayers, others say three. The reasoning is based on whether we consider the actual loss of six prayers (in reality) or a constructive loss (in meaning). The supporters of seven argue that since he only missed three prayers in reality, tartib (order) is not dropped, so he must perform a sequence that ensures the correct order by repeating prayers. The supporters of three argue that by requiring seven, the missed prayers become like seven in meaning, and since tartib is dropped when there are six missed prayers, it is even more likely to be dropped with seven. The relied-upon position, as stated by the author, is that he only makes up what he missed (three) without repeating any. This is because requiring seven would cause hardship and potentially cause missing the time-based prayer. The weak opinion (al-qawl al-da'if) requires a complex sequence of seven, fifteen, or even thirty-one prayers depending on how many prayers are missed. The commentary then explains the reasoning behind the relied-upon view and clarifies that the fatwa is on the correct madhhab.

Key Terms
الترتيب (al-tartib): The order in which missed prayers must be made up according to their original sequence.
الفوائت (al-fawa'it): Missed prayers that need to be made up (qada).
اختلاف المشايخ (ikhtilaf al-mashayikh): Differences of opinion among later Hanafi scholars, not necessarily from the founding imams.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person misses dhuhr, asr, and maghrib from different days and does not know their order, what is the relied-upon Hanafi ruling on how many prayers he must make up?
A) He must make up seven prayers.
B) He must make up three prayers only.
C) He must make up six prayers.
D) He must make up the three prayers and also repeat the time-based prayer.

Key Takeaway
When missed prayers are three or more and their order is unknown, the Hanafi school drops the requirement of tartib due to hardship, and only the missed number need be made up.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Making Up Two Missed Prayers with Unknown Order
Presents the dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the ruling for two missed prayers with unknown order

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the number of prayers to make up when two prayers are missed with unknown order, and apply the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
When order is unknown, Abu Hanifa requires three prayers; mufta bihi (Sahibayn) requires only two.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute. When a person misses two prayers from different days and cannot recall which came first, the school's founding imams differ on the required number of makeup prayers. Understanding this dispute illuminates how tarjih (preference) works within the Hanafi tradition, especially when later scholars opt for the more lenient view as a concession.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario
Two prayers (e.g., dhuhr and asr) from different days are missed. The person does not know which was first.
2
Identify Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa requires three prayers: either dhuhr between two asrs or asr between two dhuhrs. His reasoning: certainty of fulfilling tartib (order) requires a sequence covering all possibilities.
He analogizes to nasi al-ta'yin (one who forgets the specific prayer missed) who must pray a full day and night.
3
Identify the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad require only two prayers. They liken the case to a person who forgets the order (nasi), where tartib is dropped.
They see no need for extra prayers beyond what was missed.
4
Examine the tarjih
Later fatwa (Fatawa Qadikhan) adopts the Sahibayn's view as a leniency (takhfif) for people due to laziness. Some scholars consider Abu Hanifa's evidence stronger, but the operative ruling is the Sahibayn's.
The passage from al-Hawi al-Qudsi notes that when Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn differ, the evidence should be weighed; but here the fatwa favors the Sahibayn.
5
Apply the mufta bihi ruling
In practice, a person who misses two prayers with unknown order makes up only those two prayers, not three.
This applies whether the missed prayers are two or more (the ruling generalizes).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإنما قيدنا بكون الفائت ثلاثة فأكثر لأنه لو فاتته صلاتان الظهر من يوم والعصر من يوم ولا يدري الأول فعند أبي حنيفة يلزمه قضاء ثلاث صلوات وهو إما ظهر بين عصرين أو عصر بين ظهرين لأن المتروك أولاً إن كان هو المؤدى أولاً فالأخير نفل وإلا فالأول نفل . وقالا : لا يلزمه إلا صلاتان إلحاقاً له بالناسي فيسقط الترتيب . وأبو حنيفة ألحقه بناسي التعيين وهو من فاته صلاة لم يدر ما هي ولم يقع تحريه على شي يعيد يوم وليلة بجامع تحقق طريق يخرج بها عن العهدة بيقين فيجب سلوكها، وهذا الوجه يصرح بإيجاب الترتيب في القضاء عنده فيجب الطريق التي يعينها إلا كما قيل إنه مستحب عندهم فلا خلاف بينهم. وفي فتاوى قاضيخان أن الفتوى على قولهما كأنه تخفيفاً على الناس لكسلهم وإلا فدليلهما لا يترجح على دليله، وقد ذكر في آخر الحاوي القدسي أنه إذا اختلف أبو حنيفة وصاحباه فالأصح أن الاعتبار لقوة الدليل. فالحاصل أن الأصح المفتى به أنه لا يلزمه القضاء إلا بقدر ما ترك، سواء كان المتروك صلاتين أو أكثر
We only restricted it to the missed prayers being three or more because if he missed two prayers—dhuhr of a day and asr of a day—and does not know which was first, then according to Abu Hanifa, he must make up three prayers: either dhuhr between two asrs or asr between two dhuhrs, because if the first missed was the one performed first, then the last is nafl; otherwise, the first is nafl. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: he is only obligated for two prayers, likening him to the one who forgets, so tartib is dropped. Abu Hanifa likened him to the one who forgets the specific (nasi al-ta'yin)—the one who missed a prayer and does not know which it was and no ijtihad fell on anything—who repeats a day and night, on the basis that there is a known way to exit from responsibility with certainty, so it must be followed. This explicit statement indicates that he considers tartib obligatory in qada, so the way that ensures certainty must be followed. Except as it is said that it is mustahabb according to them (the Sahibayn), so there is no real disagreement. In Fatawa Qadikhan: the fatwa is on the opinion of the two (Sahibayn), as a leniency for people due to their laziness; otherwise, their evidence does not outweigh his evidence. It has been mentioned at the end of al-Hawi al-Qudsi that when Abu Hanifa and his two companions differ, the correct view is to consider the strength of the evidence. So the conclusion: the correct (asahh) and mufta bihi position is that he is only obligated to make up what he left, whether the missed prayers are two or more.
Source pages p. 152

Commentary
This passage addresses the scenario where a person misses two prayers (dhuhr and asr from different days) and does not know their order. There is a famous intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two main disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn). According to Abu Hanifa, he must make up three prayers: either praying dhuhr between two asrs (i.e., asr, then dhuhr, then asr again) or asr between two dhuhrs. The reasoning is that since tartib (order) is obligatory in qada, he must follow a sequence that guarantees the correct order, given the uncertainty. The Sahibayn hold that he only makes up two prayers (dhuhr and asr) because they liken him to a person who forgets the order, and in that case tartib is dropped, so only the missed prayers are required. The fatwa has shifted over time: in Fatawa Qadikhan, it is stated that the fatwa is on the opinion of the Sahibayn as a concession for people. However, some later scholars (e.g., in al-Hawi al-Qudsi) maintain that the stronger evidence is with Abu Hanifa, but the practice (fatwa) is on the Sahibayn's view. The final conclusion of the passage is that the correct (asahh) and mufta bihi position is that he only makes up what he missed, whether two or more, which aligns with the Sahibayn's view and the earlier ruling for three or more missed prayers.

Key Terms
ناسي التعيين (nasi al-ta'yin): A person who missed a specific prayer but does not know which one it is, and no ijtihad helps.
الترتيب (al-tartib): The obligation to make up missed prayers in the order they were missed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school, how many prayers must a person make up if he misses dhuhr and asr from different days and does not know which was first?
A) Three prayers: dhuhr, asr, and dhuhr again.
B) Three prayers: asr, dhuhr, and asr again.
C) Two prayers: only dhuhr and asr.
D) Two prayers: asr and dhuhr in any order.

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi position for two missed prayers with unknown order is that only two prayers are required, following the Sahibayn's more lenient view.

Saqt al-Tartib Among Multiple Fawa'it and Old vs. New Missed Prayers
Ruling on suqut al-tartib among fawa'it and dispute on old vs. new

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tartib when missed prayers are many, and distinguish the positions on whether old missed prayers count toward saqt al-tartib.

Core Idea
When missed prayers exceed six, tartib drops among them; scholars differ on including old missed prayers.

In the previous lesson, we learned that when missed prayers (fawa'it) reach six or more, the obligation of tartib (order) between them and the current time-based prayer is dropped. The present passage extends this principle to the relationship among the missed prayers themselves. It also introduces a key intra-madhhab dispute: whether old missed prayers (from a period of negligence) are treated differently from new ones. Understanding these nuances is critical for correctly applying the ruling when a person has a backlog of missed prayers.

Guided Path
1
State the extended ruling
Identify the ruling that when fawa'it are many (six or more), tartib drops not only between them and the current salah, but also among the fawa'it themselves.
This is the position affirmed in al-Hidayah and al-Muhit.
2
Understand the reasoning (qiyas jaliy)
The cause (multiplicity) that drops tartib in the relation between fawa'it and time-based prayer operates even more strongly within the fawa'it themselves. This is a fortiori logic.
The author cites Ghayat al-Bayan for this.
3
Identify the dispute on old vs. new
Some scholars (e.g., al-Sadr al-Shahid) argue that only new missed prayers (fawa'it haditha) cause suqut; old ones are treated as if they never happened to deter negligence.
The passage notes this view is corrected in Mi'raj al-Diraya.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The passage shows disagreement: al-Tajnis supports the distinction (old do not drop), while al-Mujtaba calls the first view (no distinction) more correct. Know both positions.
The fatwa according to al-Tajnis and al-Kafi differs; the student must be aware of the ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد أفاد كلام المصنف أن الفوائت إذا كثرت سقط الترتيب فيما بين الفوائت نفسها كما سقط بينها و بين الوقتية، وقد صرح به في الهداية وجزم به في المحيط، وعلله في غاية البيان بأن الكثرة إذا كانت مسقطة للترتيب في غيرها كانت مسقطة له في نفسها بالطريق الأولى لأن العلة إذا كان لها أثر في غير محلها فلأن يكون لها أثر في محلها أولى اهـ. ونص الزاهدي على أنه الأصح وبهذا اندفع ما في الظهيرية والخانية من أن الفوائت لو كثرت وأراد أن يقضيها فإنه يراعي الترتيب في القضاء، وتفسير ذلك أنه إذا قضى فائتة ثم فائتة فإن كان بين الأولى والثانية فوائت ست يجوز له قضاء الثانية، وإن كانت أقل من ست لا يجوز قضاء الثانية ما لم يقض ما قبلها. وقيل في الفوائت إذا كثرت سقط الترتيب حتى لو قضى ثلاثين فجراً ثم قضى ثلاثين ظهراً ثم قضى ثلاثين عصراً جاز اهـ. وأفاد كلامه أيضاً أنه لا فرق بين الفوائت القديمة والحديثة حتى لو ترك صلاة شهر فسقاً ثم أقبل على الصلاة ثم ترك فائتة حادثة فإن الوقتية جائزة مع تذكر الفائتة الحادثة لانضمامها إلى الفوائت القديمة وهي كثيرة فلم يجب الترتيب، ولأن بالحديثة ازدادت الكثرة فيتأكد السقوط، ولأنه لو اشتغل بهذه الفائتة لكان ترجيحاً بلا مرجح، ولو اشتغل بالكل تفوت الوقتية فتعين ما ذكرنا وقال بعضهم : إن المسقط الفوائت الحديثة، وأما القديمة فلا تسقط ويجعل الماضي كأن لم يكن زجراً له عن التهاون بالصلوات فلا تجوز الوقتية مع تذكرها. وصححه في معراج الدراية معزياً إلى المحيط للصدر الشهيد، وفي التجنيس وعليه الفتوى، وذكر في المجتبى أن الأول أصح، وفي الكافي والمعراج وعليه الفتوى فقد اختلف
The statement of the author (musannif) conveys that when missed prayers become many, the order (tartib) drops among the missed prayers themselves just as it drops between them and the time-based prayer. It is stated explicitly in al-Hidayah and affirmed in al-Muhit. He gave the reason in Ghayat al-Bayan that when multiplicity is a cause for dropping tartib in other than itself, then it is more appropriate that it be a cause for dropping in itself, because if a cause has an effect in other than its locus, it should have an effect in its own locus. Al-Zahidi stated that this is the most correct (asahh). With this, what is in al-Zahiriyya and al-Khaniyya is refuted, namely that if missed prayers become many and one wants to make them up, he should observe tartib in making them up. The explanation of that is: if he makes up one missed prayer then another, and if between the first and second there are six missed prayers, it is permissible to make up the second; if less than six, it is not permissible to make up the second until he makes up what is before it. And it was said that when missed prayers become many, tartib is dropped, even if he makes up thirty fajr prayers, then thirty dhuhr, then thirty asr, it is permissible. His statement also conveys that there is no difference between old missed prayers and new ones, such that if he missed a month's prayers out of wickedness, then he started praying, then he missed a new prayer, then the time-based prayer is permissible despite remembering the new missed prayer because it is joined to the old ones which are many, so tartib is not obligatory. And because the new one increases the multiplicity, so the dropping is confirmed. And because if he occupied himself with this new missed prayer, it would be a preference without a preponderant; and if he occupied himself with all, the time-based prayer would be lost, so what we mentioned is determined. And some said that the dropper is the new missed prayers; as for the old ones, they do not drop, and the past is made as if it did not happen, as a deterrent for his negligence in prayers, so the time-based prayer is not permissible while remembering them. This was corrected in Mi'raj al-Diraya attributed to al-Muhit of al-Sadr al-Shahid, and in al-Tajnis the fatwa is upon it. It is mentioned in al-Mujtaba that the first is more correct, and in al-Kafi and al-Mi'raj the fatwa is upon it, so there is disagreement.
Source pages p. 152

Commentary
This passage extends the principle of suqut al-tartib (dropping of order) to the relationship among multiple missed prayers themselves. Just as tartib drops between missed prayers and the current time-based prayer when the number of missed prayers reaches six or more, it also drops among the missed prayers themselves. This is logical because the cause (kathra/multiplicity) operates more strongly within its own domain. The author refutes the view in al-Zahiriyya and al-Khaniyya that still requires tartib among missed prayers even when many, except with a specific interpretation (that if the gap between two missed prayers is six or more, then the second can be made up without the first). He then addresses the question of old missed prayers (e.g., from a month of negligence) versus new ones. The majority view (including al-Hidayah, al-Muhit) is that old and new are not distinguished; the accumulation of many, whether old or new, causes tartib to drop. Thus, if someone has many old missed prayers and then misses a new one, he may pray the current time-based prayer without making up the new one first, because the old ones already make the count exceed six. Some scholars (like al-Sadr al-Shahid) hold that only new missed prayers count toward dropping tartib; old ones are considered as if they never happened as a deterrent. However, the passage notes disagreement on which view is the fatwa.

Key Terms
الفوائت القديمة (al-fawa'it al-qadima): Missed prayers from a long time ago, often due to negligence or sin.
الفوائت الحديثة (al-fawa'it al-haditha): Recently missed prayers, after a period of regular prayer.
سقوط الترتيب (suqut al-tartib): The dropping of the obligation to make up missed prayers in order.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the view supported in al-Hidayah and al-Muhit, when missed prayers become many (six or more), what is the ruling on tartib among the missed prayers themselves?
A) Tartib must always be observed strictly.
B) Tartib drops among them, just as it drops between them and the time-based prayer.
C) Tartib only drops if all missed prayers are new.
D) Tartib is replaced by a requirement to make up prayers in groups of six.

Key Takeaway
When missed prayers reach six or more, the order requirement drops among them; the status of old missed prayers remains disputed within the Hanafi school.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Does the Order of Missed Prayers Return After Being Dropped by Multitude?
Expands on the ruling regarding the dropping of order due to multitude and the dispute on its return.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on whether the obligation of order returns after being dropped by multitude and evaluate the proofs used by each side.

Core Idea
Order of missed prayers is dropped by multitude; whether it returns is disputed between the majority (no) and al-Hidayah (yes).

When a person misses many prayers, the requirement to make them up in order is dropped to prevent hardship. But what if he later makes up most of them, leaving only a few? Does the order obligation return? This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents the two Hanafi positions and the arguments behind the mufta bihi.

Guided Path
1
Define the key concepts: kathrah and suqut al-tartib
Understand that 'multitude' (kathrah) means six or more missed prayers, and this drops the requirement to make them up in order among themselves and with current prayers.
The threshold of six is from the Hidayah and other sources.
2
State the two positions on al-'awd (return of order)
List the majority view (no return) and minority view (return) with key proponents: al-Sarakhsi, al-Bazdawi, al-Kafi vs. al-Hidayah.
The mufta bihi is the majority view.
3
Analyze the dalil for the return view
Examine the narration from Imam Muhammad about a person who missed a day and night and then makes up prayers alongside current ones. The current prayers are invalid if performed first, implying order is required when the missed prayers are few.
The wording is: 'fiman taraka salata yawm wa layla...'
4
Evaluate the counter-argument and the rebuttal
Understand the critique from al-Kafi and al-Tabyin: the narration does not prove return because the order was never dropped (the missed prayers were only five, not reaching six). The rebuttal by Shaykh Qasim argues that the order drops upon entry into the sixth time, not exit, so the scenario may still be under the dropping rule.
This is a subtle point about the timing of suqut.
5
Apply the mufta bihi to a scenario
Given a person with many missed prayers who makes up all but one, determine that his current prayer is valid without making up the last missed prayer first, because the order does not return.
The fatwa is on this view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

في غيرها كانت مسقطة له في نفسها بالطريق الأولى لأن العلة إذا كان لها أثر في غير محلها فلأن يكون لها أثر في محلها أولى اهـ. ونص الزاهدي على أنه الأصح وبهذا اندفع ما في الظهيرية والخانية من أن الفوائت لو كثرت وأراد أن يقضيها فإنه يراعي الترتيب في القضاء، وتفسير ذلك أنه إذا قضى فائتة ثم فائتة فإن كان بين الأولى والثانية فوائت ست يجوز له قضاء الثانية، وإن كانت أقل من ست لا يجوز قضاء الثانية ما لم يقض ما قبلها. وقيل في الفوائت إذا كثرت سقط الترتيب حتى لو قضى ثلاثين فجراً ثم قضى ثلاثين ظهراً ثم قضى ثلاثين عصراً جاز اهـ. وأفاد كلامه أيضاً أنه لا فرق بين الفوائت القديمة والحديثة حتى لو ترك صلاة شهر فسقاً ثم أقبل على الصلاة ثم ترك فائتة حادثة فإن الوقتية جائزة مع تذكر الفائتة الحادثة لانضمامها إلى الفوائت القديمة وهي كثيرة فلم يجب الترتيب، ولأن بالحديثة ازدادت الكثرة فيتأكد السقوط، ولأنه لو اشتغل بهذه الفائتة لكان ترجيحاً بلا مرجح، ولو اشتغل بالكل تفوت الوقتية فتعين ما ذكرنا وقال بعضهم : إن المسقط الفوائت الحديثة، وأما القديمة فلا تسقط ويجعل الماضي كأن لم يكن زجراً له عن التهاون بالصلوات فلا تجوز الوقتية مع تذكرها. وصححه في معراج الدراية معزياً إلى المحيط للصدر الشهيد، وفي التجنيس وعليه الفتوى، وذكر في المجتبى أن الأول أصح، وفي الكافي والمعراج وعليه الفتوى فقد اختلف الظهر ثم العصر ثم الظهر ثم المغرب ثم الظهر ثم العصر ثم الظهر لما ذكره من التعليل الثاني قوله: (مستدلاً بما روي عن محمد الخ) وجه الاستدلال أنه إذا قدم الوقتية صارت هي سادسة المتروكات التصحيح والفتوى كما رأيت والعمل بما وافق إطلاق المتون أولى خصوصاً أن على القول الثاني يؤدي إلى التهاون لا إلى زجره عنه، فإن من اعتاد تفويت الصلوات لو أفتى بعدم الجواز يفوّت أخرى ثم وثم حتى تبلغ الحديثة حد الكثرة كما في الكافي. بسبب قوله (ولم يعد بعودها إلى القلة أي لم يعد وجوب الترتيب بعود الفوائت إلى القلة القضاء بعد سقوطه بكثرتها كما إذا ترك رجل صلاة شهر مثلاً ثم قضاها إلا صلاة ثم صلى الوقتية ذاكراً لها فإنها صحيحة لأن الساقط قد تلاشى فلا يحتمل العود كالماء القليل إذا تنجس فدخل عليه الماء الجاري حتى كثر وسال ثم عاد إلى القلة لا يعود نجساً. واختاره الإمام السرخسي والإمام البزدوي حيث قالا: ومتى سقط الترتيب لم يعد في أصح الروايتين. وصححه أيضاً في الكافي والمحيط، وفي معراج الدراية وغيره وعليه الفتوى. وقيل يعود الترتيب وليس هو من قبيل عود الساقط بل من قبيل زوال المانع كحق الحضانة إذا ثبت للأم ثم تزوجت ثم ارتفعت الزوجية فإنه يعود لها واختاره في الهداية قال: إنه الأظهر مستدلاً بما روي عن محمد فيمن ترك صلاة يوم وليلة وجعل يقضي من الغد مع كل وقتية فائتة فالفوائت جائزة على كل حال والوقتيات فاسدة إن قدمها لدخول الفوائت في حد القلة وإن أخرها فكذلك إلا العشاء الأخيرة لأنه لا فائتة عليه في ظنه حال أدائها اهـ. ورده في الكافي والتبيين بأنه لا دلالة فيه لأن الترتيب لو سقط الجازت الوقتية التي بدأ بها ولأن الترتيب إنما يسقط بخروج وقت السادسة ولم يخرج هنا ولا يمكن حمله على ما روي عن محمد أن الترتيب يسقط بدخول وقت السادسة لأن حكمه بفساد الوقتية التي بدأ بها يمنع من ذلك إذ لو كان مراده على تلك الرواية لما فسدت التي بدأ بها أول مرة لسقوط الترتيب عنده. وذكره في فتح القدير وارتضاه ورده الشيخ قاسم في حاشيته على الزيلعي بأنه مبني على ما روي عن محمد فقد نص جماعة من محققي المشايخ على أن من أصل محمد أنه إذا دخل وقت السادسة سقط الترتيب إلا أن سقوطه يتقرر بخروج وقت السادسة فإذا أدى وقتية توقف جوازها على قضاء الفائتة وعدمه، فإذا قضى دخلت الفوائت في حد القلة فبطلت الوقتية لأنها أديت عند ذكر الفائتة أربعاً وفسدت الوقتية إلا العشاء فإنه صلاها. وعنده أن ما جميع فسقط الترتيب فعلى تقدير أن لا يعود كان ينبغي أنه إذا قضى بعدها فائتة حتى عادت المتروكات إلى خمس أن تجوز الوقتية الثانية قدمها أو أخرها وإن وقعت بعد عدة لا توجب سقوط الترتيب أعني خمساً أو أربعاً لسقوط الترتيب قبل أن تصير إلى الخمس كذا في الفتح. قوله: (لأنه لا فائتة عليه في ظنه حال أدائها محمول على ما إذا كان جاهلاً، أما لو اعتقد وجوب الترتيب كانت أيضاً فاسدة وعليه أن يقال: إذا كان الفرض جهل وجوب الترتيب وأنه معتبر في صحة العشاء إذا أخرها لمصادفته محل اجتهاد فلا وجه للفصل بين تقديمها وتأخيرها، بل يجب أن
The author's statement indicated that when the missed prayers become many, order is dropped among the missed prayers themselves just as it is dropped between them and the current time prayer... [full translation omitted due to length; it covers the various positions and proof texts]
Source pages p. 152

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on two issues:
1. When there is a large number of missed prayers (kathrah), the requirement to make them up in order (tartib) is dropped, both among the missed prayers themselves and between them and the current time prayer (waqtiyyah). The author cites al-Hidayah and al-Muhit as stating this definitively. The reasoning is that since multitude drops order in relation to the current time prayer (which is not among the missed ones), it should also drop order among the missed prayers themselves a fortiori. This is the view of al-Zahidi and considered the correct one. This refutes earlier texts like al-Zahiriyyah and al-Khaniyyah that required order even with many, with a threshold of six prayers.

2. The second issue is whether the obligation of order returns when the missed prayers are reduced to a small number (qillah) after having been dropped by multitude. The text presents two positions:
   - The majority view (Imam al-Sarakhsi, al-Bazdawi, al-Kafi, al-Muhit, and fatwa is on this): Order does NOT return once dropped. The analogy is to water that becomes impure when little, then becomes pure when a large quantity of fresh water flows in and then reduces again; it does not become impure again. Similarly, the dropped order is gone.
   - A minority view (al-Hidayah, citing a narration from Muhammad): Order does return when the missed prayers become few again. The analogy is the right of child custody (hadanah) that returns to the mother after her marriage ends. The proof is a report from Muhammad about a person who missed one full day and night and then started making up from the next day alongside the current prayers: the current prayers are invalid if he performed them before making up the missed ones because the missed ones are now few (within the threshold). This indicates that order returns.

The text then discusses a critique of the proof from al-Kafi and al-Tabyin, and a rebuttal by Shaykh Qasim in his hashya. The passage ends with a discussion on whether ignorance excuses the obligation of order.

The fatwa in this passage is stated to be on the first view (order does not return), as it is the one that prevents leniency and is easier for people.

Key Terms
الكثرة (al-kathrah): Multitude; the number of missed prayers that cause the obligation of order to drop. The threshold is six or more.
سقوط الترتيب (suqut al-tartib): The dropping of the requirement to make up missed prayers in order due to their large number.
العود (al-'awd): The return of the obligation of order when the missed prayers are reduced to a small number after having been dropped.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority view mufta bihi in this passage, if a person had many missed prayers (order dropped) and then makes up all but one of them, does the order return?
A) Yes, order returns for the remaining one missed prayer.
B) No, order does not return; the remaining prayer can be made up at any time.
C) The person must repeat all prayers with order.
D) Only if he had less than six missed prayers initially.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi is that the obligation of order, once dropped by multitude, does not return even if the missed prayers become few again.

Salah — Prayer
advanced
12 min
Does the Obligation of Order for Missed Prayers Return After Dropping?
Debating whether tartib returns after dropping.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the return of tartib and apply the qiyas used to support non-return.

Core Idea
Once order drops due to many missed prayers, it never returns.

This lesson explores an intra-Hanafi debate: when a person has many missed prayers, the obligation to make them up in order (tartib) is dropped due to hardship. But if the number later becomes few, does the obligation revive? Two views exist, and the relied-upon position is that it does not return. We will examine the proofs, including a powerful qiyas to a water purification case, and understand why this view prevails.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
State the two opposing views: (1) order does not return (mufta bihi); (2) order does return. Note the key scholars on each side.
The first view is endorsed by al-Sarakhsi and al-Bazdawi; the second by the author of al-Hidayah.
2
Analyze the Hanafi qiyas
Break down the analogy to impure water: asl (small impure water becomes pure after flowing, then returns to small – does not become impure again), far' (order drops due to multitude, then becomes few – does not return). Identify the illa: complete dissipation (talāshī).
The illa is the complete removal of the original state; it cannot be revived by a later change in condition.
3
Examine the opposing analogy
The opposing view uses qiyas to the right of custody (haḍānah): it returns after removal of the impediment (marriage). Understand why this is rejected: dropping of order is due to dissipation, not a temporary impediment.
The Hanafi response: the ruling has been annulled, not merely suspended.
4
Evaluate the narration from Muhammad
Both sides cite a narration from Muhammad. The pro-return view interprets it as evidence that order remains. The Hanafi response distinguishes between entry and exit of the time of the sixth prayer, and notes that the narration is used as istishhād (witness) not istidlāl (proof).
The relied-upon narrations from early masters confirm non-return.
5
Determine the practical consequence
Apply the ruling: if a person with many missed prayers makes up all but one, then prays a current prayer while remembering the missed one, the current prayer is valid according to the mufta bihi view and invalid according to the other view.
This is the thamarah al-khilāf (practical difference).

الكتاب الخ أقول : قد ذكر في المعراج هذا الرد بصورة سؤال ثم أجاب عنه وعبارته : فإن قيل قال في الكتاب صلى مع كل وقتية فائتة ومع للقران قلنا: إن القرآن غير مراد إجماعاً فإن الصلاتين لا تؤديان معاً فيكون المراد أن كل فائتة تقضى مع ما يجانسها من الوقتية من غير اشتراط البيان في وقت واحد اهـ. قال في النهر : فذكره السؤال بدون الجواب مما لا ينبغي وقال : إن هذا الجواب أي المذكور في المعراج أحسن الأجوبة ا هـ . لكن استشكله شيخنا بما مر عن الشيخ قاسم من أصل محمد فإن مقتضاه أنه إذا لم يؤد الفائتة في وقت السادسة يتقرر سقوط الترتيب فيلزم صحة الوقتية تأمل قوله : (وذكر في فتح القدير) أي جواباً عما ذكره سابقاً من الرد على الهداية تبعاً للكافي والتبيين قوله : فكيف بالاستشهاد أي أن ما ذكره صاحب الهداية عن محمد استشهاد على مدعاه لا استدلال فإبطاله لا يستلزم بطلان المستشهد عليه بالأولى قوله : (وليس هو من قبيل المانع الخ) سبقه إلى هذا العلامة قاسم في فتاواه .
Chapter on Making up Missed Prayers. The correction and fatwa is as you have seen, and acting according to the general statements of the texts is better, especially since the second opinion leads to leniency, not deterrence. For one who habitually misses prayers, if he is given a fatwa of impermissibility, he will miss another and another until the new misses reach the level of multitude, as in al-Kafi. His statement: (And it does not return by their returning to fewness) means: the obligation of order does not return by the missed prayers returning to fewness after it has dropped due to their multitude; as if a man leaves a month's prayers, then makes them up except one prayer, then prays the current prayer while mindful of them, it is valid because what has dropped has dissipated and cannot return, like a small amount of water that becomes impure, then flowing water enters it until it becomes abundant and flows, then returns to fewness: it does not become impure again. This is chosen by Imam al-Sarakhsi and Imam al-Bazdawi, who said: Whenever order has dropped, it does not return in the more correct of the two narrations. This has also been declared correct in al-Kafi and al-Muhit, and in Mir'aj al-Diraya and others, and the fatwa is upon it. And it is said that order returns, and this is not of the type of return of what has dropped but rather of the removal of an impediment, like the right of custody when it is established for the mother, then she marries, then the marriage is dissolved: it returns to her. This was chosen in al-Hidayah; he said: It is more apparent, adducing what was narrated from Muhammad concerning one who leaves a day and night's prayers and begins to make them up the following day, praying with each current prayer a missed one: the missed prayers are valid in any case, and the current prayers are invalid if he offers them first due to the missed prayers entering the limit of fewness, and if he delays them likewise except the last Isha, because there is no missed prayer upon him in his assumption at the time of its performance. End. And it was refuted in al-Kafi and al-Tabyin that there is no indication in it, because if order had dropped, the current prayer that he began with would be valid, and because order only drops by the exit of the time of the sixth, and it has not exited here, and it cannot be construed according to what was narrated from Muhammad that order drops by the entry of the time of the sixth, because his ruling of the invalidity of the current prayer he began with prevents that; for if his intention were according to that narration, the one he began with first would not have been invalid due to the dropping of order according to him. And it was mentioned in Fath al-Qadir and approved, and Shaykh Qasim refuted it in his gloss on al-Zayla'i, saying it is based on what was narrated from Muhammad, for a group of verifying scholars have stated that according to Muhammad's principle, when the time of the sixth enters, order drops, but its dropping is finalized by the exit of the time of the sixth. So if he performs a current prayer, its permissibility depends on the making up of the missed prayer or not. So if he makes up, the missed prayers enter the limit of fewness, and thus the current prayer becomes invalid because it was performed while remembering the missed prayer four times, and the current prayer became invalid except for Isha because he prayed it while he thought there was no missed prayer upon him. And when order dropped, on the assumption that it does not return, it would be appropriate that if he thereafter makes up a missed prayer so that the missed ones return to five, that the second current prayer would be valid whether he offered it first or last, even if it occurred after a number that does not necessitate dropping of order, i.e., five or four, due to the dropping of order before it reached five, as in al-Fath. His statement: (because there is no missed prayer upon him in his assumption at the time of its performance) is carried on the case of ignorance. But if he believed in the obligation of order, it would also be invalid. And it must be said: if the assumption is ignorance of the obligation of order and that it is considered in the validity of Isha when he delays it because it falls within a field of ijtihad, there is no face for distinguishing between offering it earlier and later; rather it must be that he has made it up, so he resembles a forgetful person. End. And what was answered in al-Mi'raj – that the case is assumed for one who extends the current prayer he began until the end of the time, then makes up the missed prayer after the time exits, and the commencement must be in the wide time, because if it were at the time of constraint, the current prayer would be valid – was refuted by his statement in the book: 'with each missed prayer, a current prayer' and 'with' implies association. And it is mentioned in Fath al-Qadir: It is not hidden that the invalidation of the specific proof does not necessitate the invalidation of the proved, so how about using as a witness? Its summary is the invalidation of that being a text from Muhammad in the issue; so be it, it is not textually narrated from the early masters, but the aspect supports it by making it of the type of termination of a ruling by termination of its cause: the dropping of order was due to the cause of multitude leading to hardship, or it being a means of destroying the current prayer; so when it became few, the cause ceased, so the previous ruling returned, like the right of custody. End. And there is objection to this, for we have transmitted from the two imams al-Sarakhsi and al-Bazdawi, as in Ghayat al-Bayan, that when order has dropped, it does not return in the more correct of the two narrations. And in al-Muhit: it does not return in the more correct of the narrations. So how can it be said that it is not textually narrated from the early masters, whereas it is the more correct of the narrations from the early masters? For narrations are attributed to them, not to the later scholars. And in reality, this is not of the type of removal of an impediment, because the efficient cause is valid even if he offers it first, because the assumption is that he is ignorant of the obligation of order between it and the missed prayer upon him. And the answer is known from their answer to the request for the distinction between the case of one who prays Zuhr without ablution then prays Asr while mindful of it, to the end of the issue mentioned; its answer is similar to our case: if he delays Isha, its invalidity is due to the invalidity of the current prayers and the invalidity of the ijtihad-based invalidity, so it is analogous to Asr in the aforementioned issue; and if he offers it first, its invalidity is due to the certain existence of the missed prayer, which is the last of the missed ones. This is what was verified in Fath al-Qadir. His statement: (And it has not exited here) i.e., in that case, if he makes up a missed prayer before the time exits, the missed prayers remain four and become five by the exit of time, so there is a return from five to four and from four to five, so multitude is not realized. His statement: (And what was answered in al-Mi'raj) i.e., concerning the refutation of the author of al-Hidayah mentioned in al-Kafi and al-Tabyin. His statement: (The case) i.e., the one used as evidence in al-Hidayah. His statement: (Refuted by his statement in the book, etc.) I say: al-Mi'raj mentioned this refutation in the form of a question, then answered it. His expression: 'If it is said: He said in the book: Pray with each missed prayer a current prayer, and 'with' implies simultaneity. We say: The simultaneity is not intended by consensus, for two prayers cannot be performed together, so the meaning is that each missed prayer is made up with its like from the current prayer without requiring simultaneity in one time.' End. He said in al-Nahr: Mentioning the question without the answer is not proper, and said: This answer mentioned in al-Mi'raj is the best of answers. But our teacher found it problematic due to what passed from Shaykh Qasim about Muhammad's principle, for its implication is that if he does not perform the missed prayer at the time of the sixth, the dropping of order is confirmed, necessitating the validity of the current prayer; ponder. His statement: (And it is mentioned in Fath al-Qadir) i.e., as an answer to what he mentioned earlier of the refutation of al-Hidayah following al-Kafi and al-Tabyin. His statement: 'So how about using as a witness?' i.e., what the author of al-Hidayah mentioned from Muhammad is a witness to his claim, not a proof, so its invalidation does not necessitate the invalidation of what is witnessed, a fortiori. His statement: (And it is not of the type of impediment, etc.) The scholar Qasim preceded him in this in his Fatawa.
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether the obligation of order (tartib) in making up missed prayers returns after it has been dropped due to their multitude. The passage type is an expansion probe, typical of sharh works: it presents the ruling, proofs, objections, and counter-objections. The author begins by stating the relied-upon position: once the order drops due to many missed prayers, it does not return even if those missed prayers become few. This is attributed to Imam al-Sarakhsi and al-Bazdawi, and it is the basis for fatwa. The analogy given is that of a small amount of water that becomes impure, then is diluted by flowing water until it becomes pure, and then returns to its original small quantity: it does not become impure again. The reasoning is that what has dropped (sāqiṭ) has dissipated (talāshā) and cannot return. The opposing view, chosen in al-Hidayah, holds that order does return, analogizing it to the right of custody (haq al-ḥaḍānah) which, once established for the mother, drops when she remarries, but returns when the marriage ends. The Hidayah's proof is a narration from Muhammad concerning a person who leaves a day and night's prayers and makes them up with each current prayer. The author of al-Kafi refutes this by arguing that if order had truly dropped, the first current prayer would be valid, contradicting the narration. The text then delves into technical details involving the time of the sixth missed prayer and whether order drops at its entry or exit. The author of Fath al-Qadir suggests that the Hidayah's use of Muhammad's narration is 'istishhād' (witnessing) rather than 'istidlāl' (proof), so its invalidation does not affect the main claim. However, this is criticized because the relied-upon narrations from the early masters confirm that order does not return. The discussion concludes with a comparison to the case of one who prays Zuhr without ablution and then prays Asr while mindful, used to explain the validity of Isha when delayed due to ijtihad. Ultimately, the text affirms the view that order does not return, as it is the more correct and relied-upon position.

Key Terms
ترتيب (tartīb): The obligation to perform missed prayers in order (i.e., making them up in sequence).
فوائت (fawāʾit): Missed prayers that were not performed on time and must be made up (qaḍāʾ).
حد القلة (ḥadd al-qilla): The threshold of fewness (i.e., when the number of missed prayers is less than six, triggering the obligation of order).
ساقط (sāqiṭ): The obligation or ruling that has dropped or ceased due to a certain condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what is the ruling on a current prayer offered by someone who had many missed prayers (over six) and has made up all but one, while remembering the remaining missed prayer?
A) The current prayer is valid because order does not return.
B) The current prayer is invalid because order returns when the missed prayers become few.
C) The current prayer is valid only if he delays it to the end of its time.
D) The current prayer is invalid regardless of order.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, once the obligation of order (tartib) for missed prayers drops due to multitude, it does not return, and this is the basis for fatwa.

Return of Order Obligation After Drop Due to Narrow Time or Forgetfulness
Critiquing the view that order does not return

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether the order obligation returns upon removal of its cause and identify the relied-upon position.

Core Idea
The order obligation returns upon remembrance and ample time, as established by the twelve issues.

This lesson examines a critical refinement within the Hanafi school. Al-Mujtaba asserts that once the order obligation drops due to narrow time or forgetfulness, it never returns. The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq challenges this, citing unanimous agreement on the 'twelve issues' that show the order does return. Understanding this dispute is crucial for determining the validity of prayers when one remembers a missed prayer while performing a current one.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on order return
The majority Hanafi view, including the author, holds that the order obligation returns when the cause (narrow time or forgetfulness) is removed. This is supported by the agreement on the twelve issues.
2
Identify the opposing view from al-Mujtaba
Al-Mujtaba claims that the order does not return, giving examples: if time exits during an on-time prayer, it remains ada'; a traveler cannot follow a resident after sunset; forgetfulness causes permanent drop.
3
Examine the opposing evidence
The examples seem to indicate that the order does not return. Analyze each: the traveler case involves time expiry, and the non-return cases are when remembrance occurs after the prayer is completed.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response using the twelve issues
The author invokes the twelve agreed cases where if a missed prayer is remembered during a current prayer before tashahhud, the current prayer is invalidated by consensus. This proves that the order returns upon remembrance.
5
Determine the mufta bihi (operative position)
The author favors the return of order, citing Miraj al-Diraya and al-Nihaya that state return by agreement. Al-Quduri's al-Mukhtasar limits non-return to the case of few missed prayers, but the general ruling is that order returns.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال في المجتبي : ولو سقط الترتيب لضيق الوقت ثم خرج الوقت لا يعود على الأصح حتى لو خرج في خلال الوقتية لا تفسد على الأصح وهو مؤدٍ على الأصح لا قاض، واقتداء المسافر بعد غروب الشمس في العصر بمقيم شرع فيه في الوقت لا يصح، وكذا لو سقط النسيان ثم تذكر لا يعود. ولو نسي الظهر وافتتح العصر ثم ذكره عند احمرار الشمس يمضي لضيق الوقت، وكذا لو غربت، وكذا لو افتتحها عند الاصفرار ذاكراً ثم غربت اهـ. وقوله «واقتداء المسافر» ينتجه كونه مؤدياً كما لا يخفة والذي ظهر للعبد الضعيف أن ما ذكره في المجتبي من عدم عوده بالتذكر خطأ لأن كلمتهم اتفقت عند ذكر المسائل الاثني عشرية السابقة أنه لو تذكر فائتة وهو يصلي فإن كان قبل القعود قدر التشهد بطلت صلاته اتفاقاً، وإن كان بعد القعود بطلت عنده، وعندهما لا تبطل . فقد حكموا بعوده بالتذكر ولهذا قال في معراج الدراية والنهاية : إنه لوسقط بالنسيان وضيق الوقت فإنه يعود بالتذكر وسعة الوقت بالاتفاق اهـ. ولذا والله أعلم اقتصر في المختصر على عدم العود بقلة الفوائت وإن حمل ما في المجتبي على تذكره بعد الفراغ من الصلاة فيكون محل الخلاف الترتيب بين الفائتة والوقتية في المستقبل لا فيما صلاه .
He said in al-Mujtaba: 'If the order dropped due to narrow time, then the time exited, it does not return according to the most correct view, such that if it exited during an on-time prayer, the on-time prayer is not invalidated according to the most correct view, and it is performed as a time-bound prayer (ada') according to the most correct view, not a make-up prayer. And a traveler following a resident in Asr after sunset, where the resident started it in time, is not valid. Similarly, if [order] dropped due to forgetfulness, then he remembered, it does not return. And if he forgot Dhuhr and started Asr, then remembered at reddening of the sun, he continues due to narrow time, and similarly if it set, and similarly if he started it at yellowness remembering then set...' etc. And his statement 'and a traveler following a resident' results in its being ada', as is not hidden. And what appears to this weak servant is that what al-Mujtaba mentioned about non-return upon remembrance is wrong, because their words agreed when mentioning the previous twelve issues that if he remembers a missed prayer while praying, if it is before the sitting of [the amount of] tashahhud, his prayer is invalidated by agreement, and if after the sitting, it is invalidated according to him (Abu Hanifa) and not invalidated according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). So they ruled for its return upon remembrance. Therefore, it was said in Miraj al-Diraya and al-Nihaya: 'If [order] dropped due to forgetfulness and narrow time, it returns upon remembrance and ample time by agreement.' Hence, and Allah knows best, al-Mukhtasar limited the non-return to few missed prayers, even if what is in al-Mujtaba is interpreted as his remembering after finishing the prayer, so the point of dispute is the order between the missed prayer and the on-time prayer in the future, not in what he already prayed.
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement (hāshiya) where the author of al-Bahr al-Rā'iq critiques the view presented in al-Mujtabā regarding the return of the obligation of order (tartib) when dropped due to narrow time or forgetfulness. Al-Mujtabā states that the order does not return on the most correct view, and gives several examples: if the time exited during an on-time prayer, the prayer is valid as ada' (not qada'); a traveler cannot follow a resident in Asr after sunset; if forgetfulness is removed, the order does not return. The author of al-Bahr declares this view 'wrong' (khaṭa'), because in the well-known twelve issues (al-masā’il al-ithnā 'ashariyya), the Hanafi jurists agreed that if a person remembers a missed prayer while performing a current prayer, the current prayer is invalidated if the remembrance occurs before the sitting for tashahhud, and at least according to Abu Hanifa after the sitting as well. This shows that the order returns upon remembrance. He cites Miraj al-Diraya and al-Nihaya that explicitly state that if order dropped due to forgetfulness or narrow time, it returns upon remembrance and when time is ample, by agreement. The author then suggests that al-Mukhtasar (by al-Quduri) correctly limited the non-return to the case of few missed prayers (i.e., when the number is the reason for dropping), and that al-Mujtaba's statement can be reinterpreted to refer to remembrance after finishing the prayer, so that the dispute is about future order, not past.

Key Terms
النسيان (al-nisyān): Forgetfulness of the obligation to pray in order, which can cause the order to drop.
الضيق (al-ḍīq): Narrowness of time, i.e., when the time for a prayer is about to end, causing the order to drop.
الإعادة (al-i'āda): Return of a dropped obligation; here specifically the return of the order requirement.
الترتيب (al-tartīb): The obligation to perform missed prayers in sequence before current prayers, when the missed prayers are few (five or fewer) and one remembers.
المسائل الاثنا عشرية (al-masā’il al-ithnā ‘ashariyya): The twelve agreed-upon cases detailing the effects of remembering a missed prayer during a current prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, what is the ruling if a person remembers a missed prayer while performing a current prayer, before sitting for tashahhud, and there is ample time?
A) The current prayer is valid and he completes it.
B) The current prayer is invalidated by agreement.
C) The current prayer is invalidated only according to Abu Hanifa.
D) The current prayer becomes a make-up prayer.

Key Takeaway
The order obligation returns upon remembrance and ample time, as established by the twelve issues and the majority Hanafi view, contra the view in al-Mujtaba.

Contingent Invalidation: Abu Hanifa vs. the Sahibayn on Remembering Missed Prayers
Explains a ruling and intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi intra-madhhab dispute on contingent invalidation of a current prayer performed while remembering a missed prayer, and apply the rule of 'one validates five'.

Core Idea
A current prayer while remembering a missed one is invalidated, but if missed prayers become six, order drops and it becomes valid — according to Abu Hanifa.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq delves into a subtle disagreement within the Hanafi school. When someone prays a current obligatory prayer while remembering a missed one, both Abu Hanifa and his two companions agree that the current prayer is initially invalid. However, they differ sharply on whether this invalidation is final or can be reversed if the number of missed prayers accumulates. Understanding this dispute requires careful attention to how legal causes (ʿilal) operate in time and how rulings can be contingent on future events.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario
Identify the exact situation: a person prays a current fard prayer (e.g., ʿAsr) while remembering that they have missed a previous fard (e.g., Zuhr). The current prayer is ruled invalid, but is this invalidation absolute or contingent?
2
Identify the two positions
Abu Hanifa holds that the invalidation is contingent (muqawwaf): if the missed prayer is made up before the total missed prayers reach six, the current prayer becomes invalid; if it is not made up and six are accumulated, the current prayer becomes valid. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the invalidation is absolute (mutahattim) and does not reverse.
3
Analyze the proofs
The Sahibayn rely on qiyas: the cause (kathrah – multiplicity) can only affect future prayers, not retroactively. Abu Hanifa argues that the ruling and cause are concomitant; multiplicity is an attribute of the totality, so when the last prayer is performed, the attribute applies back to the beginning. Consider the analogies from zakah, hajj, and hayd given in the text.
4
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
According to Abu Hanifa, if a person prays ʿAsr remembering a missed Zuhr, then later misses five more prayers (total six), and then makes up none, the ʿAsr becomes valid. According to the Sahibayn, the ʿAsr remains invalid regardless.
The famous phrase 'one validates five and one invalidates five' refers to the sixth missed prayer that, by its existence, validates five earlier prayers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (فلو) صلى فرضاً ذاكراً فائتة ولو وترا فسد فرضه (موقوفاً) أي فساد هذا الفرض موقوف على قضاء الفائتة قبل أن تصير الفوائت كثيرة مع الفائتة فإن قضاها قبله فسد هذا الفرض وما صلاه بعده متذكراً وإن لم يقضها حتى صارت الفوائت مع الفائتة ست صلوات فما صلاه متذكراً لها صحيح. قال في المبسوط : هذه المسألة التي يقال واحدة تصحح خمساً وواحدة تفسد خمساً فالواحدة المصححة للخمس هي السادسة قبل قضاء المتروكة والواحدة المفسدة للخمس هي المتروكة تقضى قبل السادسة .اهـ. وهذا عند أبي حنيفة، وعندهما الفساد متحتم لا يزول وهو القياس لأن سقوط الترتيب حكم والكثرة علة له فإنما يثبت الحكم إذا ثبتت العلة في حق ما بعدها، فأما في حق نفسها فلا. وهذا لأن العلة ما تحل بالمحل فيتغير لحلوله المحل فلا يجوز أن يكون نفس العلة محلاً للعلة للاستحالة. ولأبي حنيفة أن الحكم مع العلة يقترنان لما عرف في الأصول والكثرة صفة هذا المجموع وحكمها سقوط الترتيب فإذا ثبت صفة الكثرة بوجود الأخيرة استندت الصفة إلى أولها بحكمها فيجوز

المستقبل فيخالف حكاية الاتفاق على عوده قوله : (وتذكر قبل الفراغ فبعيد) قال الرملي نقلاً. شيخ شيخه العلامة المقدسي : قوله بعيد هو البعيد لأن صاحب المجتبى أعلى مقاماً من أن تخفي عليه مسألة مشهورة في المتون حتى يجيء مثلك يخطئه فيها فيحمل كلامه في كل مقام على ما يليق به، فأما ضيق الوقت فإذا خرج الوقت وهو في أثناء الصلاة زال ضيق الوقت بخروجه ولا يعود الترتيب، وأما التذكر في أثناء الصلاة فلا يمكن القول به لما اشتهر بين الصغار في الاثني عشر فيحمل على ما يمكن وهو لو كان عليه ظهر وعصر مثلاً فصلي المغرب ناسياً لهما ثم تذكرهما بعد المغرب فلا يعيدهما، وإن كان مقتضى الشرطية ذلك فبعد دخول وقت العشاء ليس له أن يقدم العشاء، فحملك كلام المجتبى على ما وهو الخطأ ا هـ . قلت : ولا يخفى عليك أن هذا الجواب وإن كان صحيحاً في نفسه لكنه بعيد من الأفهام وكثرة التعنيف لا تروجه عند من له أدنى إلمام، وقد سلم في النهر ما فهمه المؤلف المحقق لكنه قال : الأولى أن يحكم بضعفه وأن من حكي الاتفاق لم يلتفت إليه
