لشذوذه قوله: (فشمل (النوعين أي نوعي الترتيب وهما بين الفائتة والوقتية بين الفوائت نفسها .
الكل كمرض الموت لما ثبت له هذا الوصف استند إليه بحكمه ولهذا لو أعادها بلا ترتيب جازت عندهما أيضاً، وهذا لأن المانع من الجواز قلتها وقد زالت فيزول المنع. وفي العناية : لا يقال كل واحدة من آحادها جزؤها متقدمة عليها فكيف يكون معلولاً لها لأنها جزؤها من حيث الوجود ولا كلام فيه وإنما الكلام من حيث الجواز وذلك متأخر لأنه لم يكن ثابتاً لكل واحدة منها قبل الكثرة ولا يمتنع أن يتوقف حكم على أمر حتى يتبين حاله كتعجيل الزكاة إلى الفقير يتوقف كونها فرضاً على تمام الحول والنصاب نام، فإن تم على نمائه كان فرضاً وإلا نفل. وكون المغرب في طريق مزدلفة فرضاً على عدم إعادتها قبل الفجر فإن أعادها كانت نفلاً. والظهر يوم الجمعة على عدم شهودها فإن شهدها كانت نفلاً. وصحة صلاة المعذور إذا انقطع العذر فيها على عوده في الوقت الثاني فإن لم يعد فسدت وإلا صحت. وكون الزائد على العادة حيضاً على عدم مجاوزة العشرة فإن جاوزت فاستحاضة وإلا حيض. وصحة الصلاة التي صلتها صاحبة العادة فيما إذا انقطع دمها دون العادة فاغتسلت وصلت على عدم العود فإن عادت ففاسدة وإلا فصحيحة.
His statement: (If) he performs an obligatory prayer while remembering a missed prayer, even if it is witr, his obligatory prayer is invalidated (contingently), meaning the invalidation of this obligatory prayer is contingent upon the qada of the missed prayer before the missed prayers become many with the missed prayer. If he makes it up before that, then this obligatory prayer and what he prayed after it while remembering are invalid. If he does not make it up until the missed prayers with the missed one become six prayers, then what he prayed while remembering it is valid. He said in al-Mabsut: This is the issue of which it is said: one makes five valid and one invalidates five. So the one that makes the five valid is the sixth before qada of the missed one, and the one that invalidates the five is the missed one performed before the sixth. End. This according to Abu Hanifa. According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the invalidation is absolute and does not go away, and that is the analogy (qiyas) because the dropping of order is a ruling and multiplicity is its cause; the ruling is only established when the cause is established with respect to what comes after, not with respect to itself. This is because the cause attaches to the locus and changes with its attachment, so it is impossible for the cause itself to be a locus for the cause. For Abu Hanifa, the ruling and the cause are concomitant as is known in usul, and multiplicity is an attribute of this totality, and its ruling is the dropping of order; so when the attribute of multiplicity is established by the existence of the last one, the attribute relates back to its first [prayer] with its ruling, so it is permissible. ... (continues with the rest of the passage).
Source pages p. 156

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqaiq. The author explains the ruling when someone prays a current obligatory prayer while remembering a missed prayer. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the current prayer is invalidated, but this invalidation is contingent (muqawwaf) upon whether the missed prayer is made up before the number of missed prayers becomes many (six). If the person makes up the missed prayer before accumulating six missed prayers, the current prayer becomes invalid. If, however, he delays qada until the missed prayers become six (including the original missed prayer), then the order (tartib) drops, and all prayers performed while remembering become valid. This is the famous case of 'one validates five and one invalidates five.' The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the invalidation is absolute (mutahattim) and does not become valid later, based on qiyas: the cause (kathrah) only takes effect for future prayers, not retroactively. Abu Hanifa argues that the ruling and the cause coexist; multiplicity is a cumulative attribute that, once complete, retroactively applies to its parts. The author then discusses a separate point about tadhakkur before finishing a prayer, quoting al-Ramli and others, and concludes that the preferred view is that the order does not return. He then continues with analogies from other areas of fiqh (zakah, hajj, hayd) to support Abu Hanifa's position that rulings can be contingent on future events.

Key Terms
الترتيب (al-tartib): The obligation to perform missed prayers in order (qada) before current prayers, and the order among missed prayers themselves.
الفساد الموقوف (al-fasad al-muqawwaf): Invalidation that is contingent on a future condition; here, if the missed prayers become many, the invalidation is lifted retroactively.
الكثرة (al-kathrah): The multiplicity of missed prayers (specifically six or more) that causes the obligation of order to drop.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if someone prays the current 'Asr prayer while remembering a missed Zuhr, and then makes up the Zuhr after the 'Asr but before accumulating six missed prayers, what is the status of the 'Asr prayer?
A) It remains valid because the order was not required.
B) It becomes invalid because the missed prayer was made up before reaching six.
C) It becomes valid only if the missed Zuhr was made up within the same day.
D) It becomes a nafl prayer.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the invalidation of a current prayer performed while remembering a missed one is contingent according to Abu Hanifa: if the missed prayers total six, the current prayer becomes valid; the Sahibayn hold it absolute.
